Legislative Decree of April 3, 2006, no. 152
Provisions on environmental matters
(Official Gazette no. 88 of 14/04/2006 - Ordinary Supplement no. 96)
Text updated, most recently, by Law Decree no. 300 of December 28, 2006 - the so-called "Milleproroghe Decree" (Official Gazette no. 300 of 28/12/2006), as amended during its conversion into Law no. 17/2007 (Official Gazette no. 47 of 26.2.2007, Ordinary Supplement no. 48) and by the 2007 Finance Act (Law no. 296/2006, published in Official Gazette no. 299 of 27.12.2006 - Ordinary Supplement no. 244)
Note: Pursuant to Art. 1, para. 5 of Legislative Decree 284/2006 (Official Gazette no. 274 of 24/11/2006), "...All references to the Supervisory Authority for water resources and waste contained in Legislative Decree no. 152 of April 3, 2006, are repealed."
THE PRESIDENT OF THE REPUBLIC
Having regard to Articles 76, 87, and 117 of the Constitution;
Having regard to Law no. 308 of December 15, 2004, delegating to the Government the reorganization, coordination, and integration of environmental legislation and measures for direct application;
Having regard to Art. 14 of Law no. 400 of August 23, 1988, on the discipline of Government activity and the organization of the Presidency of the Council of Ministers;
Having regard to Legislative Decree no. 112 of March 31, 1998, on the conferral of administrative functions and tasks of the State to the regions and local authorities, in implementation of Chapter I of Law no. 59 of March 15, 1997;
Having regard to Directives 2001/42/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of June 27, 2001, on the assessment of the effects of certain plans and programmes on the environment, and 85/337/EEC of the Council of June 27, 1985, as amended by Directives 97/11/EC of the Council of March 3, 1997, and 2003/35/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of May 26, 2003, on the assessment of the environmental impact of certain public and private projects, as well as the reorganization and coordination of procedures for environmental impact assessment (EIA), for strategic environmental assessment (SEA), and for integrated pollution prevention and control (IPPC);
Having regard to Council Directive 96/61/EC of September 24, 1996, on integrated pollution prevention and control;
Having regard to Directive 2000/60/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of October 23, 2000, establishing a framework for Community action in the field of water policy;
Having regard to Council Directive 91/156/EEC of March 18, 1991, amending Directive 75/442/EEC on waste;
Having regard to Council Directive 91/689/EEC of December 12, 1991, on hazardous waste;
Having regard to Directive 94/62/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of December 20, 1994, on packaging and packaging waste;
Having regard to Council Directive 84/360/EEC of June 28, 1984, on the combating of air pollution from industrial plants;
Having regard to Directive 94/63/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of December 20, 1994, on the control of volatile organic compound (VOC) emissions resulting from the storage of petrol and its distribution from terminals to service stations;
Having regard to Council Directive 1999/13/EC of March 11, 1999, on the limitation of emissions of volatile organic compounds due to the use of organic solvents in certain activities and installations;
Having regard to Council Directive 1999/32/EC of April 26, 1999, relating to a reduction in the sulphur content of certain liquid fuels and amending Directive 93/12/EEC;
Having regard to Directive 2001/80/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of October 23, 2001, on the limitation of emissions of certain pollutants into the air from large combustion plants;
Having regard to Directive 2004/35/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of April 21, 2004, on environmental liability with regard to the prevention and remedying of environmental damage, which, for this purpose, "establishes a framework for environmental liability" based on the "polluter pays" principle;
Having regard to the preliminary resolution of the Council of Ministers, adopted at the meeting of November 18, 2005;
Having acquired the opinion of the Unified Conference referred to in Article 8 of Legislative Decree no. 281 of August 28, 1997;
Having acquired the opinions of the competent Committees of the Chamber of Deputies and the Senate of the Republic;
Having regard to the preliminary resolution of the Council of Ministers, adopted at the meeting of January 19, 2006;
Having acquired the opinions of the competent Committees of the Chamber of Deputies and the Senate of the Republic;
Having regard to the resolutions of the Council of Ministers, adopted at the meetings of February 10 and March 29, 2006;
On the proposal of the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory, in concert with the Ministers for Community Policies, for Public Function, for Regional Affairs, of the Interior, of Justice, of Defence, of Economy and Finance, of Productive Activities, of Health, of Infrastructure and Transport, and of Agricultural and Forestry Policies;
Hereby issues
the following legislative decree:
PART I - COMMON PROVISIONS
Art. 1
Scope of application
This legislative decree governs, in implementation of Law no. 308 of December 15, 2004, the following matters:
a) in part two, the procedures for the strategic environmental assessment (SEA), for the environmental impact assessment (EIA), and for the integrated environmental permit (IPPC);
b) in part three, soil protection and the fight against desertification, the protection of waters from pollution, and the management of water resources;
c) in part four, waste management and the remediation of contaminated sites;
d) in part five, air protection and the reduction of atmospheric emissions;
e) in part six, liability for environmental damage.
Art. 2
Objectives
The primary objective of this legislative decree is to promote levels of human quality of life, to be achieved through the safeguarding and improvement of environmental conditions and the prudent and rational use of natural resources.
For the purposes referred to in paragraph 1, this decree provides for the reorganization, coordination, and integration of legislative provisions in the matters referred to in Article 1, in accordance with the principles and guiding criteria set out in paragraphs 8 and 9 of Art. 1 of Law no. 308 of December 15, 2004, and in compliance with the Community legal order and the powers of the regions and local authorities.
The provisions of this decree shall be implemented within the limits of the human, instrumental, and financial resources available under current legislation and without new or increased burdens on public finances.
Art. 3
Criteria for the adoption of subsequent measures
The provisions of this decree may not be derogated from, amended, or repealed except by express declaration, through the amendment or repeal of the individual provisions contained herein.
Within two years from the date of publication of this legislative decree, with one or more regulations to be issued pursuant to Art. 17, paragraph 2, of Law no. 400 of August 23, 1988, the Government, on the proposal of the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory, shall adopt the necessary measures to amend and integrate the implementing and executive regulations on environmental matters, in compliance with the objectives, principles, and provisions of this decree.
For the purpose of preparing the measures referred to in paragraph 2, the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory shall avail itself of the opinion of the qualified representatives of the economic and social interests present in the Economic and Social Council for Environmental Policies (CESPA), without new or increased burdens on public finances.
Within the same period as referred to in paragraph 2, the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory shall provide for the amendment and integration of the technical standards on environmental matters with one or more regulations to be issued pursuant to Article 17, paragraph 3, of Law no. 400 of August 23, 1988, in compliance with the objectives, principles, and provisions of this decree. The application of Art. 13 of Law no. 11 of February 4, 2005, remains unaffected, concerning the transposition of Community directives that amend the implementing methods and technical characteristics of directives already transposed into the national legal order.
For the purposes of the fulfilments referred to in this article, the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory shall avail itself, for a duration of two years and without new or increased burdens on public finances, of a group of ten experts appointed by its own decree, from among university professors, senior managers of public research institutes, and highly qualified experts in the sectors and matters covered by this decree. The members of the expert group are not entitled to any compensation, indemnity, emoluments of any kind, or reimbursement of expenses.
PART II - PROCEDURES FOR STRATEGIC ENVIRONMENTAL ASSESSMENT (SEA), FOR ENVIRONMENTAL IMPACT ASSESSMENT (EIA), AND FOR THE INTEGRATED ENVIRONMENTAL PERMIT (IPPC)
TITLE I - GENERAL PROVISIONS
Art. 4
Content and objectives
The provisions of part two of this decree constitute the implementation of:
a) Directive 2001/42/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of June 27, 2001, on the assessment of the effects of certain plans and programmes on the environment, with the following objectives:
to ensure a high level of environmental protection;
to contribute to the integration of environmental considerations into the preparation, adoption, and approval phases of certain plans and programmes in order to promote sustainable development;
to promote the use of environmental assessment in the drafting of state, regional, and supra-municipal plans and programmes;
to ensure that an environmental assessment is carried out for plans and programmes that are likely to have significant effects on the environment;
b) Directive 85/337/EEC of the Council of June 27, 1985, on the assessment of the environmental impact of certain public and private projects, as amended and integrated by Council Directive 97/11/EC of March 3, 1997, and by Directive 2003/35/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of May 26, 2003, and of Directive 96/61/EC of September 24, 1996, transposed by Legislative Decree no. 59 of February 18, 2005, on integrated pollution prevention and control, with the following objectives:
to ensure the full transposition of Community directives on environmental impact assessment;
to simplify, without prejudice to the provisions of Art. 1, paragraph 2, of Law no. 443 of December 21, 2001, also through the issuance of regulations pursuant to Art. 17, paragraph 2, of Law no. 400 of August 23, 1988, the environmental impact assessment procedures, which shall take into account the cost-benefit ratio of the project from an environmental, economic, and social point of view;
to advance the environmental impact assessment procedures to the earliest configuration of the project that can be subjected to an exhaustive examination;
to introduce a system of controls capable of ascertaining effective compliance with the requirements imposed during the assessment;
to encourage public participation in the elaboration of plans and programmes on environmental matters;
to ensure the completion of procedures within certain timeframes;
to introduce coordination mechanisms between the environmental impact assessment procedure and the strategic environmental assessment procedure;
to adopt coordination measures between the environmental impact assessment procedures and those for integrated pollution prevention and control, or for the integrated environmental permit, in the case of plants subject to both procedures, in order to avoid duplication and overlaps.
Strategic environmental assessment, or simply environmental assessment, concerns plans and programmes for intervention on the territory and is aimed at ensuring that the environmental effects arising from the implementation of said plans and programmes are taken into consideration during their elaboration and before their approval.
The procedure for strategic environmental assessment constitutes, for the plans and programmes subject to such assessment, an integral part of the ordinary procedure for adoption and approval. Approval measures adopted without prior strategic environmental assessment, where required, are null and void.
Environmental impact assessment concerns projects for works and interventions which, due to their nature or size, may have a significant impact on the environment and is aimed at ensuring that the effects deriving from the construction and operation of said works and interventions on the ecosystem are taken into consideration during their planning and before the approval or authorization of the related projects, or in any case before their implementation.
The procedure for environmental impact assessment constitutes, for the projects of works and interventions subject to it, a prerequisite or an integral part of the ordinary authorization or approval procedure. Authorization or approval measures adopted without prior environmental impact assessment, where required, are null and void.
Art. 5
Definitions
For the purposes of part two of this decree, the following definitions shall apply:
a) strategic environmental assessment procedure - SEA: the preparation of a report concerning the environmental impact resulting from the implementation of a specific plan or programme to be adopted or approved, the carrying out of consultations, the assessment of the environmental report and the results of the consultations in the decision-making process for the approval of a plan or programme, and the making available of information on the decision;
b) environmental impact assessment procedure - EIA: the preparation of a study concerning the environmental impact that may derive from the construction and operation of a work whose project is subject to approval or authorization, the carrying out of consultations, the assessment of the environmental study and the results of the consultations in the decision-making process for the approval or authorization of the project for the work, and the making available of information on the decision;
c) environmental impact: the qualitative and/or quantitative alteration of the environment, understood as a system of relationships between anthropic, physical, chemical, naturalistic, climatic, landscape, architectural, cultural, and economic factors, as a consequence of the implementation on the territory of plans or programmes or the realization of projects relating to particular plants, works, or public or private interventions, as well as the commissioning of the related activities;
d) plans and programmes: all acts and measures of planning and programming, however named, provided for by legislative, regulatory, or administrative provisions adopted or approved by state, regional, or local authorities, including those co-financed by the European Community, as well as their modifications; unless the applicable sector regulations provide otherwise, the strategic environmental assessment is carried out, before approval, on the adopted plans and programmes or, where a formal act of adoption is not provided for, on the proposals for plans or programmes that have reached a sufficient degree of elaboration for their presentation for approval;
e) project for a work or intervention: the preliminary, final, or executive technical design concerning the realization of a plant, work, or intervention, including interventions on the natural environment or landscape such as those intended for the exploitation of natural resources and soil; unless the applicable sector regulations expressly provide otherwise, the environmental impact assessment is carried out on the preliminary projects that contain the exact indication of the areas involved and the performance characteristics of the works to be realized, in addition to any further elements deemed useful for carrying out the environmental impact assessment;
f) substantial modification of a plan, programme, or project: the modification of an approved plan, programme, or project which, in the opinion of the competent authority, is likely to have significant effects on the environment;
g) substantial modification of a work or intervention: the intervention on an existing work from which a work with substantially different characteristics from the previous one derives; for the works or interventions for which dimensional thresholds are set in Annex III to part two of this decree, an intervention of expansion, enhancement, or extension also constitutes a substantial modification if said intervention, in itself, is equal to or greater than thirty percent of these thresholds;
h) proponent or developer: the entity or public authority responsible for the adoption of a plan or programme or, in general, that requests its approval, as well as the entity or public authority that takes the initiative for a public project and the subject who requests the authorization for a private project;
i) environmental report: the technical-scientific study containing the identification, description, and assessment of the significant effects that the implementation of a specific plan or programme could have on the environment, as well as the reasonable alternatives that can be adopted in consideration of the objectives and the territorial scope of the plan or programme;
l) environmental impact study: the technical-scientific study containing a description of the project with information on its location, design, and size, the identification, description, and assessment of the significant effects that the realization of the project would have on the environment, as well as a comparison with the reasonable alternatives that can be adopted in consideration of the objectives, interests, and services related to the planned work or intervention and the territorial area concerned;
m) environmental compatibility judgment: the act with which the competent body concludes the strategic environmental assessment or environmental impact assessment procedure;
n) authorization: the decision of the competent authority that enables the developer or proponent to realize the project;
o) competent authority: the administration responsible, under current legislation, for the adoption of a final measure of the procedure or of one of its phases;
p) consultation: the set of forms of participation, including direct participation, of other administrations and the public concerned in the collection and assessment of data and information that constitute the necessary knowledge base to express the judgment of environmental compatibility of a specific plan or programme or of a specific project;
q) public: one or more natural or legal persons and, in accordance with national legislation or practice, their associations, organizations, or groups;
r) public concerned: the public affected or likely to be affected by, or having an interest in, the environmental decision-making procedures; for the purposes of this definition, non-governmental organizations promoting environmental protection and meeting any requirements under national law, as well as the qualified representatives of economic and social interests present in the Economic and Social Council for Environmental Policies (CESPA), shall be deemed to have such an interest;
s) interested parties: any person who, taking into account the socio-economic and territorial characteristics of the plan or programme subject to strategic impact assessment or the project subject to environmental impact assessment, intends to provide cognitive and evaluative elements concerning the possible effects of the intervention itself;
t) screening procedure: the preliminary procedure, which precedes the presentation of the plan or programme proposal, or the presentation of the project, initiated for the purpose of defining whether a specific plan or programme must be subject to strategic environmental assessment, or whether a specific project must be subject to the environmental impact assessment procedure;
u) scoping phase: the procedure that precedes the presentation of the project, initiated for the purpose of defining, in consultation between the competent authority and the proponent, the information that must be provided in the environmental impact study.
Art. 6
Technical-advisory committee for environmental assessments
By decree of the President of the Council of Ministers, on the proposal of the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory, the Technical-Advisory Committee for Environmental Assessments is established at the Ministry for the Environment and Protection of the Territory. The same decree establishes the duration and the methods for the organization and functioning of the Committee itself.
The Committee provides the Ministry for the Environment and Protection of the Territory with technical-scientific support for the implementation of the provisions of part two of this decree. In particular, the Committee provides for the preliminary investigation and expresses opinions on the environmental reports and environmental impact studies relating to plans and programmes or projects respectively subject to strategic environmental assessment and environmental impact assessment of state competence, and also expresses opinions on integrated environmental permits of state competence.
The Committee is composed of seventy-eight members, in addition to the president and three vice-presidents, chosen from among university professors, professionals, and experts qualified in management systems, in measurements, and in design, geological, environmental, legal, economic, and social matters, as well as from among managers of the public administration.
The activity of the Committee is structured in three operational sectors headed by the three vice-presidents and concerning, respectively, the following procedures:
a) strategic environmental assessment;
b) environmental impact assessment;
c) integrated pollution prevention and control.
The Committee normally operates through subcommittees. The subcommittees are composed of a variable number of members depending on the professional skills necessary for the complete and adequate examination of the specific case. The identification of the necessary professional skills is the responsibility of the competent vice-president. Once the professional profiles of the members and the coordinator of the subcommittee have been identified, the individual commissioners are assigned to the subcommittees on the basis of a predefined rotation order.
Due to the specific regional interests involved in the exercise of an activity subject to the provisions of part two of this decree, the relevant subcommittee is supplemented by the expert designated by each of the regions directly affected by the activity by territory.
For the purposes of paragraph 6, the regional administrations directly affected by territory shall notify the Ministry for the Environment and Protection of the Territory of their interest.
If the administrations referred to in paragraph 7 have not provided for the designation of the experts, the subcommittee is constituted in its ordinary composition and proceeds in any case with the investigation entrusted to it, without prejudice to the possibility of its subsequent integration, in compliance with the stage of elaboration and any partial conclusions already reached.

TITLE II - STRATEGIC ENVIRONMENTAL ASSESSMENT - SEA
CHAPTER I - COMMON PROVISIONS ON SEA
Art. 7
Scope of application
The plans and programmes referred to in paragraph 2, as well as those referred to in paragraphs 3 and 4, if they are likely to have significant effects on the environment and cultural heritage, are subject to strategic environmental assessment. The modifications referred to in paragraph 5 are also subject to strategic environmental assessment.
Without prejudice to the provision of paragraph 3, the following are subject to strategic environmental assessment:
a) plans and programmes that meet both of the following requirements:
they concern the agricultural, forestry, fisheries, energy, industrial, transport, waste and water management, telecommunications, tourism, land-use planning or land use sectors;
they set the framework for the approval, authorization, location, or realization of works and interventions whose projects are subject to environmental impact assessment under current legislation;
b) plans and programmes concerning sites designated as special protection areas for the conservation of wild birds and those classified as sites of Community importance for the protection of natural habitats and wild flora and fauna.
Plans and programmes other than those referred to in paragraph 2, which set the framework for the approval, authorization, location, or realization of works and interventions whose projects, although not subject to environmental impact assessment under these provisions, may nevertheless have significant effects on the environment and cultural heritage, in the opinion of the competent subcommittee for strategic environmental assessment, are also subject to strategic environmental assessment.
The plans and programmes referred to in paragraph 2 that determine the use of small areas at a local level and the modifications of the plans and programmes referred to in paragraphs 2 and 3 that have already been approved are subject to strategic environmental assessment only if they are likely to have significant effects on the environment.
For the purposes of applying paragraphs 3 and 4, the authority competent for the approval of the plan or programme must preliminarily verify whether the specific plan or programme subject to approval is likely to have significant effects on the environment according to the criteria set out in Annex II to part two of this decree. An analogous verification must be carried out when approving a modification of an already approved plan or programme.
In the examination of individual cases and in the specification of the types of plans and programmes referred to in paragraph 2, other authorities which, due to their specific environmental competences, may be interested in the environmental effects resulting from the application of the plan or programme under examination must be consulted. For plans and programmes whose approval is the responsibility of State bodies, the opinion of the committee referred to in Article 6 must in any case be obtained.
The conclusions adopted pursuant to paragraphs 5 and 6, including the reasons for not carrying out the strategic environmental assessment, must be made available to the public.
The following are in any case excluded from the scope of application of the provisions of part two of this decree:
a) plans and programmes intended exclusively for national defence purposes characterized by extreme urgency or covered by state secrecy;
b) financial or budget plans and programmes;
c) plans and programmes relating to mobile telephony interventions subject to the provisions of Art. 87 of Legislative Decree no. 259 of August 1, 2003.
Art. 8
Integration of environmental assessment in planning procedures
The strategic environmental assessment must be carried out during the preparatory phase of the plan or programme and prior to its approval in a legislative or administrative capacity.
The administrative procedures provided for in this title are integrated into the ordinary procedures in force for the adoption and approval of plans and programmes.
In the case of hierarchically ordered plans and programmes, the authorities competent for the approval of the individual plans or programmes shall take into account, in order to avoid duplication of judgment, the assessments already carried out for the approval of the higher-level plan and those to be carried out for the approval of the subordinate plans.
Art. 9
Environmental report
For plans and programmes subject to strategic environmental assessment, an environmental report must be drawn up, before and for the purposes of approval, which constitutes an integral part of the documentation of the proposed or adopted plan or programme to be approved.
The environmental report must identify, describe, and evaluate the significant effects that the implementation of the proposed plan or programme could have on the environment and cultural heritage, as well as the reasonable alternatives that can be adopted in consideration of the objectives and the territorial scope of the plan or programme itself. Annex I to part two of this decree lists the information to be provided for this purpose to the extent that it can be reasonably required, taking into account the level of knowledge and current assessment methods, the contents and level of detail of the plan or programme and, in cases of multi-level planning processes, taking into account that certain aspects are more adequately assessed in other subsequent phases of said process.
To prepare the environmental report, the information referred to in Annex I to part two of this decree concerning the environmental effects of the plan and programme under assessment may be used, which is in any case available and has also been obtained within the framework of other decision-making levels or otherwise acquired in implementation of other regulatory provisions.
The proponent has the option of initiating a preliminary phase for the purpose of defining, in consultation with the competent authority, the information to be provided in the environmental report.
Other authorities which, due to their specific environmental competences, may be interested in the environmental effects of the application of the plan or programme under examination must be consulted at the time of the decision on the scope of the information to be included in the environmental report and on its level of detail.
A non-technical summary of the contents of the proposed plan or programme and of the other data and information contained in the report itself must be attached to the environmental report.
Art. 10
Consultations
Before approval, the adopted plan or programme, or, if a formal act of adoption is not provided for, the proposal of the plan or programme and the environmental report prepared in accordance with Article 9 must be made available to the other authorities which, due to their specific environmental or landscape competences, exercise administrative functions related to the environmental effects of the application of the plan or programme, and to the public.
For the purposes of paragraph 1 and paragraph 4, the proposal of the plan or programme and the related environmental report must be sent to all the aforementioned other authorities. The non-technical summary, indicating the locations where the full documentation can be inspected, must be deposited in an adequate number of copies at the offices of the provinces and regions whose territory is even partially affected by the plan or programme or by the effects of its implementation.
The sending and deposit referred to in paragraph 2 must be announced in the press in the manner established by a specific regulation, which ensures uniform publicity criteria for all plans and programmes subject to strategic environmental assessment, guaranteeing that the public concerned is in all cases adequately informed. The same regulation establishes the cases and methods for the simultaneous total or partial publication on the internet of the proposal of the plan or programme and the related environmental report. The regulation must be issued by decree of the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory within ninety days from the date of entry into force of part two of this decree. Until the entry into force of the regulation, publications must be carried out at the care and expense of the interested party in a national newspaper and in a regional newspaper for each directly interested region.
Within a period of forty-five days from the publication of the notice of deposit and any publication on the internet pursuant to paragraph 3, anyone with an interest may inspect the proposal of the plan or programme and the related environmental report deposited and publicized in accordance with paragraphs 1, 2, and 3. Within the same period, anyone may submit their own observations, including by providing new or further cognitive and evaluative elements.
The deposits and publications, referred to in paragraphs 2 and 3, with the connected and consequent consultations, referred to in paragraph 4, replace for all purposes all forms of information and participation possibly provided for by the ordinary procedures for the adoption and approval of the same plans or programmes.
Art. 11
Transboundary consultations
Where the implementation of a specific plan or programme subject to strategic environmental assessment is likely to have significant effects on the environment of another Member State of the European Union, or where the Member State that is likely to be significantly affected so requests, a full copy of the proposal of the plan or programme and the environmental report, prepared in accordance with Article 9, must be transmitted, before the approval of the plan or programme, also to said interested Member State, inviting it to express its opinion within a period of sixty days from the receipt of the transmitted documentation.
Where the Member State, to which a copy of the proposal of the plan or programme and the environmental report has been transmitted pursuant to paragraph 1, communicates within thirty days of receipt that, in order to express its opinion, it intends to proceed with consultations, the competent authority must grant a suitable period, in any case not exceeding ninety days, to allow the Member State to proceed with consultations with its own internal authorities and the public concerned. In the meantime, any other deadline is suspended.
Art. 12
Environmental compatibility judgment and approval of the proposed plan or programme
Before the approval of the plan or programme subject to strategic environmental assessment, the environmental report prepared pursuant to Article 9, the opinions expressed pursuant to Article 10, as well as any opinions of other Member States rendered pursuant to Article 11, must be examined and evaluated.
Based on the results of the examination and evaluations referred to in paragraph 1, the authority responsible for the environmental assessment, within sixty days from the expiry of the last deadline for the submission of opinions under Articles 10 and 11, shall issue the environmental compatibility judgment containing a detailed and reasoned environmental opinion which constitutes a prerequisite for the continuation of the procedure for the approval of the plan or programme. The environmental compatibility judgment may be conditional on the adoption of specific modifications and integrations to the proposal of the evaluated plan or programme. In such cases, the judgment is transmitted to the proponent with an invitation to make the necessary changes before resubmitting the plan or programme for approval. The expiration of the term referred to in this paragraph without action implies the exercise of substitutive power by the Council of Ministers, which shall act within sixty days, after formal notice to the competent body to comply within a period of twenty days, also at the request of the interested parties.
In the absence thereof, for plans and programmes subject to environmental assessment at the state level, a negative judgment on the environmental compatibility of the presented plan or programme is deemed to have been issued. For plans and programmes subject to environmental assessment at a non-state level, the provisions of the preceding period apply until the entry into force of specific regional and autonomous province regulations, to be adopted in compliance with the relevant Community discipline in force.
The approval of the plan or programme shall take into account the opinion referred to in paragraph 2. To this end, the approval measure must be accompanied by a summary statement illustrating how environmental considerations have been integrated into the plan or programme and how the environmental report prepared pursuant to Article 9, the opinions expressed pursuant to Article 10, and the results of the consultations initiated pursuant to Article 11 have been taken into account, as well as the reasons for which the adopted plan or programme was chosen, also with respect to the possible alternatives that had been identified, and, finally, the measures adopted regarding monitoring.
If, during the investigation for the approval of a plan or programme to be subjected to strategic environmental assessment pursuant to Article 7, it is found that the relevant procedure has not been initiated, the authority competent for the approval of said plan or programme shall formally invite the proponent to initiate said procedure and simultaneously suspend the approval procedure.
Art. 13
Information about the decision
The environmental compatibility judgments and the approval measures referred to, respectively, in paragraphs 2 and 3 of Article 12 must be made available to the public, together with the related documentation, by the proponent, who is required to give notice thereof in the press according to the methods established by the regulation referred to in Article 10, paragraph 3.
The same environmental compatibility judgments and approval measures are transmitted in full copy by the competent authority to the other authorities and to the Member States that have participated in the consultations referred to in Articles 10 and 11.
Art. 14
Monitoring
The authorities responsible for the approval of plans or programmes shall, using the system of Environmental Agencies, monitor the significant environmental effects of the implementation of the approved plans and programmes, in order, among other things, to identify at an early stage unforeseen negative effects and to be able to adopt appropriate corrective measures.
To comply with the provision of paragraph 1, existing control mechanisms must be used, as far as possible, in order to avoid duplication of monitoring.
The corrective measures adopted pursuant to paragraph 1 shall be notified to the public by means of the press according to the methods established by the regulation referred to in Article 10, paragraph 3.
CHAPTER II - SPECIFIC PROVISIONS FOR SEA AT THE STATE LEVEL
Art. 15
Plans and programmes subject to SEA at the state level
Plans and programmes referred to in Article 7 whose approval is the responsibility of State bodies are subject to strategic environmental assessment at the state level.
For the environmental assessment of the plans and programmes referred to in paragraph 1, the provisions of this chapter supplement and specify the provisions of Chapter I; the latter also apply to the assessment of the projects referred to in paragraph 1 where not otherwise provided for in this Chapter II.
Art. 16
Initiation of the procedure
For the plans and programmes referred to in Article 15, before the initiation of the approval procedure, the adopted or otherwise proposed plan or programme must be submitted, accompanied by the environmental report and the non-technical summary, to the Ministry for the Environment and Protection of the Territory, to the Ministry for Cultural Heritage and Activities, to the Technical-Advisory Committee for Environmental Assessments referred to in Article 6, and to any other interested Ministries.
For the plans and programmes referred to in Article 15, before the initiation of the approval procedure, pursuant to Article 10, paragraphs 1 and 2, an adequate number of copies of the non-technical summary must be deposited at the offices of the provinces and regions whose territory is even partially affected by the plan or programme or by the effects of its implementation; a full copy of the proposal of the plan or programme and the environmental report must also be sent to the regions.
Notice of the deposits and submissions must be published in the manner provided for in Article 10, paragraph 3.
In the phases referred to in Articles 19 and 20, if carried out, and in any case at the start of the investigation, due to the specific characteristics of the proposed plan or programme and also at the request of the proponent, specific and different methods of publication and information may be established, as appropriate, supplementing or simplifying those referred to in paragraphs 2 and 3. If such modifications are ordered during the investigation and involve the renewal of the press notice referred to in paragraph 3, all deadlines of the procedure are interrupted and restart from the publication of the new announcement.
Art. 17
Investigation and adoption of the environmental compatibility judgment
The technical-investigative activities for the strategic environmental assessment of plans and programmes whose approval is the responsibility of State bodies are carried out by the Committee referred to in Article 6. To this end, the competent vice-president, for each proposal of a plan or programme sent to him pursuant to Article 16, paragraph 1, provides for the establishment of a specific subcommittee according to the criteria of Article 6, paragraph 5; where the conditions are met, the subcommittee is supplemented pursuant to paragraph 6 of the same Article 6.
If the subcommittee verifies the incompleteness of the submitted documentation, it may request its integration. In this case, the deadlines of the procedure remain suspended until the receipt of the requested integrations.
The appointed subcommittee acquires and evaluates all the submitted documentation, as well as the observations, objections, and suggestions forwarded pursuant to Articles 10 and 11, and expresses its reasoned opinion within a period of thirty days from the expiry of all the deadlines referred to in Articles 10 and 11, without prejudice to any suspension ordered pursuant to paragraph 2.
In case of delay, and after formal notice to act within ten days, also at the request of the interested parties, all the powers of the vice-presidents are exercised by the President of the Committee.
The opinion expressed by the subcommittee is immediately transmitted by the competent vice-president to the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory, who, in concert with the Minister for Cultural Heritage and Activities and with the proposing Minister, within the following thirty days, provides for the adoption of the environmental compatibility judgment.
The expiration of the term referred to in paragraph 5 without action implies the exercise of substitutive power by the Council of Ministers, pursuant to and with the effects of Article 12, paragraph 2.
Art. 18
Effects of the environmental compatibility judgment
The proposals of plans and programmes subject to strategic environmental assessment, even if they have already been adopted with a formal act, are reviewed and, if necessary, reformulated, on the basis of the environmental compatibility judgment rendered pursuant to Article 17.
For the purposes of the provisions of Article 4, paragraph 3, the environmental compatibility judgment is in any case attached to the plan or programme submitted for approval.
For the purposes of the approval of the plan or programme, Article 12, paragraph 3, applies.
Art. 19
Screening procedure
Plans and programmes other than those referred to in Article 7, paragraph 2, but which nevertheless concern the agricultural, forestry, fisheries, energy, industrial, transport, waste and water management, telecommunications, tourism, land-use planning or land use sectors, as well as modifications to said plans and programmes, are subject to a screening procedure in order to ascertain whether the conditions of paragraphs 3, 4, and 5 of the same Article 7 are met.
The screening is carried out by the authority competent for the approval of the plans or programmes, at the request of the proponent and having acquired the opinion of the Committee referred to in Article 6, which shall decide, based on the criteria of Annex II to part two of this decree, within thirty days of the request. To this end, the screening request, together with the proposal of the plan or programme and its related attached documents, must be forwarded in copy to said Committee to allow the timely establishment of the subcommittee responsible for expressing the opinion. In case of a positive outcome, the investigation referred to in Article 17 is also assigned to the appointed subcommittee; moreover, taking into account the specific characteristics of the proposed plan or programme, the information methods may be simultaneously specified, also in derogation of the provisions of paragraphs 2 and 3 of Article 16.
If, during the investigation for the approval of a new plan or programme, or of a modification to an already approved plan or programme, it is found that the screening procedure referred to in paragraphs 1 and 2 has not been carried out, such procedure is initiated by the authority competent for the approval, which, to this end, transmits to the Committee referred to in Article 6 all the useful documentation in its possession and simultaneously suspends the approval procedure.
Art. 20
Scoping phase
For plans and programmes subject to strategic environmental assessment at the state level, the scoping phase referred to in Article 9, paragraph 4, takes place in consultation between the proponent and the Committee referred to in Article 6.
For the purposes of paragraph 1, the interested proponent has the option to directly request the competent vice-president to establish, according to the criteria of Article 6, paragraphs 5 and 6, a specific subcommittee with which to interact.
At the end of the scoping phase, the appointed subcommittee, having heard the territorially interested regions pursuant to and for the effects of Article 9, paragraph 5, drafts a report indicating precisely all the information that must be included in the environmental report and its relative level of detail. With the same report, taking into account the specific characteristics of the proposed plan or programme, the information methods may be specified, also in derogation of paragraphs 2 and 3 of Article 16.
The subcommittee appointed for the scoping phase is also responsible for the investigation referred to in Article 17.
CHAPTER III - SPECIFIC PROVISIONS FOR SEA AT THE REGIONAL OR PROVINCIAL LEVEL
Art. 21
Plans and programmes subject to SEA at the regional or provincial level
Plans and programmes referred to in Article 7 whose approval is the responsibility of the regions or local authorities are subject to strategic environmental assessment at the regional or provincial level.
Art. 22
SEA procedures at the regional or provincial level
Without prejudice to the provisions of Articles 4, 5, 7, 8, 9, 10, 11, 12, 13, and 14, the regions and the autonomous provinces of Trento and Bolzano shall regulate with their own laws and regulations the procedures for the strategic environmental assessment of the plans and programmes referred to in Article 21.
Until the entry into force of the regional and provincial regulations referred to in paragraph 1, the provisions of part two of this decree shall apply
TITLE III - ENVIRONMENTAL IMPACT ASSESSMENT - EIA
CHAPTER I - COMMON PROVISIONS ON EIA
Art. 23
Scope of application
The following are subject to the environmental impact assessment procedure:
a) projects listed in list A of Annex III to part two of this decree, wherever located;
b) projects listed in list B of Annex III to part two of this decree that fall, even partially, within protected natural areas as defined by Law no. 394 of December 6, 1991;
c) projects listed in list B of Annex III to part two of this decree that do not fall within protected natural areas, but which, based on the elements indicated in Annex IV to part two of this decree, in the opinion of the competent authority, nevertheless require the environmental impact assessment procedure to be carried out;
d) projects for specific works or interventions for which the environmental impact assessment procedure is expressly required by special sector-specific laws governing said works or interventions.
For projects of works or interventions referred to in paragraph 1, letter a), located within protected natural areas, the dimensional thresholds, where provided, are reduced by fifty percent.
The same procedure also applies to interventions on existing works not falling within the categories of paragraph 1, if such interventions result in a work that falls into those same categories. It also applies to substantial modifications of works and interventions falling within the categories of paragraph 1, letters a) and b).
The following projects may be excluded from the scope of application of this title which, in the opinion of the competent authority, do not require the environmental impact assessment procedure to be carried out:
a) projects related to works and interventions intended exclusively for national defence purposes;
b) projects related to works and interventions intended exclusively for civil protection purposes, or ordered in situations of necessity and urgency for the purpose of safeguarding human life from imminent danger or in response to disasters;
c) projects related to works of a temporary nature, including those exclusively necessary for the execution of authorized remediation interventions.
For the projects referred to in paragraph 1, letter c), and paragraph 4, letters a), b), and c), the screening procedure referred to in Article 32 applies. During this screening procedure, for the projects referred to in paragraph 4, the competent authority shall communicate to the European Commission, before granting any exemption, the reasons justifying such an exemption pursuant to Art. 2, paragraph 3, letter c), of Directive 85/337/EEC.
For the purposes of the application of Art. 4 of Legislative Decree no. 13 of January 17, 2005, for airport projects subject to the environmental impact assessment procedure pursuant to part two of this decree, such procedure shall take into account the requirements defined in ANNEX 2 of the same Legislative Decree no. 13 of January 17, 2005.
In the case of works and interventions of extreme urgency intended exclusively for national defence as per paragraph 4, letter a), the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory shall, on the proposal of the Minister of Defence, grant an exemption from any environmental compatibility verification only for projects related to works covered by state secrecy.
Art. 24
Objectives of the EIA
The environmental impact assessment procedure must ensure that:
a) in the decision-making processes concerning the realization of projects identified in the Annexes to part two of this decree, the objectives of protecting health and improving the quality of human life are considered, in order to contribute with a better environment to the quality of life, provide for the maintenance of species diversity and preserve the reproductive capacity of the ecosystem as an essential life resource, as well as the objectives of ensuring the multiple use of natural resources, of public goods intended for collective enjoyment, and of ensuring sustainable development;
b) for each project, the direct and indirect effects of its realization on humans, fauna, flora, soil, surface and groundwater, air, climate, landscape, and the interaction between these factors, on material assets, and on cultural and environmental heritage are evaluated;
c) for each project, the main reasons for the choice among the alternatives proposed by the developer are made explicit;
d) at every stage of the procedure, the exchange of information and consultation between the proponent and the competent authority are guaranteed;
e) public information and participation in the procedure are guaranteed;
f) the simplification, rationalization, and coordination of assessments and authorizations in environmental matters are achieved.
Art. 25
Jurisdiction and procedures
The environmental impact assessment is the responsibility of:
a) for projects of works and interventions subject to state authorization and for those with interregional or international environmental impact, the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory, in concert with the Minister for Cultural Heritage and Activities, according to the provisions of this Chapter I and Chapter II;
b) in other cases, the authority identified by the region or autonomous province by its own law, taking into account the attributions of competence for the issuance of the authorization for the realization of the various works and interventions and according to the procedures established by the same, on the basis of the guiding criteria of Chapter III of this title, without prejudice to the common provisions of this Chapter I.
Art. 26
Initiation of the procedure
The developer or proponent of the work or intervention must submit a specific application to the competent authority, enclosing the project, the environmental impact study, and the non-technical summary.
A full copy of the application referred to in paragraph 1 and its annexes must be transmitted to the interested regions, provinces, and municipalities and, in the case of protected natural areas, also to their respective managing bodies, which must express their opinion within sixty days of receiving the application. After this period has elapsed, the competent authority shall issue the environmental compatibility judgment even in the absence of said opinions.
Due to the specific dimensional and functional characteristics of the planned work or intervention, or due to the number of potentially interested local authorities and the size of the project's documentation and related environmental impact study, the developer or proponent, by initiating a specific preliminary phase for this purpose, may request to be fully or partially exempted from the obligations under paragraph 2, or to be authorized to adopt other appropriate disclosure systems.
Without prejudice to the provisions of Article 29, paragraph 5, in case of acceptance of opinions, observations, or findings, any integrations to the submitted study or to the attached documentation may be requested, with an indication of a reasonable deadline for the response, or submitted by the developer or proponent, on a single occasion. In such cases, all deadlines of the procedure are interrupted and restart from the date of receipt of the supplementary documentation. If the interested party does not comply, the assessment shall not proceed further. The developer or proponent has the option to submit a new application.
Art. 27
Environmental impact study
The environmental impact study is prepared at the care and expense of the developer or proponent, according to the indications in Annex V to part two of this decree.
For projects subject to environmental impact assessment, the developer or proponent has the option, before initiating the environmental impact assessment procedure, to request the competent authority to carry out a preliminary phase for the purpose of defining, in consultation with said authority, the information, including that in Annex V to part two of this decree, that must be contained in the environmental impact study. To this end, the developer or proponent submits a report which, based on the identification of the expected environmental impacts, defines the work plan for the preparation of the environmental impact study, the methodologies it intends to adopt for the elaboration of the information contained therein, and its relative level of detail. The competent authority, even if said opinion has been rendered, may request the developer or proponent, after the initiation of the environmental impact assessment procedure, for clarifications and integrations regarding the submitted documentation.
Other authorities which, due to their specific environmental competences, may be interested in the environmental effects of the realization and operation of the planned work or intervention must be consulted, at the time of the decision, on the scope of the information to be included in the environmental impact study and on its level of detail.
The requested information must be consistent with the necessary level of detail and strictly relevant to the specific characteristics of a certain type of project and the components of the environment likely to be affected, also in relation to the location of the intervention, taking into account available knowledge and assessment methods. If the developer or proponent believes that certain information should not be disclosed for reasons of business or personal confidentiality, protection of intellectual property, public security, or national defence, they may produce, along with the complete version, a version of the environmental impact study devoid of said information. The competent authority, having assessed the reasons for confidentiality provided by the proponent, may order that the consultation of the environmental impact study by the public concerned be limited to this version.
The environmental impact study must in any case contain at least the following information:
a) a description of the project with information on its characteristics, location, and dimensions;
b) a description of the measures planned to avoid, reduce, and possibly offset significant negative effects;
c) the data necessary to identify and assess the main effects on the environment and cultural heritage that the project may produce, both in the construction and operational phases;
d) a summary description of the main alternatives examined by the developer, including the so-called "zero option," with an indication of the main reasons for the choice, from the perspective of environmental impact;
e) an assessment of the cost-benefit ratio of the project from an environmental, economic, and social point of view.
A non-technical summary of the dimensional and functional characteristics of the planned work or intervention and of the data and information contained in the study itself must be attached to the environmental impact study.
For the purposes of preparing the study, the public or private entity interested in the realization of the works or plants has the right to access the information and data available at the offices of public administrations.
Art. 28
Publicity measures
The administrations of the State, the regions, and the autonomous provinces of Trento and Bolzano shall ensure the identification of the offices where, on a permanent or case-by-case basis, the documents and acts relating to the assessment procedures, pending or concluded, concerning works and interventions relevant to their respective powers and competences, are deposited and can be consulted by the public.
Simultaneously with the submission of the application referred to in Article 26, the developer or proponent shall, at their own expense:
a) deposit the project of the work, the environmental impact study, and an adequate number of copies of the non-technical summary at the offices identified, pursuant to paragraph 1, by the State administrations, the regions, and the interested autonomous provinces;
b) disseminate a press announcement of the deposit, according to the methods established by the competent authority with a specific regulation that ensures uniform publicity criteria for all projects subject to environmental impact assessment, guaranteeing that the public concerned is in all cases adequately informed. The same regulation establishes the cases and methods for the simultaneous total or partial publication of the project on the internet. The regulation must be issued by decree of the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory within ninety days from the date of entry into force of part two of this decree. Until the entry into force of the regulation, publications shall be carried out at the care and expense of the interested party in a national newspaper and in a regional newspaper for each directly interested region.
Appeals against the decisions, acts, or omissions subject to the provisions on public participation established by Title III of part two of this decree are always admissible according to the general rules on challenging illegal administrative acts.
Art. 29
Participation in the procedure
The interested party who intends to provide cognitive and evaluative elements concerning the possible effects of the planned work or intervention may submit written observations on said project, subject to the environmental impact assessment procedure, to the competent authority within a period of forty-five days from the publication referred to in Article 28, paragraph 2, letter b). The environmental compatibility judgment shall consider, simultaneously, individually or in groups, such observations, the opinions provided by public administrations, and any other observations from the public.
The competent authority for the environmental impact assessment may order a public inquiry to examine the study presented by the developer or proponent, the opinions provided by public administrations, and the observations of the public.
The inquiry referred to in paragraph 2 suspends the deadline referred to in Article 31, paragraph 1, and concludes within the sixtieth day from the one on which it was initiated, regardless of the stage reached by the planned operations. Within the same period, the competent authority shall draft a report on the work carried out and a judgment on the results that have emerged, which are acquired and evaluated for the purposes of the judgment referred to in Article 31.
The developer or proponent, if the inquiry referred to in paragraph 2 does not take place, may, also at their own request, be summoned by the competent authority, before the conclusion of the procedure, for a summary adversarial hearing with the parties who have submitted opinions or observations. The record of the adversarial hearing is acquired and evaluated for the purposes of the judgment referred to in Article 31.
When the developer or proponent intends to conform, in whole or in part, the project to the opinions or observations, or to the findings that emerged during the public inquiry or the adversarial hearing, they shall make a request to the competent authority, indicating the necessary time. The request suspends all deadlines of the procedure, which resume their course with the deposit of the modified project.
Art. 30
Technical investigation
The technical investigation of the projects referred to in Article 23 has the following objectives:
a) to ascertain the completeness of the submitted documentation;
b) to verify the correspondence of the description of the places and their environmental characteristics with those documented by the proponent;
c) to verify that the project data, concerning the production and management of liquid and solid waste, polluting emissions into the atmosphere, noise, and any other potential source of pollution, correspond to the requirements dictated by the sector regulations;
d) to ascertain the coherence of the project, concerning the construction techniques and the planned production processes, with the data on the use of raw materials and natural resources;
e) to ascertain the correct use of analysis and forecasting tools, as well as the suitability of the detection and forecasting techniques employed by the proponent in relation to the environmental effects;
f) to identify and describe the overall impact of the project's realization on the environment and cultural heritage, also in relation to the final quality levels, comparing the existing situation at the time of the communication with the forecast of the subsequent one.

Art. 31
Environmental compatibility judgment
The environmental impact assessment procedure must conclude with a reasoned judgment within ninety days from the publication referred to in Article 28, paragraph 2, letter b), except in cases of interruption and suspension expressly provided for.
The expiration of the term referred to in paragraph 1 without action, calculated taking into account any interruptions and suspensions that have occurred, implies the exercise of substitutive power by the Council of Ministers, which shall act within sixty days, after formal notice to the competent body to comply within a period of twenty days, also at the request of the interested parties. In the absence thereof, for projects subject to environmental impact assessment at the state level, a negative judgment on the environmental compatibility of the project is deemed to have been issued. For projects subject to environmental impact assessment at a non-state level, the provisions of the preceding period apply until the entry into force of specific regional and autonomous province regulations, to be adopted in compliance with the relevant Community discipline in force.
The administration competent for the final authorization for the realization of the work or the planned intervention shall acquire the environmental compatibility judgment, including any requirements for the mitigation of impacts, the monitoring of the works and plants, and the measures planned to avoid, reduce, or possibly offset significant negative effects. In the case of initiatives promoted by public authorities, the final measure authorizing their realization must adequately demonstrate the conformity of the choices made with the outcomes of the environmental impact procedure. In other cases, the projects must be adapted to the outcomes of the environmental compatibility judgment before the issuance of the authorization for realization.
The outcomes of the environmental impact assessment procedure must be communicated to the parties to the procedure, to all competent public administrations, including in matters of environmental controls, and must be adequately publicized. In particular, the information made available to the public includes: the content of the decision and any conditions attached to it; the main reasons and considerations on which the decision is based, taking into account the requests and opinions of the public, as well as information on the public participation process; a description, where necessary, of the main measures prescribed in order to avoid, reduce, and if possible, offset the most significant negative effects.
Art. 32
Screening procedure
For the projects referred to in Article 23, paragraph 1, letter c), and paragraph 4, letters a), b), and c), the developer or proponent shall first request the screening provided for therein from the competent authority. The information that the developer or proponent must provide for said screening concerns a description of the project and the data necessary to identify and assess the main effects that the project may have on the environment.
If the competent authority deems that the project must be subject to environmental impact assessment, Articles 26 and following shall apply.
The competent authority must rule within sixty days from the date of the application, identifying any requirements for the mitigation of impacts and for the monitoring of the works or plants; the remedies provided for by current legislation are available against administrative silence. The Ministry for the Environment and Protection of the Territory, the regions, and the autonomous provinces of Trento and Bolzano shall ensure that the list of projects for which screening has been requested and their respective outcomes are made public.
Art. 33
Relations between SEA and EIA
For projects of works and interventions to be carried out in implementation of plans or programmes that have already been subject to strategic environmental assessment, and which fall within the categories for which environmental impact assessment is required, all elements positively evaluated during the strategic assessment or in any case decided during the approval of the plan or programme shall constitute acquired data during the execution of the latter assessment.
Art. 34
Relations between EIA and IPPC
For works and interventions subject to environmental impact assessment and simultaneously falling within the scope of application of Legislative Decree no. 59 of February 18, 2005, as well as for substantial modifications, according to the definition in Article 5, paragraph 1, letter g), of such works or interventions, the proponent has the option to obtain that the environmental impact assessment procedure be integrated into the procedure for the issuance of the integrated environmental permit.
For the purposes of paragraph 1, where the proponent expresses the will to avail itself of said option:
a) the project and the environmental impact study, to be submitted pursuant to part two of this decree, shall also include the information referred to in Article 5, paragraphs 1 and 2, of Legislative Decree no. 59 of February 18, 2005, with the necessary level of detail;
b) the deposits of acts and documents, the publications, and the consultations provided for by part two of this decree shall replace for all purposes all forms of information and participation provided for in the aforementioned Legislative Decree no. 59 of February 18, 2005;
c) pending the environmental impact assessment procedure, the procedure for the issuance of the integrated environmental permit, if already initiated, remains suspended;
d) the investigation of the environmental impact study is conducted by the bodies responsible for the investigation of the application for the integrated environmental permit, and the related opinion on environmental impact assessment is supplemented with regard to the aspects connected with integrated pollution prevention and control, in accordance with Community principles and the dictates of the relevant implementing rules;
e) once the environmental impact assessment procedure is concluded, the environmental compatibility judgment is also communicated to the authority competent for the issuance of the integrated environmental permit, which resumes the relevant procedure with the transmission of the aforementioned judgment to the administrations referred to in Art. 5, paragraphs 10 and 11, of Legislative Decree no. 59 of February 18, 2005, for the expression of their competent opinion; with the preceding phases being absorbed into the procedure already carried out, the conference of services referred to in Article 5, paragraph 10, of Legislative Decree no. 59 of February 18, 2005, is held within the following thirty days, simultaneously with the final phase of the conference of services referred to in Art. 1, paragraph 2, of Decree-Law no. 7 of February 7, 2002, converted, with amendments, by Law no. 55 of April 9, 2002;
f) the authority competent for the issuance of the integrated environmental permit shall rule taking into account the environmental compatibility judgment issued on the project of the work or intervention for which said permit has been requested;
g) is required to pay a single fee in the amount established by the decree referred to in Article 49, paragraph 2.
Modifications to plants subject to the discipline laid down by Legislative Decree no. 59 of February 18, 2005, which constitute a mere implementation of requirements contained in the integrated environmental permit, are not considered substantial modifications for the purposes of part two of this decree.
The modifications planned for plants subject to the discipline laid down by Legislative Decree no. 59 of February 18, 2005, which pursuant to Art. 10 of said legislative decree are not found to be substantial, do not constitute substantial modifications for the purposes of the provisions of part two of this decree.
For thermal power plants with a capacity exceeding 300 MW, as well as for substantial modifications to them, according to the definition in Article 5, paragraph 1, letter g), the environmental impact assessment procedure is integrated into the procedure for the issuance of the integrated environmental permit. Paragraph 2 of this article applies, with the exception of the provision in letter c).
Modifications to electricity production plants and related connected works, which are also subject to the discipline of Legislative Decree no. 59 of February 18, 2005, and which constitute mere implementations of requirements contained in the integrated environmental permit and in the authorization referred to in Art. 1, paragraph 1, of Decree-Law no. 7 of February 7, 2002, converted, with amendments, by Law no. 55 of April 9, 2002, are not considered substantial modifications for the purposes of part two of this decree and are to be included in the relevant authorization measures.
CHAPTER II - SPECIFIC PROVISIONS FOR EIA AT THE STATE LEVEL
Art. 35
Projects subject to EIA at the state level
The environmental impact assessment of projects for works and interventions falling into the categories of Article 23 is the responsibility of the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory, in concert with the Minister for Cultural Heritage and Activities, having consulted the interested region and based on the investigation carried out by the Technical-Advisory Committee referred to in Article 6, in cases where it concerns:
a) works or interventions subject to authorization for construction or operation by State bodies;
b) works or interventions located in the territory of more than one region or which may in any case have significant impacts on more than one region;
c) works or interventions that may have significant effects on the environment of another Member State of the European Union.
For the environmental impact assessment of the projects referred to in paragraph 1, the provisions of this Chapter II supplement and specify the provisions of Chapter I; the latter also apply to the assessment of the projects referred to in paragraph 1 where not otherwise provided for in this Chapter II.
Art. 36
Assessment procedure
Pursuant to and for the purposes of Article 26, paragraphs 1 and 2, the projects for the works and interventions referred to in Article 35 must be submitted to the Ministry for the Environment and Protection of the Territory, to the Ministry for Cultural Heritage and Activities, to the territorially interested region, to the Technical-Advisory Committee for Environmental Assessments referred to in Article 6, and to any other interested Ministries. The environmental impact study referred to in Article 27 and its related non-technical summary must be attached to the project. If the planned work or intervention affects more than one region, a copy of the project, to which the environmental impact study referred to in Article 27 and its related non-technical summary are attached, must be sent to each region.
For works and interventions that fall within the territory of multiple local authorities, only the extract of the project and the environmental impact study relating to the portion of the work or intervention that affects the relevant territorial area may be deposited with each province and each municipality, without prejudice to the deposit of the non-technical summary in its full version. The same possibility is permitted with regard to protected natural areas and their respective managing bodies.
The option for the developer or proponent to request in advance from the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory the definition, pursuant to Article 26, paragraph 3, of more adequate and practicable disclosure methods in relation to the specific characteristics of the project remains unaffected. With the same methods, at the express request of the developer or proponent, the communications and deposits to be made for the reopening before the Ministry for the Environment and Protection of the Territory of the procedure originally initiated at the regional or provincial level, and for which the authority designated by the region or autonomous province has declared itself incompetent pursuant to Article 42, paragraph 3, can be defined.
The interested regions, provinces, and municipalities must express their opinion within sixty days from the date of the transmission referred to in paragraphs 1 and 2. After this period has elapsed, the compatibility judgment may be issued even in the absence of said opinions.
Without prejudice to the provisions of the regulation referred to in Article 28, paragraph 2, letter b), the announcement of the submission must in any case be published, at the care of the developer or proponent, at least in a national newspaper and in a regional newspaper for each territorially interested region.
Anyone with an interest, pursuant to the laws in force, may submit to the Ministry for the Environment and Protection of the Territory, or directly to the Technical-Advisory Committee referred to in Article 6, and to the interested region, written petitions, observations, or opinions on the work subject to environmental impact assessment, within a period of thirty days from the publication of the project's communication.
The Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory, based on the investigation carried out pursuant to Article 37, shall rule on the environmental compatibility, in concert with the Minister for Cultural Heritage and Activities and with the proposing Minister, within ninety days from the date of the last of the publications referred to in paragraph 5, and in any case not before sixty days have elapsed from the last of the transmissions referred to in paragraphs 1 and 2, subject to extension decided by the Council of Ministers in cases of particular importance.
The expiration of the terms referred to in paragraph 7 without action, calculated taking into account any interruptions and suspensions that have occurred, implies the exercise of substitutive power by the Council of Ministers, which shall act pursuant to and with the effects of Article 31, paragraph 2.
For the works referred to in paragraph 1, letter a), of Article 35, the Minister competent for their realization, if he does not deem it appropriate to conform the proposed project to the compatibility judgment of the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory, may propose with justification to the President of the Council of Ministers the adoption of a measure to review said judgment, or order the non-realization of the project. The Council of Ministers shall decide on the review proposal within the terms and with the effects referred to in paragraph 8 of this article.

Art. 37
Investigative tasks of the technical-advisory committee
The technical-investigative activities for the environmental assessment of projects for works and interventions of State competence are carried out by the Committee referred to in Article 6. To this end, the competent vice-president, for each project sent to him pursuant to Article 26, paragraph 1, provides for the establishment of a specific subcommittee according to the criteria of Article 6, paragraph 5; where the conditions are met, the subcommittee is supplemented pursuant to paragraph 6 of the same Article 6.
