4. For the management and provision of the integrated management service and for the pursuit of the objectives determined by the Area Authority, the following activities are entrusted, pursuant to article 202 and in respect of the community and national legislation on public evidence:
a) the realization, management, and provision of the entire service, including the management and realization of the plants;
b) the collection, separate collection, commercialization, and complete disposal of all urban and assimilated waste produced within the ATO.
5. In each area:
a) self-sufficiency of disposal is reached, within five years of its constitution, also, where appropriate, through forms of cooperation and connection with other public and private subjects;
b) the presence of at least one complex technology treatment plant, including a service landfill, is guaranteed.
6. The duration of the management by the entrusted subjects, not less than fifteen years, is regulated by the regions in such a way as to allow the achievement of objectives of efficiency, effectiveness, and economy.

**Art. 202**
**Entrustment of the service**
1. The Area Authority shall award the integrated urban waste management service by means of a tender regulated by the principles and community provisions, in accordance with the criteria of article 113, paragraph 7, of legislative decree no. 267 of 18 August 2000, as well as with reference to the amount of the consideration for the management carried out, taking into account the technical guarantees and the previous specific experiences of the competitors, according to modalities and terms defined by decree of the Minister of the Environment and for the Protection of the Land and Sea in respect of the regional competencies on the matter.
2. The participants in the tender must formulate, with a specific technical-illustrative report attached to the offer, proposals for the improvement of the management, for the reduction of the quantities of waste to be disposed of, and for the improvement of the environmental factors, proposing their own plan for the reduction of the considerations for the management upon the achievement of autonomously defined objectives.
3. In the evaluation of the proposals, account will be taken, in particular, of the weight that will fall on the user both in economic terms and in terms of the complexity of the operations at his charge.
4. The plants and the other patrimonial endowments owned by the local authorities already existing at the time of the assignment of the service are conferred on loan to the subjects entrusted with the same service.
5. The new plants are realized by the subject entrusted with the service or directly, pursuant to article 113, paragraph 5-ter, of legislative decree no. 267 of 18 August 2000, if it is in possession of the requirements prescribed by the current legislation, or by recourse to the procedures of law no. 109 of 11 February 1994, or according to the project financing scheme of articles 37 bis and following of the aforesaid law no. 109 of 1994.
6. The personnel who, as of 31 December 2005 or in any case eight months before the entrustment of the service, belong to the municipal administrations, to the former municipal or consortium companies and to the private companies, including cooperatives, that operate in the sector of municipal services for waste management shall be subject, without prejudice to the termination of the employment relationship, to the direct and immediate transfer to the new manager of the integrated waste service, with the safeguarding of the contractual, collective and individual conditions in place. In the case of transfer of employees of public entities and of former municipal or consortium companies and of private companies, including cooperatives, to the manager of the integrated urban waste service, the discipline of the transfer of a business branch of art. 2112 of the civil code applies, pursuant to article 31 of legislative decree no. 165 of 30 March 2001.

**Art. 203**
**Standard service contract type**
1. The relations between the Area Authorities and the subjects entrusted with the integrated service are regulated by service contracts, to be attached to the tender specifications, conforming to a standard type adopted by the regions in accordance with the criteria and guidelines of article 195, paragraph 1, letters m), n), and o).
2. The standard type provides for:
a) the legal regime chosen for the management of the service;
b) the obligation to achieve the economic-financial equilibrium of the management;
c) the duration of the entrustment, in any case not less than fifteen years;
d) the criteria for defining the economic-financial plan for the integrated management of the service;
e) the modalities of control of the correct exercise of the service;
f) the principles and general rules relating to the activities and types of control, in relation to the service levels and the consideration, the modalities, the terms and the procedures for the carrying out of the control and the characteristics of the organizational structures for this purpose;
g) the obligations of communication and transmission of data, information and documents of the manager and the relative sanctions;
h) the penalties, the sanctions in case of non-fulfillment and the conditions of resolution according to the principles of the civil code, diversified according to the type of control;
i) the level of efficiency and reliability of the service to be assured to the users, including with reference to the maintenance of the plants;
l) the faculty of redemption according to the principles of title I, chapter II, of the regulation approved by decree of the President of the Republic no. 902 of 4 October 1986;
m) the obligation of return of the works, plants and other patrimonial endowments instrumental to the provision of the service in conditions of efficiency and in a good state of conservation;
n) suitable financial and insurance guarantees;
o) the criteria and modalities of application of the tariffs determined by the local entities and their updating, including with reference to the different categories of users.
3. For the purpose of defining the contents of the standard type of paragraph 2, the Area Authorities carry out the survey of the existing works and plants, transmitting the relative data to the region. The Area Authorities also, for the same purposes, define the procedures and modalities, including on a multi-year basis, for the achievement of the objectives provided for by the fourth part of this decree and elaborate, on the basis of the criteria and guidelines established by the regions, an area plan including a program of the necessary interventions, accompanied by a financial plan and the connected management and organizational model. The financial plan indicates, in particular, the available resources, those to be found, as well as the proceeds deriving from the application of the tariff on waste for the considered period.

**Art. 204**
**Existing management**
1. The subjects who exercise the service, including in-house, at the date of entry into force of the fourth part of this decree, shall continue to manage it until the establishment and organization of the integrated waste management service by the Area Authorities.
2. In relation to the expiry of the term of paragraph 15-bis of article 113 of legislative decree no. 267 of 18 August 2000, the Area Authority shall arrange for the new entrustments, in respect of the provisions of the fourth part of this decree, within nine months from the entry into force of the same fourth part.
3. If the Area Authority does not provide for the fulfillments of paragraphs 1 and 2 within the terms established therein, the President of the Regional Council shall exercise, giving communication to the Minister of the Environment and for the Protection of the Land and Sea and to the Supervisory Authority on water resources and waste(*), the substitute powers, appointing an "ad acta" commissioner who starts the entrustment procedures within forty-five days, determining the deadlines for the individual procedural fulfillments. If the regional commissioner does not provide within the terms so established, the substitute powers preordained to the completion of the entrustment procedure fall to the Minister of the Environment and for the Protection of the Land and Sea.
4. Upon expiry, or early termination, of the managements of paragraph 1, the assets and plants of the already concessionaire companies are transferred directly to the granting local authority within the limits and according to the modalities provided for by the respective conventions of entrustment.

(*) Note: the text of art. 1, c. 5 of D.Lgs. 284/2006 is reported below:
"5. Articles 159, 160, and 207 of Legislative Decree No. 152 of April 3, 2006, are repealed and the Committee for the supervision of the use of water resources and the National Observatory on waste are reconstituted and exercise their respective functions. All references to the Supervisory Authority on water resources and waste contained in Legislative Decree No. 152 of April 3, 2006, are suppressed."

**Art. 205**
**Measures to increase separate collection**
1. In each optimal territorial area, a separate collection of urban waste must be ensured equal to the following minimum percentages of produced waste:
a) at least thirty-five percent by 31 December 2006;
b) at least forty-five percent by 31 December 2008;
c) at least sixty-five percent by 31 December 2012.
2. The wet organic fraction physically separated after collection and aimed at the overall recovery between material and energy, according to the criteria of economy, effectiveness, efficiency, and transparency of the system, contributes to the achievement of the objectives of paragraph 1.
3. In the case where at the level of the optimal territorial area the minimum objectives provided for by this article are not achieved, an additional twenty percent is applied to the tribute for the conferment of waste in landfills charged to the Area Authority, established by art. 3, paragraph 24, of law no. 549 of 28 December 1995, which shall distribute the burden among those municipalities of its territory that have not reached the percentages provided for in paragraph 1 on the basis of the separate collection quotas reached in the individual municipalities.
4. By decree of the Minister of the Environment and for the Protection of the Land and Sea in concert with the Minister of Productive Activities in agreement with the Unified Conference of article 8 of legislative decree no. 281 of 28 August 1997, the methodology and the calculation criteria of the percentages of paragraphs 1 and 2 are established, as well as the new determination of the correction coefficient of article 3, paragraph 29, of law no. 549 of 28 December 1995, in relation to the achievement of the objectives of paragraphs 1 and 2.
5. Until the issuance of the decree of paragraph 4, the implementing discipline of article 3, paragraphs from 24 to 40, of law no. 549 of 28 December 1995, continues to apply.
6. The regions by special law, and after agreement with the Minister of the Environment and for the Protection of the Land and Sea, may indicate higher recycling and recovery objectives.

**Art. 206**
**Agreements, program contracts, incentives**
1. For the purpose of the implementation of the principles and objectives established by the provisions of the fourth part of this decree in order to pursue the rationalization and simplification of the procedures, with particular reference to small enterprises, the Minister of the Environment and for the Protection of the Land and Sea, in concert with the Minister of Productive Activities, and in agreement with the regions, the autonomous provinces, and the local authorities may stipulate specific agreements and program contracts with public entities, with sector companies, public or private subjects, and category associations. The agreements and program contracts have as their object:
a) the implementation of specific sector plans for the reduction, recovery, and optimization of waste flows;
b) the experimentation, promotion, implementation, and development of productive processes and clean technologies suitable to prevent or reduce the production of waste and their hazardousness and to optimize the recovery of waste;
c) the development of innovations in productive systems to favor methods of production of goods with less polluting and in any case recyclable materials;
d) the modifications of the productive cycle and the redesign of components, machinery, and control instruments;
e) the experimentation, promotion, and production of goods designed, packaged, and placed on the market in such a way as to reduce the quantity and hazardousness of waste and the risks of pollution;
f) the experimentation, promotion, and implementation of activities of reuse, recycling, and recovery of waste;
g) the adoption of techniques for the reuse and recycling of waste within the production plant;
h) the development of appropriate techniques and control systems for the elimination of waste and the hazardous substances contained therein;
i) the use by economic and public entities of materials recovered from the separate collection of urban waste;
l) the use of systems for controlling the recovery and reduction of waste.
2. The Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory, in concert with the Minister for Production Activities, may also stipulate specific agreements and program contracts with public and private entities or with trade associations to:
a) promote and favor the use of environmental certification systems as per Regulation (EC) No. 761/2001 of the European Parliament and of the Council of 19 March 2001;
b) implement programs for the take-back of consumer goods at the end of their useful life for the purpose of reuse, recycling, and recovery of secondary raw materials, also through simplified procedures for the collection and transport of waste, which must in any case guarantee a high level of environmental protection.
3. The aforementioned agreements are stipulated in concert with the Minister for Agricultural and Forestry Policies if they concern activities related to agricultural production.
4. By decree of the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory, in concert with the Minister for Production Activities, the financial resources to be allocated, on the basis of specific financing legislative provisions, to the agreements and program contracts referred to in paragraphs 1 and 2 are identified, and the methods for their stipulation are established.
5. Pursuant to the communication 2002/412 of 17 July 2002 of the Commission of the European Communities, it is also possible to conclude environmental agreements that the Commission can use in the context of self-regulation, understood as encouragement or recognition of the same agreements, or of co-regulation, understood as a proposal to the legislator to use the agreements, when appropriate.

**Art. 207 * [ Supervisory Authority for Water Resources and Waste**
1. The Supervisory Authority for Water Resources and Waste referred to in Article 159, hereinafter referred to as the "Authority," shall ensure and supervise compliance with the principles and the pursuit of the objectives set out in Part Four of this decree, with particular reference to the efficiency, effectiveness, cost-effectiveness, and transparency of the service.
2. The Authority, in addition to the attributions identified by this article, shall take over all the other competencies already assigned by art. 26 of Legislative Decree No. 22 of 5 February 1997, to the National Waste Observatory, which shall continue to operate until the entry into force of the regulation referred to in paragraph 4 of Article 159 of this decree.
3. The structure and composition of the Authority are governed by Article 159.
4. The authority shall carry out the functions provided for in Article 160.
5. For the performance of its tasks and in order to improve, increase, and adapt to European standards, to the best available technologies and to the best environmental practices the interventions in the field of inland water protection, waste, and remediation of polluted sites, as well as to increase the efficiency of said interventions also in terms of the ability to use resources deriving from co-financing, the Authority shall make use of the Technical Secretariat referred to in art. 1, paragraph 42, of Law No. 308 of 15 December 2004, within the limits of the human, instrumental, and financial resources provided for by current legislation. It may also make use of inspection and verification bodies and offices of other public administrations.]
*NOTE: article repealed by art. 1, c. 5 of Legislative Decree 284/2006 (G.U. n. 274 of 24/11/2006). The text is reported below:
"5. Articles 159, 160, and 207 of Legislative Decree No. 152 of 3 April 2006, are repealed and the Committee for the supervision of the use of water resources and the National Waste Observatory are reconstituted and exercise their respective functions. All references to the Supervisory Authority for water resources and waste contained in Legislative Decree No. 152 of 3 April 2006, are suppressed."

**CHAPTER IV - AUTHORIZATIONS AND REGISTRATIONS**

---
**Art. 208**
**Single Authorization for New Waste Disposal and Recovery Plants**
1. Persons intending to build and operate new waste disposal or recovery plants, including hazardous ones, must submit a specific application to the competent region for the territory, attaching the final project of the plant and the technical documentation required for the realization of the project itself by the provisions in force on urban planning, environmental protection, health, safety at work, and public hygiene. If the plant is to be subject to the environmental impact assessment procedure under current legislation, the communication of the project to the competent authority for said purposes must also be attached to the application; the terms referred to in paragraphs 3 and 8 remain suspended until the acquisition of the ruling on environmental compatibility pursuant to the second part of this decree.
2. The application of the national legislation implementing Directive 96/61/EC on integrated pollution prevention and control for plants falling within its scope of application remains unaffected, with particular reference to Legislative Decree No. 59 of 18 February 2005.
3. Within thirty days of receipt of the application referred to in paragraph 1, the region identifies the person responsible for the procedure and convenes a specific services conference attended by the heads of the competent regional offices and representatives of the Area Authorities and interested local authorities. The applicant for authorization or their representative is also invited to participate, with at least twenty days' notice, in order to acquire documents, information, and clarifications. The documentation referred to in paragraph 1 is sent to the members of the services conference at least twenty days before the date set for the meeting; in the case of a majority decision, the resolution of adoption must provide an adequate and analytical motivation with respect to the dissenting opinions expressed during the conference.
4. Within ninety days of its convocation, the Services Conference shall:
a) proceed with the evaluation of the projects;
b) acquire and evaluate all elements relating to the compatibility of the project with environmental and territorial needs;
c) acquire, where provided for by current legislation, the environmental compatibility assessment;
d) transmit its conclusions with the relevant documents to the region.
5. For the technical examination of the application, the regions may use the regional agencies for environmental protection.
6. Within thirty days of receiving the conclusions of the services conference and on the basis of its findings, the region, in the case of a positive evaluation, approves the project and authorizes the construction and operation of the plant. The approval replaces for all purposes visas, opinions, authorizations, and concessions of regional, provincial, and municipal bodies, constitutes, where necessary, a variant to the urban planning instrument, and entails the declaration of public utility, urgency, and non-deferability of the works.
7. If the project concerns areas subject to constraints under Legislative Decree No. 42 of 22 January 2004, the provisions of Article 146 of said decree regarding authorization shall apply.
8. The procedure shall be concluded within one hundred and fifty days from the presentation of the application referred to in paragraph 1 with the issuance of the single authorization or with the reasoned denial thereof.
9. The terms referred to in paragraph 8 are interrupted, only once, by any requests for information made by the person responsible for the procedure to the interested party and start running again from the receipt of the elements provided by the interested party.
10. If the competent authority does not conclude the procedure for issuing the single authorization within the terms provided for in paragraph 8, the substitute power referred to in art. 5 of Legislative Decree No. 112 of 31 March 1998 shall apply.
11. The authorization identifies the conditions and prescriptions necessary to guarantee the implementation of the principles referred to in Article 178 and contains at least the following elements:
a) the types and quantities of waste to be disposed of or recovered;
b) the technical requirements with particular reference to the compatibility of the site, the equipment used, the types and maximum quantities of waste, and the conformity of the plant to the approved project;
---
c) the precautions to be taken regarding safety and environmental hygiene;
d) the location of the plant to be authorized;
e) the treatment and recovery method;
f) the prescriptions for the safety, closure, and site restoration operations of the plant;
g) the financial guarantees required, which must be provided only at the moment of the effective start of the plant's operation; to this end, the financial guarantees for the management of the landfill, including for the phase subsequent to its closure, must be provided in accordance with the provisions of art. 14 of Legislative Decree no. 36 of 13 January 2003;
h) the expiry date of the authorization, in accordance with the provisions of paragraph 12;
i) the emission limits into the atmosphere for thermal treatment processes of waste, including those accompanied by energy recovery.
12. The authorization referred to in paragraph 1 is granted for a period of ten years and is renewable. To this end, at least one hundred and eighty days before the expiry of the authorization, a specific application must be submitted to the region, which decides before the expiry of the authorization itself. In any case, the activity can be continued until the express decision, subject to the extension of the financial guarantees provided.
13. When, following subsequent checks after the start-up of the plants, these are not found to be in conformity with the authorization referred to in this article, or the conditions and prescriptions contained in the same authorization are not satisfied, the latter is suspended, after a formal warning, for a maximum period of twelve months. Once this period has elapsed without the holder having complied with the provisions of the warning notice, the authorization is revoked.
14. The control and authorization of loading, unloading, transfer, deposit, and handling operations of waste in port areas are governed by the specific provisions of Law no. 84 of 28 January 1994, and of Legislative Decree no. 182 of 24 June 2003, implementing Directive 2000/59/EC on ship-generated waste, and by other provisions in force on the matter. In the case of transboundary shipment of waste, the authorization for embarkation and disembarkation operations cannot be issued if the applicant does not demonstrate that they have fulfilled the obligations under Article 194 of this decree.
15. Mobile disposal or recovery plants, excluding mobile plants that carry out the dehydration of sludge generated by purification plants and reintroduce the water at the head of the purification process where they operate, with the exclusion of mere volume reduction and separation of extraneous fractions, are authorized, definitively, by the region where the interested party has its registered office or the foreign company owning the plant has its representative office. For the performance of individual activity campaigns on the national territory, the interested party, at least sixty days before the installation of the plant, must notify the region in whose territory the chosen site is located of the specific details relating to the activity campaign, attaching the authorization referred to in paragraph 1 and the registration in the National Register of Environmental Managers, as well as any further documentation requested. The region may adopt supplementary prescriptions or may prohibit the activity with a reasoned measure if its performance in the specific site is not compatible with the protection of the environment or public health.
16. The provisions of this article also apply to proceedings in progress at the date of entry into force of the fourth part of this decree, except for those for which the environmental impact assessment procedure has been completed.
17. Without prejudice to the obligation to keep loading and unloading registers by the subjects referred to in Article 190 and the prohibition of mixing under Article 187, the provisions of this article do not apply to temporary storage carried out in compliance with the conditions established by Article 183, paragraph 1, letter m). The same exclusion also applies when the temporary storage activity at the place of production is entrusted by the producer to another subject authorized for waste management. The conferment of waste by the producer to the person entrusted with temporary storage constitutes fulfillment of the obligations under Article 188, paragraph 3. In this case, the annotations by both the producer and the person entrusted with temporary storage must be made within twenty-four hours.
---
18. The authorization referred to in this article must be communicated, by the administration that issues it, to the Register referred to in Article 212, paragraph 1, which ensures its inclusion in a national list, accessible to the public, of the identifying elements referred to in Article 212, paragraph 23, without new or greater charges for public finance.
19. In the event of incidents affecting the authorization, these are communicated, after notice to the interested party, as well as to the same, also to the Register.
20. The procedures referred to in this article also apply to the realization of substantial variants during operation or exercise that involve modifications as a result of which the plants are no longer compliant with the authorization issued.

**Art. 209**
**Renewal of authorizations for companies with environmental certification**
1. In compliance with community regulations, during the completion of the procedures for the renewal of authorizations for the operation of a plant, or for the renewal of registration in the Register referred to in Article 212, companies that are registered under Regulation (EC) No. 761/2001 of the European Parliament and of the Council of 19 March 2001 (Emas) and operate within the Ecolabel system under Regulation No. 1980 of 17 July 2000, or are UNI-EN ISO 14001 certified, may replace such authorizations or the new registration certificate with a self-certification submitted to the competent authorities, pursuant to the Decree of the President of the Republic of 28 December 2000, No. 445.
2. The self-certification referred to in paragraph 1 must be accompanied by a certified copy of the registration certificate obtained under the regulations and parametric standards referred to in the same paragraph 1, as well as by a declaration of continuation of activities, attesting to the conformity of the company, its means, and plants with legislative and regulatory prescriptions, with an attached certification of the outcome of tests for this purpose, where provided.
3. The self-certification and the related documents, as per paragraphs 1 and 2, replace for all purposes the authorization for the continuation, or for the exercise of the activities provided for by the rules referred to in paragraph 1, and to them apply, insofar as compatible, the provisions of the Decree of the President of the Republic of 26 April 1992, No. 300. The sanctioning provisions of art. 21 of Law No. 241 of 7 August 1990 also apply.
4. The self-certification and related documents maintain the substitutive effectiveness referred to in paragraph 3 for a maximum period of one hundred and eighty days following the date of communication to the interested party of the revocation, for any reason, of the registration obtained under the regulations and parametric standards referred to in paragraph 1.
5. Without prejudice to the application of specific sanctions and unless the act constitutes a more serious crime, in the case of ascertained falsity of the statements contained in the self-certification and its related documents, art. 483 of the penal code applies to anyone who has signed the documentation referred to in paragraphs 1 and 2.
6. The application of the national legislation implementing Directive 96/61/EC on integrated pollution prevention and control for plants falling within its scope of application remains unaffected, with particular reference to Legislative Decree No. 59 of 18 February 2005.
7. The enabling titles referred to in this article must be communicated, by the administration that issues them, to the Register referred to in Article 212, paragraph 1, which ensures their insertion in a national list, accessible to the public, of the identifying elements referred to in Article 212, paragraph 23, without new or greater charges for public finance.

**Art. 210**
**Authorizations in special cases**
1. Those who, at the date of entry into force of the fourth part of this decree, have not yet obtained authorization for the management of the plant, or intend, in any case, to request a modification of the management authorization they possess, or request its renewal, shall submit an application to the competent region for the territory, which shall decide within ninety days of the request. The procedure referred to in this paragraph also applies to those who intend to start a waste recovery or disposal activity in an existing plant, previously used or adapted for other activities. If the new recovery or disposal activity is subject to an environmental impact assessment, the provisions of the second part of this decree for substantial modifications apply.
---
2. The application of the national legislation implementing Directive 96/61/EC on integrated pollution prevention and control for plants falling within its scope of application remains unaffected, with particular reference to Legislative Decree No. 59 of 18 February 2005.
3. The authorization identifies the conditions and prescriptions necessary to guarantee the implementation of the principles referred to in Article 178 and contains at least the following elements:
a) the types and quantities of waste to be disposed of or recovered;
b) the technical requirements, with particular reference to the compatibility of the site, the equipment used, the types and maximum quantities of waste, and the conformity of the plant to the new requested form of management;
c) the precautions to be taken regarding safety and environmental hygiene;
d) the location of the plant to be authorized;
e) the treatment and recovery method;
f) the emission limits into the atmosphere for thermal treatment processes of waste, also accompanied by energy recovery;
g) the prescriptions for the operations of securing, closing, and restoring the site;
h) financial guarantees, where provided for by current legislation, or other equivalent guarantees; such guarantees are in any case reduced by fifty percent for companies registered under Regulation (EC) No. 761/2001 of the European Parliament and of the Council of 19 March 2001 (Emas), and by forty percent in the case of companies possessing environmental certification according to the Uni En Iso 14001 standard;
i) the expiry date of the authorization, in accordance with the provisions of Article 208, paragraph 12.
4. When, following subsequent checks after the start-up of the plants, the construction of which has been authorized, they are not found to be compliant with the aforementioned authorization, or the conditions and prescriptions contained in the authorization for the exercise of the operations referred to in paragraph 1 are not satisfied, the latter is suspended, after a formal warning, for a maximum period of twelve months. Once this term has elapsed without the holder having complied with the provisions of the warning, the authorization itself is revoked.
5. The provisions of this article do not apply to temporary storage carried out in compliance with the conditions of Article 183, paragraph 1, letter m), which is subject only to the requirements related to the loading and unloading register under Article 190 and the prohibition of mixing under Article 187. The same exclusion also applies when the temporary storage activity at the place of production is entrusted by the producer to another subject authorized for waste management. The conferment of waste by the producer to the person entrusted with temporary storage constitutes fulfillment of the obligations under Article 188, paragraph 3. In such a case, the annotations by both the producer and the person entrusted with temporary storage must be made within twenty-four hours.
6. For waste in port areas and for embarkation and disembarkation operations in the case of transboundary shipment of waste, the provisions of Article 208, paragraph 14, apply.
7. For mobile plants, as referred to in Article 208, paragraph 15, the provisions provided therein apply.
8. If the competent authority fails to conclude the procedure for issuing the authorization within the terms provided for in paragraph 1, the substitute power under art. 5 of Legislative Decree No. 112 of 31 March 1998 applies.
9. The authorizations referred to in this article must be communicated, by the administration that issues them, to the Register referred to in Article 212, paragraph 1, which ensures their insertion in a national list, accessible to the public, of the identifying elements referred to in Article 212, paragraph 23, without new or greater charges for public finance.

**Art. 211**
**Authorization of research and experimentation plants**
1. The terms referred to in Articles 208 and 210 are reduced by half for the authorization of the construction and operation of research and experimentation plants, provided that the following conditions are met:
---
a) the management activities of the plants do not result in economic profit;
b) the plants have a capacity not exceeding 5 tons per day, unless exceptions are justified by the need to conduct tests on plants characterized by innovations, which must however be limited to the duration of such tests.
2. The duration of the authorization under paragraph 1 is two years, subject to extension which may be granted after an annual verification of the results achieved and may not in any case exceed another two years.
3. If the project or the construction of the plant have not been approved and authorized within the term specified in paragraph 1, the interested party may submit a request to the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory, who shall decide within the following sixty days in concert with the Ministers for Production Activities and for Education, University and Research. In this case, the financial guarantee is provided in favor of the State.
4. In case of risk of pathogenic agents or of unknown and dangerous substances from a health point of view, the authorization under paragraph 1 is issued by the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory, who shall decide within the following sixty days, in concert with the Ministers for Production Activities, Health, and Education, University and Research.
5. The authorization referred to in this article must be communicated, by the administration that issues it, to the Register referred to in Article 212, paragraph 1, which shall ensure its insertion in a national, publicly accessible list of the identifying elements referred to in Article 212, paragraph 23, without new or greater costs for public finance.

**Art. 212**
**National Register of Environmental Managers**
1. The National Register of Environmental Managers, hereinafter referred to as the Register, is established at the Ministry for the Environment and Protection of the Territory. It is structured into a National Committee, with its headquarters at the same Ministry, and into regional and provincial Sections, established at the Chambers of Commerce, Industry, Crafts, and Agriculture of the regional capitals and of the autonomous provinces of Trento and Bolzano. The members of the National Committee and of the Regional and Provincial Sections hold office for five years.
2. By decree of the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory, special sections of the National Committee are established for each single activity subject to registration with the Register, without new or greater charges on public finance, and their composition and competencies are determined. The National Committee of the Register has deliberative power and is composed of nineteen members with proven and documented technical-economic or legal experience in environmental matters, appointed by decree of the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory and designated respectively:
a) two by the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory, one of whom serves as President;
b) one by the Minister for Production Activities, with the function of Vice-President;
c) one by the Minister of Health;
d) one by the Minister of Economy and Finance
e) one by the Minister of Infrastructure and Transport;
f) one by the Minister of the Interior;
g) three by the regions;
h) one by the Italian Union of Chambers of Commerce, Industry, Crafts, and Agriculture;
i) six by the most representative organizations of the interested economic categories, of which two are from the organizations representing the road haulage category and two from the associations representing waste managers;
l) two by the most representative trade union organizations.
3. The Regional and Provincial Sections of the Register are established by decree of the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory and are composed of:
a) the President of the Chamber of Commerce, Industry, Crafts and Agriculture or a member of the Chamber Council designated for this purpose by the same, with the functions of President;
b) an official or manager with proven experience in environmental matters designated by the region or the autonomous province, with the functions of Vice-President;
c) an official or manager with proven experience in environmental matters, designated by the Regional Union of Provinces or by the autonomous province;
d) an expert with proven experience in environmental matters, designated by the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory;
---
e) by two experts designated by the most representative organizations of the economic categories;
f) by two experts designated by the most representative trade union organizations.
4. The functions of the National Committee and the Regional Sections of the Register are carried out, until the expiry of their mandate, respectively by the National Committee and the Regional Sections of the National Register of companies that carry out waste management, as already provided for in art. 30 of legislative decree no. 22 of 5 February 1997, integrated, without new or greater burdens on public finance, with the new components identified pursuant to, respectively, paragraph 2, letter l), and paragraph 3, letters e) and f), in compliance with the provisions of paragraph 16.
5. Registration in the Register is a prerequisite for carrying out the activities of collection and transport of non-hazardous waste produced by third parties, collection and transport of hazardous waste, remediation of sites, remediation of goods containing asbestos, trade and intermediation of waste without holding the waste itself, as well as management of third-party disposal and recovery plants and management of mobile waste disposal and recovery plants, within the limits referred to in article 208, paragraph 15. The organizations referred to in articles 221, paragraph 3, letters a) and c), 223, 224, 228, 233, 234, 235 and 236 are exempt from the obligation under this paragraph, provided they have documentary or accounting evidence that they perform similar functions, without prejudice to the documentary and accounting obligations required of the aforementioned subjects by current regulations.
6. The registration must be renewed every five years and constitutes the title for the exercise of the activities of collection, transport, trade, and intermediation of waste; for the other activities, the registration enables the management of plants whose operation has been authorized or the carrying out of activities subject to registration.
7. Companies that carry out waste collection and transport activities, companies that carry out waste intermediation and trade activities, without holding the waste, and companies that carry out the management of mobile disposal and recovery plants must provide suitable financial guarantees in favor of the State. Such guarantees are reduced by fifty percent for companies registered under Regulation (EC) No. 761/2001 of the European Parliament and of the Council of 19 March 2001 (Emas), and by forty percent in the case of companies possessing environmental certification under the Uni En Iso 14001 standard.
8. Companies that carry out the collection and transport of their own non-hazardous waste as an ordinary and regular activity, as well as companies that transport their own hazardous waste in quantities not exceeding thirty kilograms per day or thirty liters per day, are not subject to the provision of financial guarantees referred to in paragraph 7 and are registered in the National Register of Environmental Managers following a simple written request to the territorially competent section of the Register, without the request itself being subject to evaluation regarding financial capacity and technical suitability and without the obligation to appoint a technical manager. Such companies are required to pay an annual registration fee of 50 euros, which can be redetermined pursuant to art. 21 of the decree of the Minister of the Environment of 28 April 1998, no. 406.
9. Companies that carry out management activities of fixed disposal and recovery plants owned by third parties, companies that carry out site remediation and remediation of goods containing asbestos must provide suitable financial guarantees in favor of the territorially competent region, in compliance with the general criteria of article 195, paragraph 2, letter h). Such guarantees are reduced by fifty percent for companies registered under Regulation (EC) No. 761/2001 of the European Parliament and of the Council of 19 March 2001 (Emas), and by forty percent in the case of companies possessing environmental certification under the Uni En Iso 14001 standard. The guarantees referred to in this paragraph must in any case be provided based on the following distinction:
a) companies that carry out the management of fixed disposal and recovery plants owned by third parties must provide financial guarantees in favor of the region for each plant that is managed;
b) companies that carry out the remediation of sites and of goods containing asbestos must provide financial guarantees in favor of the region for each remediation intervention.
10. With a decree from the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, in concert with the Ministers of Production Activities, Infrastructure and Transport, and Economy and Finance,
---
finance, having heard the opinion of the National Committee, to be issued within ninety days from the date of entry into force of the fourth part of this decree, the attributions and organizational methods of the Register, the requirements, terms, and methods of registration, the annual registration fees, as well as the methods and amounts of the financial guarantees to be provided in favor of the State, shall be defined. Until the issuance of the aforesaid decree, the provisions of the decree of the Minister of the Environment of 28 April 1998, no. 406, shall continue to apply, where compatible. The decree referred to in this paragraph is based on the following principles:
a) identification of registration requirements, valid for all sections, in order to standardize the procedures;
b) coordination with the current legislation on road haulage, consistent with the purpose of letter a);
c) uniform treatment of the components of the Regional Sections, to ensure operational efficiency;
d) effective coverage of expenses through secretarial fees and annual registration fees.
11. By decree of the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, after consulting the State-Regions Conference, the general criteria for the definition of financial guarantees to be provided in favor of the regions are established.
12. A special Section is established at the Register, in which companies from European and non-European countries that carry out recovery operations of ferrous and non-ferrous scrap, listed in article 183, paragraph 1, letter u), for the production of secondary raw materials for the steel and metallurgical industry, are registered, in compliance with the conditions and national, community, and international technical standards identified by decree of the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory. Until the issuance of the aforesaid decree, the conditions and technical standards reported in Annex 1 to the decree of the Minister of the Environment of 5 February 1998 shall continue to apply. Registration is carried out following a communication to the register by the interested foreign company, accompanied by a certificate of conformity to these conditions and technical standards issued by the competent public authority in the country of origin. The operating procedures of the special section are established by the National Committee of the Register; pending such definition, registration is replaced for all purposes by the communication accompanied by the certificate of conformity from the competent authority.
13. Registration in the Register and the measures of suspension, revocation, forfeiture, and annulment of the registration, as well as the acceptance, revocation, and release of the financial guarantees to be provided in favor of the State are decided by the Regional Section of the Register of the region where the interested company has its legal headquarters, based on current legislation and the directives issued by the National Committee.
14. Until the issuance of the decrees referred to in this article, the provisions already in force on the date of entry into force of the fourth part of this decree shall continue to apply.
15. Interested parties may appeal to the National Committee of the Register against the decisions of the Regional Sections of the Register, within a peremptory term of thirty days from the notification of the decisions themselves.
16. The costs for the functioning of the National Committee and the Regional and Provincial Sections are covered by the revenues from secretarial fees and annual registration fees, according to the provisions, also relating to the methods of payment and use, which will be determined by decree of the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory in concert with the Minister of Economy and Finance. The integration of the National Committee and the Regional and Provincial Sections with the representatives referred to in paragraphs 2, letter l), and 3, letters e) and f), is subject to the entry into force of the aforementioned decree. Until the issuance of the said decree, the provisions of the decree of the Minister of the Environment of 20 December 1993 and the provisions of the decree of the Minister of the Environment of 13 December 1995 shall apply.
17. The regulatory discipline of cases in which, pursuant to articles 19 and 20 of law no. 241 of 7 August 1990, the exercise of a private activity can be undertaken on the basis of the declaration of the start of the activity does not apply to registration applications and acts within the competence of the Register.
18. Companies that carry out collection and transport of waste subject to simplified procedures pursuant to article 216, and actually sent for recycling and
---
recovery, and companies that transport waste indicated in the green list of Regulation (EEC) 259/93 of 1 February 1993 are not subject to the financial guarantees referred to in paragraph 8 and are registered with the Register by sending a communication of the start of activity to the competent regional or provincial Section. This communication must be renewed every five years and must be accompanied by appropriate documentation prepared pursuant to art. 13 of the ministerial decree of 28 April 1998, no. 406, as well as the deliberations of the National Committee from which the following elements result:
a) the quantity, nature, origin, and destination of the waste;
b) the correspondence of the technical characteristics and type of vehicle used to the requirements established by the Register in relation to the types of waste to be transported;
c) compliance with the conditions and possession of the subjective, technical suitability, and financial capacity requirements.
19. Within ten days of receiving the communication of the start of activity, the Regional and Provincial Sections acknowledge the registration and enter the companies referred to in paragraph 18 in special lists, communicating this to the National Committee, the territorially competent province, and the interested party.
20. Companies registered with the Register under the ordinary procedure pursuant to paragraph 5 are exempt from the obligation of communication under paragraph 18 if the performance of the activity of collection and transport of waste subject to simplified procedures pursuant to article 216 and actually sent for recycling and recovery does not involve changes in the category, class, and type of waste for which these companies are registered.
21. The provisions of art. 21 of Law no. 241 of 7 August 1990 apply to the communication referred to in paragraph 18. For companies that carry out the activities referred to in paragraph 18 following a communication accompanied by incomplete or unsuitable documentation, the provision of article 256, paragraph 1, shall apply.
22. The signatories of the agreements and program contracts provided for in Article 181 and Article 206 are registered in a special section of the Register, following a simple written request and without being subject to the financial guarantees referred to in paragraphs 8 and 9.
23. Registers of companies authorized for waste management are established at the National Committee, updated every thirty days, in which, upon request, the identifying elements of the company are inserted, which can be consulted by operators according to the procedures established by decree of the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory, in compliance with the principles of Legislative Decree no. 196 of 30 June 2003. The registers are public and, within twelve months from the entry into force of the fourth part of this decree, are made available to the public, without charge, also electronically, according to the criteria established by the aforementioned decree. The authorizing administrations shall communicate to the National Committee, immediately after issuing the authorization, the company name of the authorized company, the activity for which the authorization is issued, the waste subject to the management activity, the expiry of the authorization and subsequently report any variation of the aforementioned information that occurs during the validity of the authorization itself. In case of a delay by the Administration of more than thirty days from the issuance of the authorization, the interested company may send an authentic copy of the provision, also electronically, to the National Committee, which will arrange for its inclusion in the registers.
24. Companies that carry out non-hazardous waste disposal activities at the place of production of the waste itself pursuant to Article 215 are registered in a special register with the procedures provided for in the same article.
25. Companies that carry out waste recovery operations pursuant to Article 216 are registered in a special register with the procedures provided for in the same article.
26. For the keeping of the registers referred to in paragraphs 22, 23, 24, and 25, the interested parties are required to pay an annual registration fee, for each type of register, equal to 50 euros, which can be re-determined pursuant to art. 21 of the decree of the Minister of the Environment of 28 April 1998, no. 406. The fees referred to in paragraphs 8, 24, and 25 are paid, according to the methods referred to in paragraph 16, to the competent Regional Section of the Register, which proceeds to account for them separately and to use them entirely for the implementation of the same paragraphs.
27. The keeping of the registers referred to in paragraphs 22 and 23 shall begin from the entry into force of the decree referred to in paragraph 16.
28. The implementation of this article must not result in new or greater burdens on public finance.
---
**Art. 213**
**Integrated Environmental Authorizations**
1. The integrated environmental authorizations issued pursuant to Legislative Decree No. 59 of 18 February 2005, replace for all purposes, according to the procedures provided therein:
a) the authorizations referred to in this chapter;
b) the communication referred to in Article 216, limited to activities not falling under category 5 of Annex I of Legislative Decree No. 59 of 18 February 2005, which, if carried out under a simplified procedure, are excluded from the integrated environmental authorization, without prejudice to the possibility of subsequently using the simplified procedures provided for in Chapter V.
2. The provisions of Articles 214 and 216 of this decree apply to the transport of waste from the green list of Regulation (EEC) No. 259 of 1 February 1993, destined for the plants referred to in paragraph 1 of this article.

**CHAPTER V - SIMPLIFIED PROCEDURES**

**Art. 214**
**Determination of activities and characteristics of waste for admission to simplified procedures**
1. The simplified procedures of this Chapter must in any case guarantee a high level of environmental protection and effective controls.
2. By decrees of the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory in concert with the Ministers of Production Activities, Health and, for agricultural waste and activities that produce fertilizers, with the Minister of Agricultural and Forestry Policies, the rules are adopted for each type of activity, which establish the types and quantities of waste, and the conditions under which the disposal activities of non-hazardous waste carried out by producers at the place of production and the recovery activities referred to in Annex C to the fourth part of this decree are subject to the simplified procedures of Articles 215 and 216. With the same procedure, the aforementioned technical standards and conditions are updated.
3. Paragraph 2 can also be implemented according to the regulations in force for the program agreements referred to in Articles 181 and 206 and in compliance with community guidelines on the matter.
4. The rules and conditions referred to in paragraph 2 and the simplified procedures must ensure that the types or quantities of waste and the disposal or recovery procedures and methods are such as not to constitute a danger to human health and not to harm the environment. In particular, without prejudice to the discipline of Legislative Decree No. 133 of 11 May 2005, to access the simplified procedures, the thermal treatment and energy recovery activities must also respect the following conditions:
a) fuels from urban waste or specific special waste identified by homogeneous fractions are used;
b) the emission limits are not lower than those established for waste incineration and co-incineration plants by current legislation, with particular reference to Legislative Decree No. 133 of 11 May 2005;
c) the production of a minimum share of transformation of the calorific value of the waste into useful energy calculated on an annual basis is guaranteed;
d) the conditions, technical standards, and specific prescriptions of Articles 215, paragraph 2, and 216, paragraphs 1, 2, and 3 are respected.
5. Until the issuance of the decrees referred to in paragraph 2 regarding recovery activities, the provisions of the decrees of the Minister of the Environment of 5 February 1998 and 12 June 2002, no. 161 shall continue to apply.
6. The issuance of the rules and conditions referred to in paragraph 2 must first concern the waste indicated in the green list of Annex II of Regulation (EEC) No. 259 of 1 February 1993.
7. For the keeping of the registers referred to in Articles 215, paragraph 3, and 216, paragraph 3, and for the performance of periodic checks, the interested party is required to pay the annual registration fee to the Regional Section of the Register as per Article 212, paragraph 26.
8. The construction of plants that recover waste in compliance with the conditions,
---
prescriptions and technical standards referred to in paragraphs 2 and 3 is regulated by national and community legislation on air quality and atmospheric pollution from industrial plants. The authorization for the operation in the aforesaid plants of waste recovery operations not identified pursuant to this article remains, however, subject to the provisions of Articles 208, 209, 210 and 211.
9. To the reports, communications, and applications governed by this Chapter, the provisions relating to private activities subject to the discipline of Articles 19 and 20 of Law No. 241 of 7 August 1990 shall apply, where compatible. The provisions of art. 21 of Law No. 241 of 7 August 1990 shall also apply. Provided that the conditions, technical standards, and specific prescriptions adopted pursuant to paragraphs 1, 2, and 3 of Article 216 are respected, the exercise of waste recovery operations may be undertaken ninety days after the communication of the start of activity to the competent section of the Register referred to in Article 212.

**Art. 215**
**Self-disposal**
1. Provided that the technical standards and specific prescriptions of Article 214, paragraphs 1, 2, and 3 are respected, the non-hazardous waste disposal activities carried out at the place of production of the waste itself may be undertaken ninety days after the communication of the start of activity to the competent Regional Section of the Register, referred to in Article 212, which gives notice to the territorially competent province within ten days of receiving the communication itself.
2. The technical standards of paragraph 1 provide in particular:
a) the type, quantity, and characteristics of the waste to be disposed of;
b) the cycle of origin of the waste;
c) the conditions for the construction and operation of the plants;
d) the characteristics of the disposal plant;
e) the quality of emissions and water discharges into the environment.
3. The Regional Section of the Register records in a special register the companies that make the communication of the start of activity and within the term of paragraph 1 verifies ex officio the existence of the required prerequisites and requirements. To this end, a report must be attached to the communication of the start of activity, signed by the legal representative of the company, from which the following must result:
a) compliance with the conditions and specific technical standards of paragraph 1;
b) compliance with technical safety standards and authorization procedures provided for by current legislation.
4. Should the Regional Section of the Register ascertain the non-compliance with the technical standards and conditions of paragraph 1, the same Section proposes to the province to order, with a reasoned measure, the prohibition of the start or continuation of the activity, unless the interested party proceeds to conform said activity and its effects to the current legislation within the term and according to the prescriptions established by the administration.
5. The communication referred to in paragraph 1 must be renewed every five years and, in any case, in the event of substantial modification of the self-disposal operations.
6. The self-disposal activities of hazardous waste and the landfilling of waste remain subject to the provisions of Articles 208, 209, 210, and 211.

**Art. 216**
**Recovery operations**
1. Provided that the technical standards and specific prescriptions of Article 214, paragraphs 1, 2, and 3 are respected, the exercise of waste recovery operations may be undertaken ninety days after the communication of the start of activity to the competent Regional Section of the Register, referred to in Article 212, which gives notice to the territorially competent province within ten days of receiving the communication itself. In the cases of electrical and electronic waste as per Article 227, paragraph 1, letter a), end-of-life vehicles as per Article 227, paragraph 1, letter c), and co-incineration plants, the start of activities is subject to a preventive inspection by the competent province for the territory, to be carried out within sixty days from the presentation of the aforementioned communication.
2. The conditions and technical standards of paragraph 1, in relation to each type of
---
activity, provide in particular:
a) for non-hazardous waste:
1) the maximum quantities that can be used;
2) the origin, types, and characteristics of the waste that can be used, as well as the specific conditions under which the same activities are subject to the discipline provided by this article;
3) the necessary prescriptions to ensure that, in relation to the types or quantities of waste and recovery methods, the waste itself is recovered without danger to human health and without using processes or methods that could harm the environment;
b) for hazardous waste:
1) the maximum quantities that can be used;
2) the origin, types, and characteristics of the waste;
3) the specific conditions referring to the limit values of hazardous substances contained in the waste, to the emission limit values for each type of waste and for the type of activity and plant used, also in relation to other emissions present on site;
4) the other requirements necessary to carry out different forms of recovery;
5) the necessary prescriptions to ensure that, in relation to the type and quantities of hazardous substances contained in the waste and to the recovery methods, the waste itself is recovered without danger to human health and without using processes and methods that could harm the environment.
3. The regional section of the Register enrolls in a special register the companies that make the start of activity communication and, within the term referred to in paragraph 1, verifies ex officio the existence of the prerequisites and required requirements. To this end, a report must be attached to the start of activity communication, signed by the company's legal representative, from which the following must result:
a) compliance with the technical standards and specific conditions referred to in paragraph 1;
b) possession of the subjective requirements requested for waste management;
c) the recovery activities intended to be carried out;
d) the establishment, recovery capacity, and treatment or combustion cycle in which the waste itself is intended to be recovered, as well as the use of any mobile plants;
e) the product characteristics of the products deriving from the recovery cycles.
4. If the competent Regional Section of the Register ascertains non-compliance with the technical standards and conditions referred to in paragraph 1, the same section proposes to the province to order, with a reasoned measure, the prohibition of the start or continuation of the activity, unless the interested party proceeds to conform said activity and its effects to the current legislation within the term and according to the prescriptions established by the administration.
5. The communication referred to in paragraph 1 must be renewed every five years and in any case of substantial modification of the recovery operations.
6. The simplified procedure of this article replaces, limited to the qualitative and quantitative variations of the emissions determined by the waste identified by the technical standards of paragraph 1 which already set the emission limits in relation to the recovery activities of the same, the authorization of Article 269 in case of substantial modification of the plant.
7. The simplified provisions of this article do not apply to the recovery activities of urban waste, with the exception of:
a) activities for the recycling and recovery of secondary raw material and the production of quality compost from waste from separate collection;
b) urban waste treatment activities to obtain waste-derived fuel carried out in compliance with the technical standards of paragraph 1.
8. Without prejudice to compliance with the emission limits into the atmosphere as per Article 214, paragraph 4, letter b), and the limits of other polluting emissions established by current provisions, and without prejudice to the observance of other constraints for the protection of health and environmental profiles, within sixty days from the date of entry into force of the fourth part of this decree, the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory, in concert with the Minister for Production Activities, shall determine the methods, conditions, and measures relating to the granting of financial incentives provided for by current legislative provisions in favor of the use of waste as fuel to produce electricity, also taking into account the
---
prevalent public interest in energy recovery in urban waste power plants subject to preventive treatment operations aimed at producing fuel from waste and in compliance with the provisions of Directive 2001/77/EC of 27 September 2001 and its implementing legislative decree No. 387 of 29 December 2003.
9. With specific technical standards adopted pursuant to paragraph 1, to be published within sixty days from the date of entry into force of the fourth part of this decree, a list of non-hazardous waste most used in the production sectors is identified in observance of the following criteria:
a) diffusion of use in the manufacturing sector based on national accounting data or sector studies or specific waste management programs approved pursuant to the provisions of the fourth part of this decree;
b) use consistent with the best available techniques without danger to human health and without using processes or methods that could harm the environment;
c) use in authorized plants.
10. The waste identified pursuant to paragraph 9 is subject only to the provisions of articles 188, paragraph 3, 189, 190 and 193 as well as the related sanctioning norms contained in the fourth part of this decree. On the basis of the information in article 189, the Cadastre compiles for each province a list of the plants referred to in paragraph 9.
11. The ordinary rules for recovery and disposal apply in full to the activities referred to in this article if the waste is not destined for effective and objective recovery.
12. The conditions and technical standards relating to hazardous waste as per paragraph 1 are communicated to the Commission of the European Union three months before their entry into force.
13. The storage operations of hazardous waste identified pursuant to this article are subject to the simplified procedures of communication of start of activity only if carried out at the plant where the recycling and recovery operations provided for in points R1 to R9 of Annex C to the fourth part of this decree take place.
14. Without prejudice to the provisions of paragraph 13, the technical standards of paragraphs 1, 2, and 3 establish the plant characteristics of the storage centers for non-hazardous waste not located at the plants where the recycling and recovery operations identified in points R1 to R9 of Annex C to the fourth part of this decree are carried out, as well as the storage methods and the maximum terms within which the waste must be sent to the aforementioned operations.
15. The communications already made at the date of entry into force of the fourth part of this decree pursuant to art. 33, paragraph 1, of legislative decree no. 22 of 5 February 1997, and the consequent registrations in the registers kept by the Provinces remain valid and effective until the expiry date referred to in paragraph 5 of the same article 33.

**TITLE II - MANAGEMENT OF PACKAGING**

**Art. 217**
**Scope of application**
1. This title governs the management of packaging and packaging waste both to prevent and reduce its impact on the environment and to ensure a high level of environmental protection, and to ensure the functioning of the market, as well as to avoid discrimination against imported products, prevent the emergence of obstacles to trade and distortions of competition, and ensure the maximum possible return from packaging and packaging waste, in accordance with Directive 94/62/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 20 December 1994, as integrated and amended by Directive 2004/12/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council, of which the fourth part of this decree constitutes transposition into the internal legal order. The management systems must be open to the participation of the interested economic operators.
2. The discipline of paragraph 1 concerns the management of all packaging placed on the national market and all packaging waste resulting from its use, used or
---
produced by industries, businesses, offices, shops, services, households, for any reason, whatever the materials they are composed of. The operators of the respective packaging supply chains as a whole guarantee, according to the principles of "shared responsibility," that the environmental impact of packaging and packaging waste is reduced to a minimum throughout the entire life cycle.
3. The existing requirements regarding the quality of packaging, such as those relating to the safety, health protection, and hygiene of the packaged products, as well as the existing provisions on transport and hazardous waste, remain in force.

**Art. 218**
**Definitions**
1. For the purposes of applying this title, the following definitions apply:
a) packaging: the product, composed of materials of any nature, used to contain certain goods, from raw materials to finished products, to protect them, to allow their handling and delivery from the producer to the consumer or user, to ensure their presentation, as well as disposable items used for the same purpose;
b) sales packaging or primary packaging: packaging designed to constitute, at the point of sale, a sales unit for the final user or consumer;
c) multiple packaging or secondary packaging: packaging designed to constitute, at the point of sale, the grouping of a certain number of sales units, regardless of whether it is sold as such to the final user or consumer, or whether it serves only to facilitate the stocking of shelves at the point of sale. It can be removed from the product without altering its characteristics;
d) transport packaging or tertiary packaging: packaging designed to facilitate the handling and transport of goods, from raw materials to finished products, of a certain number of sales units or multiple packagings to prevent their handling and transport-related damage, excluding containers for road, rail, sea, and air transport;
e) reusable packaging: packaging or a component of packaging that has been conceived and designed to withstand a minimum number of trips or rotations within a reuse circuit during its life cycle.
f) packaging waste: any packaging or packaging material, falling under the definition of waste in Article 183, paragraph 1, letter a), excluding production residues;
g) management of packaging waste: the management activities referred to in Article 183, paragraph 1, letter d);
h) prevention: the reduction, in particular through the development of non-polluting products and technologies, of the quantity and harmfulness to the environment of both the materials and substances used in packaging and packaging waste, and of packaging and packaging waste at the production process stage, as well as in the marketing, distribution, use, and post-consumption management stages;
i) reuse: any operation in which packaging conceived and designed to be able to complete, during its life cycle, a minimum number of movements or rotations is refilled or reused for a use identical to that for which it was conceived, with or without the support of auxiliary products present on the market that allow the packaging itself to be filled; such reused packaging becomes packaging waste when it ceases to be reused;
l) recycling: reprocessing in a production process of packaging waste for its original function or for other purposes, including organic recycling and excluding energy recovery;
m) recovery of waste generated from packaging: operations that use packaging waste to generate secondary raw materials, products, or fuels, through mechanical, thermal, chemical, or biological treatments, including sorting, and, in particular, the operations provided for in Annex C to the fourth part of this decree;
n) energy recovery: the use of combustible packaging waste as a means to produce energy through thermal valorization with or without other waste but with heat recovery;
o) organic recycling: the aerobic (composting) or anaerobic (biomethanation) treatment, by microorganisms and under controlled conditions, of the
---
biodegradable parts of packaging waste, with the production of stabilized organic residues or biogas with energy recovery, excluding landfilling, which cannot be considered a form of organic recycling;
p) disposal: any operation aimed at permanently removing packaging or packaging waste from the economic and/or collection circuit and, in particular, the operations provided for in Annex B to the fourth part of this decree;
q) economic operators: producers, users, recoverers, recyclers, end-users, public administrations, and managers;
r) producers: suppliers of packaging materials, manufacturers, processors, and importers of empty packaging and packaging materials;
s) users: merchants, distributors, fillers, users of packaging, and importers of filled packaging;
t) public administrations and managers: the subjects and entities that provide for the organization, control, and management of the collection, transport, recovery, and disposal service for urban waste in the forms referred to in the fourth part of this decree or their concessionaires;
u) end-user: the subject who, in the exercise of their professional activity, purchases, as capital goods, packaged articles or goods;
v) consumer: the subject who, outside the exercise of a professional activity, purchases or imports for their own use packaging, packaged articles or goods;
z) voluntary agreement: a formally concluded agreement between the competent public administrations and the interested economic sectors, open to all interested parties, which regulates the means, instruments, and actions to achieve the objectives of Article 220;
aa) supply chain: an economic and productive organization that carries out its activity, from the beginning of the processing cycle to the finished packaging product, as well as carrying out recovery and recycling activities at the end of the life of the packaging itself;
bb) take-back: the operation of recovering primary packaging waste or waste otherwise conferred to the public service, as well as assimilated special waste, managed by the operators of urban hygiene services or similar;
cc) return: the operation of returning used secondary and tertiary packaging from the user or end-user, excluding the consumer, to the supplier of the goods or distributor and, backwards, along the supply logistics chain up to the producer of the packaging itself;
dd) used packaging: secondary or tertiary packaging already used and intended to be taken-back or returned.
2. The definition of packaging as per letters a) to e) of paragraph 1 is also based on the interpretative criteria indicated in art. 3 of Directive 94/62/EC, as amended by Directive 2004/12/EC and on the illustrative examples reported in Annex E to the fourth part of this decree.

**Art. 219**
**Guiding criteria for the management of packaging waste**
1. The management of packaging and packaging waste is guided by the following general principles:
a) encouragement and promotion of source prevention of the quantity and hazardousness in the manufacturing of packaging and packaging waste, especially through initiatives, including of an economic nature in accordance with the principles of Community law, aimed at promoting the development of clean technologies and reducing the production and use of packaging at the source, as well as favoring the production of reusable packaging and its concrete reuse;
b) encouragement of recycling and recovery of raw materials, development of separate collection of packaging waste, and promotion of market opportunities to encourage the use of materials obtained from recycled and recovered packaging;
c) reduction of the flow of packaging waste destined for final disposal through other forms of recovery;
d) application of prevention measures consisting of national programs or similar actions to be adopted after consulting the interested economic operators.
2. In order to ensure the accountability of economic operators in accordance with the "polluter pays" principle as well as their cooperation according to the principles of
---
"shared responsibility," the management of packaging waste is also inspired by the following principles:
a) identification of the obligations of each economic operator, ensuring that the cost of separate collection, valorization, and disposal of packaging waste is borne by producers and users in proportion to the quantities of packaging placed on the national market and that the public administration organizes the separate collection;
b) promotion of forms of cooperation between public and private entities;
