c) information to users of packaging and in particular to consumers according to the provisions of Legislative Decree No. 195 of 19 August 2005, implementing Directive 2003/4/EC on public access to environmental information;
d) encouragement of the return of used packaging and the conferment of packaging waste in separate collection by the consumer.
3. The information referred to in letter c) of paragraph 2 concerns in particular:
a) the available return, collection, and recovery systems;
b) the role of packaging users and consumers in the process of reuse, recovery, and recycling of packaging and packaging waste;
c) the meaning of the marks affixed to packaging as they appear on the market;
d) the significant elements of the management programs for packaging and packaging waste, as referred to in Article 225, paragraph 1, and the significant elements of the specific provisions contained in the regional plans pursuant to Article 225, paragraph 6.
4. In accordance with the decisions taken by the Commission of the European Union, by decree of the Minister for the Environment and the Protection of the Territory in concert with the Minister for Production Activities, the necessary technical measures for the application of the provisions of this title are adopted, with particular reference to hazardous packaging, including domestic, as well as to primary packaging of medical equipment and pharmaceutical products, small packaging, and luxury packaging. Where health aspects are involved, the aforesaid decree is adopted in concert with the Minister of Health.
5. All packaging must be appropriately labeled according to the methods established by decree of the Minister for the Environment and the Protection of the Territory in concert with the Minister for Production Activities in accordance with the decisions adopted by the Commission of the European Union, to facilitate the collection, reuse, recovery, and recycling of packaging, as well as to give correct information to consumers about the final destinations of the packaging. The aforesaid decree must also prescribe the obligation to indicate, for the purposes of identification and classification of the packaging by the interested industry, the nature of the packaging materials used, on the basis of Commission Decision 97/129/EC.

**Art. 220**
**Recovery and recycling objectives**
1. To comply with the principles of Article 219, producers and users must achieve the final recycling and recovery objectives for packaging waste in accordance with the community discipline indicated in Annex E to the fourth part of this decree.
2. To ensure control of the achievement of the recycling and recovery objectives, the National Packaging Consortium referred to in Article 224 shall annually communicate to the National Section of the Waste Cadastre, using the single declaration form as per art. 1 of Law No. 70 of 25 January 1994, the data, referring to the previous solar year, relating to the quantity of packaging for each material and for each type of packaging placed on the market, as well as, for each material, the quantity of reused packaging and recycled and recovered packaging waste from the national market. The aforesaid communications can be submitted by the subjects referred to in Article 221, paragraph 3, letters a) and c), for those who have joined the management systems provided therein and sent simultaneously to the National Packaging Consortium. Packaging waste exported from the Community pursuant to Council Regulation (EEC) No. 259 of 1 February 1993, Council Regulation (EC) No. 1420 of 29 April 1999, and Commission Regulation (EC) No. 1547 of 12 July 1999, are taken into consideration for the purposes of fulfilling the obligations and achieving the objectives of paragraph 1, only if there is suitable documentary evidence proving that the recovery and/or recycling operation was carried out in ways equivalent to
---
those provided for in this regard by Community legislation. The Authority referred to in Article 207, within one hundred and twenty days of its establishment, shall draw up a list of non-EU countries where recovery and/or recycling operations are considered equivalent to those provided for in this regard by Community legislation, also taking into account any decisions and orientations of the European Union on the matter.
3. Public administrations and managers shall encourage, for environmental reasons or in consideration of the cost-benefit ratio, energy recovery where it is preferable to recycling, provided that it does not result in a significant deviation from the national recovery and recycling objectives.
4. Public administrations and managers shall encourage, where appropriate, the use of materials obtained from recycled packaging waste for the manufacture of packaging and other products by:
a) improving market conditions for such materials;
b) revising existing standards that prevent the use of such materials.
5. Without prejudice to what is established by Article 224, paragraph 3, letter e), should the overall objectives for recycling and recovery of packaging waste as set in paragraph 1 not be achieved by the foreseen deadline, by decree of the President of the Council of Ministers, after deliberation of the Council of Ministers, on the proposal of the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory and the Minister for Production Activities, economic measures shall be applied to the different types of packaging materials, proportionate to the failure to achieve individual objectives, the revenue of which is paid into the State budget to be reallocated by decree of the Minister of Economy and Finance to a specific chapter of the Ministry for the Environment and Protection of the Territory. These sums will be used to promote prevention, separate collection, recycling, and recovery of packaging waste.
6. The objectives referred to in paragraph 1 refer to packaging waste generated on the national territory, as well as to all recycling and recovery systems net of scraps and are adopted and updated in accordance with community legislation by decree of the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory in concert with the Minister for Production Activities.
7. The Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory and the Minister for Production Activities shall notify the Commission of the European Union, pursuant to and according to the methods of articles 12, 16, and 17 of Directive 94/62/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 20 December 1994, the report on the implementation of the provisions of this title accompanied by the data acquired pursuant to paragraph 2 and the projects of the measures that are intended to be adopted within the scope of the same title.
8. The Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory and the Minister for Production Activities shall periodically provide the European Union and the other member States with data on packaging and packaging waste according to the tables and schemes adopted by the Commission of the European Union with Decision 2005/270/EC of 22 March 2005.

**Art. 221**
**Obligations of producers and users**
1. Producers and users are responsible for the correct and effective environmental management of packaging and packaging waste generated from the consumption of their own products.
2. Within the scope of the objectives referred to in Articles 205 and 220 and the Program referred to in Article 225, producers and users, upon request of the service operator and as provided for by the program agreement referred to in Article 224, paragraph 5, shall fulfill the obligation to take back primary packaging waste or waste otherwise conferred to the public service of the same nature and collected in a separate manner. To this end, to ensure the necessary connection with the separate collection activity organized by public administrations and for the other purposes indicated in Article 224, producers and users shall participate in the National Packaging Consortium, unless one of the systems referred to in paragraph 3, letters a) and c) of this article is adopted.
3. To fulfill the obligations of recycling and recovery as well as the obligations of taking back used packaging and collecting secondary and tertiary packaging waste on private surfaces, and with reference to the obligation of taking back, upon indication of the National Packaging Consortium referred to in Article 224, packaging waste conferred by the public service, producers may alternatively:
a) organize autonomously, also in an associated form, the management of their own packaging waste
---
on the entire national territory;
b) join one of the consortia referred to in Article 223;
c) certify under their own responsibility that a system for the return of their own packaging has been put in place, through suitable documentation demonstrating the self-sufficiency of the system, in compliance with the criteria and methods of paragraphs 5 and 6.
4. For the purposes of paragraph 3, users are required to deliver used secondary and tertiary packaging and secondary and tertiary packaging waste to a collection point organized by the producers and agreed upon with them. Users may, however, confer the said packaging and packaging waste to the public service within the limits deriving from the criteria determined pursuant to Article 195, paragraph 2, letter e). Until the adoption of the criteria referred to in Article 195, paragraph 2, letter e), the conferment of used secondary and tertiary packaging and secondary and tertiary packaging waste to the public service is permitted for private areas not exceeding 150 square meters in municipalities with a resident population of less than ten thousand inhabitants, or 250 square meters in municipalities with a resident population of more than ten thousand inhabitants.
5. Producers who do not join the National Packaging Consortium and a consortium under Article 223 must request from the Authority referred to in Article 207, upon providing suitable and exhaustive documentation, the recognition of the system adopted pursuant to paragraph 3, letters a) or c), within ninety days of assuming the status of producer pursuant to Article 218, paragraph 1, letter r) or from withdrawal from even just one of the aforementioned consortia; the withdrawal is effective twelve months after its communication. To this end, producers must demonstrate that they have organized the system according to criteria of efficiency, effectiveness, and cost-effectiveness, that the system is effectively and autonomously functioning, and that it is capable of achieving, within the scope of the activities carried out, the recovery and recycling objectives of Article 220. Producers must also ensure that users and end-users of packaging are informed about the methods of the adopted system. The Authority, after acquiring the necessary evaluation elements from the National Packaging Consortium, shall decide within ninety days of the request. In case of no response within the aforementioned term, the interested party shall ask the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory for the adoption of the relative substitute measures to be issued within the following sixty days. The Authority is required to present an annual summary report on all the investigations carried out. The recognitions already made under the previous legislation remain valid.
6. The producers referred to in paragraph 5 shall prepare and transmit to the National Packaging Consortium referred to in Article 224 their own Specific Prevention Program which constitutes the basis for the elaboration of the general program referred to in Article 225.
7. By September 30 of each year, the producers referred to in paragraph 5 shall present to the Authority provided for in Article 207 and to the National Packaging Consortium a specific prevention and management plan for the following solar year, which will be included in the general prevention and management program referred to in Article 225.
8. By May 31 of each year, the producers referred to in paragraph 5 are also required to present to the Authority provided for in Article 207 and to the National Packaging Consortium a report on the management for the previous solar year, including the nominal indication of the users who, up to consumption, participate in the system referred to in paragraph 3, letters a) or c), of the specific program and the results achieved in the recovery and recycling of packaging waste; the same report may highlight the problems inherent in achieving the institutional goals and any proposals for adapting the legislation.
9. The non-recognition of the system pursuant to paragraph 5, or the revocation ordered by the Authority, after notice to the interested party, if the results obtained are insufficient to achieve the objectives of Article 220 or if the obligations provided for in paragraphs 6 and 7 have been violated, entails for the producers the obligation to participate in one of the consortia referred to in Article 223 and, together with their users at every level up to consumption, in the consortium provided for in Article 224. The Authority's provisions are communicated to the interested producers and to the National Packaging Consortium. The mandatory adhesion to the consortia arranged in application of this paragraph has retroactive effect only for the purposes of paying the environmental contribution provided for by Article 224, paragraph 3, letter h), and the related default interest. To producers and users who, within ninety days of receiving the Authority's communication, do not proceed to join the consortia and pay the sums due to them, the sanctions provided for also apply.
---
by Article 261.
10. The costs are borne by the producers and users for:
a) the take-back of used packaging and the collection of secondary and tertiary packaging waste;
b) the additional charges related to the separate collection of packaging waste conferred to the public service for which the Area Authority requests the National Packaging Consortium or, on its behalf, the subjects referred to in paragraph 3 to proceed with the take-back;
c) the reuse of used packaging;
d) the recycling and recovery of packaging waste;
e) the disposal of secondary and tertiary packaging waste.
11. The return of used packaging or packaging waste, including the conferment of waste in separate collection, must not entail economic charges for the consumer.

**Art. 222**
**Separate collection and obligations of the public administration**
1. The public administration must organize adequate separate collection systems to allow the consumer to confer selected packaging waste from domestic waste and other types of packaging waste to the public service. In particular:
a) homogeneous coverage of the territory in each optimal territorial area must be guaranteed, taking into account the geographical context;
b) the management of separate collection must be carried out according to criteria that prioritize the efficiency, effectiveness, and cost-effectiveness of the service, as well as coordination with the management of other waste.
2. In the event that the Authority referred to in Article 207 ascertains that public administrations have not activated adequate separate collection systems for packaging waste, also for the achievement of the objectives of Article 205, and in particular those of recovery and recycling of Article 220, it may request the National Packaging Consortium to replace the operators of the separate collection services, also by using public or private subjects identified by the National Packaging Consortium itself through transparent and selective procedures, on a temporary and urgent basis, however for a period not exceeding twenty-four months, provided that this occurs within optimally identified areas, for the organization and/or integration of the service deemed insufficient. If the National Packaging Consortium, to achieve the recovery and recycling objectives provided for by Article 220, decides to adhere to the request, the value of the tariff applied for the collection of the corresponding urban waste will be paid to it, net of the revenues from the sale of the materials and the fee due for the take-back of the packaging waste and of the homogeneous commodity fractions. If the National Packaging Consortium does not declare its acceptance within fifteen days of the request, the Authority, in the following fifteen days, identifies, through transparent and selective procedures, a subject of proven and documented reliability and capacity to whom to entrust the separate collection and confer the packaging waste on a temporary and urgent basis, until the completion of the ordinary procedures for the awarding of the service and in any case for a period not exceeding twelve months, extendable by a further twelve months in case of objective and documented impossibility of awarding.
3. Public administrations shall encourage, where appropriate, the use of materials from recycled packaging waste for the manufacture of packaging and other products.
4. The Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory and the Minister for Production Activities shall oversee the publication of the measures and objectives subject to the information campaigns referred to in Article 224, paragraph 3, letter g).
5. The Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory, in concert with the Minister for Production Activities, shall oversee the publication of the national standards that transpose the harmonized standards referred to in Article 226, paragraph 3, and shall communicate them to the Commission of the European Union.

**Art. 223**
**Consortia**
1. In order to rationalize and organize the return of used packaging, the collection of
---
secondary and tertiary packaging waste on private surfaces and the take-back, upon indication of the National Packaging Consortium referred to in Article 224, of packaging waste conferred to the public service, as well as the recycling and recovery of packaging waste according to criteria of effectiveness, efficiency, cost-effectiveness, and transparency, producers who do not act pursuant to Article 221, paragraph 3, letters a) and c), shall establish one or more consortia for each packaging material operating throughout the national territory. Recoverers and recyclers who do not fall into the category of producers may participate in the consortia referred to in this paragraph, by agreement with the other members and jointly with them.
2. The consortia referred to in paragraph 1 have the legal personality of a private non-profit entity and are governed by a statute adopted in accordance with a model statute, drawn up by the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory in concert with the Minister for Production Activities, to be published in the Official Gazette within one hundred and eighty days from the date of entry into force of the fourth part of this decree, in accordance with the principles of this decree and, in particular, with those of efficiency, effectiveness, cost-effectiveness, and transparency, as well as of free competition in the sector's activities. The statute adopted by each consortium is transmitted within fifteen days to the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory who approves it within the following ninety days, with a provision adopted in concert with the Minister for Production Activities. If the Minister deems it not to approve the transmitted statute, for reasons of legitimacy or merit, he shall return it to the requesting consortium with his observations. Consortia already recognized under the previous legislation are required to adapt their statute in accordance with the new model statute within one hundred and twenty days of its publication in the Official Gazette. The ministerial decree approving the consortia's statute is published in the Official Gazette.
3. The consortia referred to in paragraph 1 are required to ensure the balance of their financial management. To this end, the financial means for the functioning of the aforesaid consortia derive from the contributions of the members and from the payments made by the National Packaging Consortium pursuant to Article 224, paragraph 3, letter h), according to the methods indicated in Article 224, paragraph 8, from the proceeds of the sale, in compliance with the principles of competition and correct environmental management, of the returned, collected or taken-back packaging and packaging waste, as well as from any other proceeds and contributions from members or third parties.
4. Each consortium shall develop and transmit to the National Packaging Consortium and to the Authority referred to in Article 207 its own Specific Prevention Program which constitutes the basis for the elaboration of the general program referred to in Article 225.
5. By September 30 of each year, the consortia referred to in this article shall submit to the Authority provided for in Article 207 and to the National Packaging Consortium a specific prevention and management plan for the following solar year, which will be included in the general prevention and management program.
6. By May 31 of each year, the consortia referred to in this article are also required to submit to the Authority referred to in Article 207 and to the National Packaging Consortium a report on the management for the previous year, with the nominal indication of the members, the specific program, and the results achieved in the recovery and recycling of packaging waste.

**Art. 224**
**National Packaging Consortium**
1. For the achievement of the global objectives of recovery and recycling and to ensure the necessary coordination of separate collection activities, producers and users, in compliance with the provisions of Article 221, paragraph 2, shall participate on an equal basis in the National Packaging Consortium, hereinafter referred to as CONAI, which has the legal personality of a private non-profit entity and is governed by a statute approved by decree of the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory in concert with the Minister for Production Activities.
2. Within twenty-four months* from the date of entry into force of the fourth part of this decree, CONAI shall adapt its statute to the principles contained in this decree and in particular to those of transparency, effectiveness, efficiency, and cost-effectiveness, as well as free competition in the sector's activities, pursuant to Article 221, paragraph 2. The adopted statute is transmitted within fifteen days to the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the
---
territory, who approves it in concert with the Minister for Production Activities, subject to reasoned observations to which CONAI is required to adapt in the following sixty days. Should CONAI not comply within the prescribed terms, the amendments to the statute are made by decree of the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory, in concert with the Minister for Production Activities.
3. CONAI performs the following functions:
a) defines, in agreement with the regions and the interested public administrations, the territorial areas in which to operate an integrated system that includes the collection, selection, and transport of selected materials to collection or sorting centers;
b) defines, with the public administrations belonging to the individual integrated systems referred to in letter a), the general conditions for the take-back by producers of selected waste from separate collection;
c) prepares and updates, on the basis of the specific prevention programs referred to in articles 221, paragraph 6, and 223, paragraph 4, the General Program for the prevention and management of packaging and packaging waste referred to in article 225;
d) promotes program agreements with economic operators to encourage the recycling and recovery of packaging waste and ensures their implementation;
e) ensures the necessary cooperation between the consortia referred to in article 223, the subjects referred to in article 221, paragraph 3, letters a) and c), and other economic operators, including by allocating a portion of the CONAI environmental contribution, referred to in letter h), to consortia that achieve recovery or recycling percentages higher than the minimums indicated in the General Program, for the purpose of achieving the global objectives of Annex E to the fourth part of this decree. To the same extent, the share of the contribution due to consortia that do not reach the individual recovery objectives is reduced;
f) ensures the necessary coordination between public administrations, consortia, and other economic operators;
g) organizes, in agreement with public administrations, the information campaigns deemed useful for the implementation of the General Program;
h) distributes among producers and users the additional costs for separate collection as per article 221, paragraph 10, letter b), as well as the costs for recycling and for the recovery of packaging waste conferred to the separate collection service, in proportion to the total quantity, weight, and type of packaging material placed on the national market, net of the quantities of used packaging reused in the previous year for each type of material. To this end, it determines and places on the members, with the methods identified by the statute, also based on the uses and criteria of paragraph 8, the contribution called the CONAI environmental contribution;
i) promotes coordination with the management of other waste as provided for in article 222, paragraph 1, letter b), also defining its areas of application;
l) promotes the conclusion, on a voluntary basis, of agreements between the consortia referred to in article 223 and the subjects referred to in article 221, paragraph 3, letters a) and c), with public and private subjects. Such agreements relate to the environmental management of the same type of material subject to the intervention of the consortia with regard to packaging, excluding in any case the use of the CONAI environmental contribution;
m) provides the data and information requested by the Authority referred to in article 207 and ensures compliance with the guidelines traced by it.
4. For the achievement of the multiannual objectives of recovery and recycling, any management surpluses set aside by CONAI and by the consortia referred to in article 223 in the reserves constituting their net assets do not contribute to the formation of income, provided that the prohibition of distribution, in any form, to the members and adherents of such surpluses and reserves is respected, even in the event of dissolution of the aforesaid management systems, consortia, and CONAI.
5. CONAI may stipulate a framework program agreement on a national basis with the National Association of Italian Municipalities (ANCI), with the Union of Italian Provinces (UPI), or with the Area Authorities in order to guarantee the implementation of the principle of shared management responsibility between producers, users, and public administrations. In particular, this agreement establishes:
a) the amount of the additional costs for the separate collection of packaging waste, referred to in article 221, paragraph 10, letter b), to be paid to the competent public
---
administrations, determined according to criteria of efficiency, effectiveness, cost-effectiveness and transparency of management of the same service, as well as on the basis of the tariff referred to in Article 238, from the date of its entry into force;
b) the obligations and sanctions imposed on the contracting parties;
c) the methods of collection of packaging waste in relation to the needs of recycling and recovery activities.
6. The program agreement referred to in paragraph 5 is transmitted to the Authority referred to in Article 207, which may request any modifications and integrations within the following sixty days.
7. For the purposes of allocating the costs referred to in paragraph 3, letter h), reusable packaging placed on the market upon deposit is excluded from the calculation.
8. The CONAI environmental contribution is used as a priority for the take-back of primary packaging or packaging otherwise conferred to the public service and is attributed by CONAI, on the basis of specific agreements, to the subjects referred to in Article 223 in direct proportion to the quantity and quality of recovered or recycled packaging waste and taking into account the quantity and type of packaging placed on the national market. For the further use of the contribution, CONAI stipulates, with the subjects referred to in Article 223, agreements for the organization of systems for collection, recovery, and recycling of secondary and tertiary packaging waste. CONAI and the subjects referred to in Article 223 are obliged to adopt a specific accounting system that distinguishes the share of the CONAI environmental contribution used for the take-back, recycling, and recovery of primary packaging, or otherwise conferred to the public service, from that used for secondary and tertiary packaging taken back, recycled, or recovered from private surfaces. CONAI provides the necessary financial means for the performance of its functions with the proceeds of its activities, with the contributions of the members, and with a share of the CONAI environmental contribution, determined to the extent necessary to meet the expenses deriving from the performance, in compliance with the criteria of cost containment and management efficiency, of the functions conferred upon it by this title.
9. The application of the CONAI environmental contribution excludes the subjection of the same good and the raw materials that constitute it to other contributions with environmental purposes provided for by the fourth part of this decree or in any case established in application of this decree.
10. A representative of consumers appointed by the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory and by the Minister of Production Activities participates with voting rights in the CONAI board of directors.
11. The administrators to whom operational delegations are attributed and the holders of management positions of the organizations referred to in Articles 221, paragraph 3, letters a) and c), and 223 may not participate in the CONAI board of directors.
12. In the event of non-stipulation of the agreements referred to in paragraphs 3 and 5, the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, in concert with the Minister of Production Activities, may determine by his own decree the amount of the additional costs for the separate collection of packaging waste, referred to in Article 221, paragraph 10, letter b), to be borne by producers and users, as well as the conditions and methods of take-back of the same waste by the producers. If such agreements are concluded by CONAI and one or more of the subjects referred to in Article 221, paragraph 3, letters a) and c), or one or more consortia referred to in Article 223 do not adhere to them or do not conclude with the competent public administrations, which request it, the local agreements for the take-back of packaging waste under the conditions established by the agreement concluded with CONAI, CONAI itself may substitute such subjects in the conclusion of local agreements, if necessary to achieve the recovery and recycling objectives provided for by Article 220.
13. In the event that the final recycling and recovery objectives for packaging waste indicated in the general prevention and management program for packaging as per Article 225 are exceeded at a national level, CONAI shall adopt, within its financial resources, special forms of incentive for the take-back of packaging waste in geographical areas that have not yet reached the separate collection objectives of Article 205, paragraph 1, within the maximum recycling limits provided for in Annex E to the fourth part of this decree.
*Note: the original term of one hundred and eighty days was first extended to 12 months from the entry into force of this legislative decree by art. 1, c. 6 of the Decree
---
Legislative Decree No. 284 of 8 November 2006 (G.U. No. 274 of 24/11/2006); it was then further extended, by effect of art. 5 of D.L. No. 300 of 28 December 2006 - so-called "Milleproroghe Decree" (G.U. No. 300 of 28/12/2006), as amended during conversion into Law No. 17/2007 (G.U. No. 47 of 26.2.2007, S.O. No. 48).

**Art. 225**
**General program for the prevention and management of packaging and packaging waste**
1. On the basis of the specific prevention programs referred to in Articles 221, paragraph 6, and 223, paragraph 4, CONAI annually prepares a General Program for the prevention and management of packaging and packaging waste which identifies, with reference to the individual types of packaging material, the measures to achieve the following objectives:
a) prevention of the formation of packaging waste;
b) increase in the proportion of the quantity of recyclable packaging waste with respect to the quantity of non-recyclable packaging;
c) increase in the proportion of the quantity of reusable packaging waste with respect to the quantity of non-reusable packaging;
d) improvement of the characteristics of the packaging in order to allow it to withstand more journeys or rotations under normally foreseeable conditions of use;
e) achievement of recovery and recycling objectives.
2. The General Prevention Program also determines:
a) the percentage by weight of each type of packaging waste to be recovered every five years and, within this global objective, on the basis of the same deadline, the percentage by weight to be recycled of the individual types of packaging materials, with a minimum percentage by weight for each material;
b) the intermediate recovery and recycling objectives with respect to the objectives referred to in letter a).
3. By November 30 of each year, CONAI transmits to the Authority referred to in Article 207 a specific prevention and management plan for the following solar year, which will be included in the general prevention and management program.
4. The general final report for the previous solar year is transmitted for an opinion to the Authority referred to in Article 207, by June 30 of each year. By decree of the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory and the Minister for Production Activities, in agreement with the Permanent Conference for relations between the State, the regions, and the autonomous provinces of Trento and Bolzano and ANCI, the approval and any modifications and integrations of the General Program for the prevention and management of packaging and packaging waste are provided for.
5. In the event that the General Program is not prepared, the same is drawn up in a substitute capacity by the Authority referred to in Article 207. In this case, the recovery and recycling objectives are the maximum ones provided for in Annex E to the fourth part of this decree.
6. The regional plans referred to in Article 199 are integrated with specific provisions for the management of packaging and packaging waste on the basis of the program referred to in this article.

**Art. 226**
**Prohibitions**
1. The disposal in landfills of recovered packaging and containers is prohibited, with the exception of waste resulting from selection, recycling, and recovery operations of packaging waste.
2. Without prejudice to the provisions of Article 221, paragraph 4, it is forbidden to place tertiary packaging of any nature into the normal collection circuit for urban waste. Any secondary packaging not returned to the user by the retail merchant may be conferred to the public service only in separate collection, where this has been activated within the limits provided for by Article 221, paragraph 4.
3. Only packaging that meets the European standards set by the European Committee for Standardization in accordance with the essential requirements established by art. 9 of Directive 94/62/EC of the European Parliament and of the Council of 20 December 1994 may be marketed. By decree of the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory, in concert with the Minister for Production Activities, the aforesaid standards are updated, taking into account the communication of the European Commission 2005/C44/13. Until
---
the issuance of the aforesaid decree, Annex F to the fourth part of this decree shall apply.
4. It is forbidden to place on the market packaging or packaging components, with the exception of packaging made entirely of crystal glass, with total concentration levels of lead, mercury, cadmium, and hexavalent chromium exceeding 100 parts per million (ppm) by weight. For glass packaging, Decision 2001/171/EC of 19 February 2001 applies, and for plastic packaging, Decision 1999/177/EC of 8 February 1999 applies.
5. By decree of the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory, in concert with the Minister for Production Activities, the following are determined, in accordance with the decisions of the European Union:
a) the conditions under which the concentration levels referred to in paragraph 4 do not apply to recycled materials and to production circuits localized in a closed and controlled chain;
b) the types of packaging exempt from the requirement of paragraph 4.

**TITLE III - MANAGEMENT OF PARTICULAR CATEGORIES OF WASTE**

**Art. 227**
**Electrical and electronic waste, sanitary waste, end-of-life vehicles and products containing asbestos**
1. The special, national, and community provisions relating to other types of waste remain in force, and in particular those concerning:
a) electrical and electronic waste: Directive 2000/53/EC, Directive 2002/95/EC, and Directive 2003/108/EC and related implementing Legislative Decree No. 151 of 25 July 2005. Relative to the date of entry into force of the individual provisions of the said measure, pending the entry into force of these provisions, the discipline of art. 44 of Legislative Decree No. 22 of 5 February 1997 continues to apply.
b) sanitary waste: Decree of the President of the Republic No. 254 of 15 July 2003;
c) end-of-life vehicles: Directive 2000/53/EC and Legislative Decree No. 209 of 24 June 2003, without prejudice to the distribution of charges, to be borne by economic operators, for the take-back and treatment of end-of-life vehicles in accordance with the provisions of art. 5, paragraph 4, of the said Directive 2000/53/EC;

**Art. 228**
**End-of-life tires**
1. Without prejudice to the provisions of Legislative Decree No. 209 of 24 June 2003, as well as the provisions of Articles 179 and 180 of this decree, in order to optimize the recovery of end-of-life tires and to reduce their generation also through reconstruction, tire producers and importers are obliged to provide, individually or in an associated form and with at least annual periodicity, for the management of quantities of end-of-life tires equal to those they have placed on the market and destined for sale on the national territory.
2. By decree of the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory, in agreement with the Permanent Conference for relations between the State, the regions, and the autonomous provinces of Trento and Bolzano, to be issued within one hundred and twenty days from the date of entry into force of the fourth part of this decree, the times and methods for implementing the obligation of paragraph 1 are regulated. In all phases of tire marketing, the contribution to be borne by end-users necessary, also in relation to the different types of tires, to meet the costs deriving from the obligation of paragraph 1, must be indicated on the invoice.
3. The transfer to the eventual associated operational structure, by the producers and importers of tires who are part of it, of the sums corresponding to the contribution for recovery, calculated on the quantity of tires placed on the market in the previous year, constitutes fulfillment of the obligation of paragraph 1 with exemption of the producer or importer from any related liability.
4. Producers and importers of tires who fail to comply with the obligations of paragraph 1 are subject to a pecuniary administrative sanction proportional to the gravity of the non-compliance, in any case not exceeding double the contribution collected for the period considered.
---
**Art. 229**
**Waste-derived fuel and high-quality waste-derived fuel - CDR and CDR-Q**
1. For the purposes and effects of the fourth part of this decree, waste-derived fuel (CDR), hereinafter CDR, as defined by Article 183, paragraph 1, letter r), is classified as special waste.
2. Without prejudice to the application of the discipline of this article, high-quality waste-derived fuel (CDR-Q), hereinafter CDR-Q, as defined by Article 183, paragraph 1, letter s), produced within a production process that adopts a quality management system based on the UNI-EN ISO 9001 standard and intended for effective use in co-combustion, as defined by Article 2, paragraph 1, letter g), of the decree of the Minister of Industry, Commerce and Crafts of 11 November 1999, published in the Official Gazette no. 292 of 14 December 1999, in electricity production plants and in cement plants, as specified in the decree of the President of the Council of Ministers of 8 March 2002, published in the Official Gazette no. 60 of 12 March 2002, is excluded from the scope of application of the fourth part of this decree. The Government is authorized to make the consequent amendments to the said decree of the President of the Council of Ministers of 8 March 2002.
3. The production of CDR and CDR-Q must take place in compliance with the hierarchy of waste treatment and remains in any case subject to the issuance of authorizations for the construction and operation of the plant provided for by the fourth part of this decree. In the production of CDR and CDR-Q, the use of non-hazardous special waste is permitted for a maximum percentage of fifty percent by weight. For the production and use of CDR, recourse to the simplified procedures of Articles 214 and 216 is permitted.
4. For the purposes of the construction and operation of incineration or co-incineration plants that use CDR, the specific community and national provisions on integrated environmental authorization and waste incineration apply. For the construction and operation of electricity production plants and cement plants that use CDR-Q, the specific sector regulations apply. The methods for the use of CDR-Q are defined by the said decree of the President of the Council of Ministers of 8 March 2002.
5. CDR-Q is a renewable source, pursuant to art. 2, paragraph 1, letter a), of Legislative Decree No. 387 of 29 December 2003, in proportion to the biodegradable fraction contained therein.
[6. CDR and CDR-Q benefit from the incentive scheme referred to in art. 17, paragraph 1, of Legislative Decree No. 387 of 29 December 2003].(*)
(*) Note: Paragraph repealed by art. 1, paragraph 1120 of the 2007 Finance Law (Law No. 296 of 27 December 2006, published in GU No. 299 of 27.12.2006 - S. O. n.244)

**Art. 230**
**Waste deriving from infrastructure maintenance activities**
1. The place of production of waste deriving from maintenance activities on infrastructures, carried out directly by the operator of the network infrastructure and of the plants for the provision of supplies and services of public interest or through third parties, may coincide with the headquarters of the site that manages the maintenance activity or with the local headquarters of the infrastructure operator in whose competence the section of infrastructure affected by the maintenance works falls, or with the place of concentration where the material removed from the works is transported for subsequent technical evaluation, aimed at identifying the material that is actually, directly, and objectively reusable, without being subjected to any treatment.
2. The technical evaluation of the infrastructure operator referred to in paragraph 1 is carried out no later than sixty days from the date of completion of the works. The documentation relating to the technical evaluation is kept, together with the loading and unloading registers, for five years.
3. The provisions of paragraphs 1 and 2 also apply to waste deriving from maintenance activities, carried out directly by operators providing public service or through third parties, of the means and plants that use the infrastructures referred to in paragraph 1.
---
4. Without prejudice to the provisions of article 190, paragraph 3, the loading and unloading registers relating to waste produced by the subjects and from the activities referred to in this article may be kept at the place of production of the waste as defined in paragraph 1.
5. By decree of the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, in concert with the Ministers of Production Activities, Health, and Infrastructure, the management methods for waste from sewer cleaning activities are defined, based on the criterion according to which such waste is considered produced at the headquarters or domicile of the subject carrying out the cleaning activity.

**Art. 231**
**End-of-life vehicles not regulated by Legislative Decree no. 209 of 24 June 2003**
1. The owner of a motor vehicle or a trailer, excluding those regulated by Legislative Decree no. 209 of 24 June 2002, who intends to proceed with its demolition must deliver it to a collection center for securing, demolition, recovery of materials, and scrapping, authorized pursuant to articles 208, 209, and 210. Such collection centers may also receive waste consisting of parts of motor vehicles.
2. The owner of a motor vehicle or a trailer as per paragraph 1 intended for demolition may also deliver it to the dealerships or branches of the manufacturing houses for subsequent delivery to the centers as per paragraph 1, if they intend to trade in the said vehicle or trailer to purchase another one.
3. Motor vehicles or trailers as per paragraph 1 found by public bodies or not claimed by their owners and those acquired by occupation pursuant to articles 927, 928, 929, and 923 of the civil code are delivered to the collection centers as per paragraph 1 in the cases and with the procedures determined by decree of the Minister of the Interior, in concert with the Ministers of Economy and Finance, Environment and Protection of the Territory, and Infrastructure and Transport. Until the adoption of such decree, the decree of 22 October 1999, no. 460, shall apply.
4. The collection centers or the dealerships or branches of the manufacturing houses shall issue to the owner of the vehicle or trailer delivered for demolition a certificate from which must result the date of delivery, the details of the center's authorization, the owner's personal details, and the vehicle's identification details, as well as the assumption, by the manager of the center itself or by the dealership or the owner of the branch, of the commitment to directly handle the procedures for cancellation from the Public Automobile Register (PRA).
5. The cancellation from the PRA of vehicles and trailers sent for demolition occurs exclusively under the care of the owner of the collection center or the dealership or the owner of the branch without agency fees charged to the owner of the vehicle or trailer. To this end, within ninety days of the delivery of the vehicle or trailer by the owner, the manager of the collection center, the dealership, or the owner of the branch must communicate the delivery for demolition of the vehicle and deliver the certificate of ownership, the registration card, and the license plates to the competent PRA office which proceeds pursuant to and for the effects of art. 103, paragraph 1, of legislative decree no. 285 of 30 April 1992.
6. Possession of the certificate referred to in paragraph 4 frees the owner of the vehicle from civil, criminal, and administrative liability connected with the ownership of the same.
7. The managers of the collection centers, the dealerships, and the owners of the branches of the manufacturing houses as per paragraphs 1 and 2 cannot alienate, dismantle, or destroy motor vehicles and trailers to be sent for dismantling and subsequent reduction into scrap without first having fulfilled the tasks as per paragraph 5.
8. The details of the receipt of the report and delivery of the license plates and documents to the competent offices must be noted in the special register of entry and exit of vehicles to be kept according to the rules of the regulation of legislative decree no. 285 of 30 April 1992.
9. The same obligations as in paragraphs 7 and 8 are subject to the managers of collection centers or other places of custody of vehicles removed pursuant to art. 159 of legislative decree no. 285 of 30 April 1992, in the case of demolition of the vehicle pursuant to art. 215, paragraph 4 of the aforesaid legislative decree no. 285 of 30 April 1992.
10. The trade of spare parts recovered from the demolition of motor vehicles or trailers is permitted, with the exclusion of those related to the
---
safety of vehicles. The origin of the spare parts put on sale must result from the invoices and receipts issued to the customer.
11. The spare parts related to the safety of vehicles are sold only to businesses engaged in auto repair as per Law No. 122 of 5 February 1992, and, to be used, each auto repair company is required to certify their suitability and functionality.
12. The use of spare parts as per paragraphs 10 and 11 by companies engaged in auto repair activities must result from the invoices issued to the customer.
13. Within six months from the date of entry into force of the fourth part of this decree, the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, in concert with the Ministers of Production Activities and of Infrastructure and Transport, shall issue the technical standards relating to the characteristics of the demolition plants, the securing operations, and the identification of spare parts related to safety as per paragraph 11. Until the adoption of such decree, the requirements relating to the collection centers and the methods of treatment of vehicles as per Annex I of legislative decree no. 209 of 24 June 2003 shall apply.

**Art. 232**
**Waste produced by ships and cargo residues**
1. The national discipline relating to waste produced by ships and cargo residues is contained in legislative decree no. 182 of 24 June 2003.
2. Plants that receive bilge water already subjected to preliminary treatment in plants authorized under current legislation may access the simplified procedures of decree no. 269 of 17 November 2005, provided that the raw materials and the products obtained have the characteristics indicated at point 6.6.4 of Annex 3 of the aforesaid decree, as amended by paragraph 3 of this article.
3. At points 2.4 of Annex 1 and 6.6.4 of Annex 3 of decree no. 269 of 17 November 2005, the conjunction: "and" is replaced by the disjunction: "or".

**Art. 233**
**National consortia for the collection and treatment of used vegetable and animal oils and fats**
1. In order to rationalize and organize the management of used vegetable and animal oils and fats, all operators in the supply chain shall form one or more consortia. The management systems adopted must comply with the principles of Article 237.
2. The consortia referred to in paragraph 1 have the legal personality of a private non-profit entity and are governed by a statute adopted in accordance with a model statute drawn up by the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory in concert with the Minister of Production Activities, to be published in the Official Gazette within one hundred and eighty days from the date of entry into force of the fourth part of this decree, in accordance with the principles of this decree and, in particular, with those of efficiency, effectiveness, cost-effectiveness and transparency, as well as of free competition in the sector's activities. The statute adopted by each consortium is transmitted within fifteen days to the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory who approves it in the following ninety days, with his provision adopted in concert with the Minister of Production Activities. If the Minister deems it not to approve the transmitted statute, for reasons of legitimacy or merit, he shall return it to the requesting consortium with the relative observations. Consortia already recognized under the previous legislation are required to adapt their statute in accordance with the new model statute within one hundred and twenty days of its publication in the Official Gazette. The ministerial decree of approval of the consortia's statute is published in the Official Gazette.
3. The consortia shall carry out the following tasks throughout the national territory:
a) ensure the collection from the subjects referred to in paragraph 12, transport, storage, treatment, and recovery of used vegetable and animal oils and fats;
b) ensure, in compliance with the provisions in force on pollution, the disposal of collected used vegetable and animal oils and fats for which regeneration is not possible or convenient;
c) promote the conduct of market surveys and sector studies in order to improve, economically and technically, the cycle of collection, transport, storage, treatment, and recovery of used vegetable and animal oils and fats.
---
4. The resolutions of the consortium bodies, adopted in relation to the purposes of the fourth part of this decree and in accordance with the statute, are binding on all participating companies.
5. The following participate in the consortia:
a) companies that produce, import, or hold used vegetable and animal oils and fats;
b) companies that recycle and recover used vegetable and animal oils and fats;
c) companies that carry out the collection, transport, and storage of used vegetable and animal oils and fats;
d) eventually, companies that have paid recycling contributions pursuant to paragraph 10, letter d).
6. The participation quotas in the consortia are determined based on the ratio between the production capacity of each member and the total production capacity developed by all members belonging to the same category.
7. The determination and assignment of quotas is the responsibility of the board of directors of the consortia, which provides for it annually according to the provisions of the statute.
8. In case of incapacity or impossibility to fulfill, through the same member companies, the obligations of collection, transport, storage, treatment, and reuse of used vegetable and animal oils and fats established by the fourth part of this decree, the consortium may, within the limits and in the ways determined by the statute, stipulate contracts with public and private companies for the fulfillment of the same obligations.
9. Operators who do not proceed pursuant to paragraph 1 may, within one hundred and twenty days from the publication in the Official Gazette of the model Statute pursuant to paragraph 2, organize autonomously, also in an associated form, the management of used vegetable and animal oils and fats throughout the national territory. In such a case, the operators themselves must request from the Authority referred to in Article 207, upon transmission of suitable documentation, the recognition of the system adopted. To this end, the aforesaid operators must demonstrate that they have organized the system according to criteria of efficiency, effectiveness, and cost-effectiveness, that the system is effectively and autonomously functioning, and that it is capable of achieving, within the scope of the activities carried out, the objectives set by this article. The operators must also ensure that users and end-users are informed about the methods of the system adopted. The Authority, after acquiring the necessary evaluation elements, shall decide within ninety days of the request. In case of no response within the above-indicated term, the interested party requests the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory to adopt the relative substitute measures to be issued within the following sixty days. The Authority is required to present an annual summary report on all the investigations carried out.
10. The consortia are required to ensure the balance of their own financial management. The financial resources of the consortia consist of:
a) the proceeds of the activities carried out by the consortia;
b) the asset management of the consortium fund;
c) the consortium quotas;
d) any recycling contributions borne by producers and importers of vegetable and animal oils and fats for food use intended for the domestic market and falling within the consortium's purposes as per paragraph 1, determined annually by decree of the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, in concert with the Minister of Production Activities, in order to guarantee the management balance of the consortia.
11. The consortia referred to in paragraph 1 and the subjects of paragraph 9 shall annually transmit to the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory and to the Minister of Production Activities the preliminary and final budgets within sixty days of their approval; moreover, by May 31 of each year, these subjects shall present to the same Ministers a technical report on the overall activity developed by them and by their individual members in the previous solar year.
12. Ninety days after the date of publication in the Official Gazette of the decree approving the Statute as per paragraph 2, anyone who, by reason of their professional activity, holds used vegetable and animal oils and fats is obliged to confer them to the consortia directly or by delivery to subjects appointed by the consortia, without prejudice to the provisions of paragraph 9. The obligation of conferment does not exclude the holder's right to cede used vegetable and animal oils and fats to companies of another State
---
member of the European Community.
13. Anyone who, by reason of their professional activity and pending conferment to the consortia, holds used animal and vegetable oils and fats is obliged to store them in a suitable container compliant with the provisions in force on disposal.
14. The community and national provisions in force regarding products, by-products, and waste of animal origin remain unaffected.
15. Legal entities belonging to the categories referred to in paragraph 5 that are established or in any case begin one of the activities proper to the same categories after the entry into force of the fourth part of this decree shall join one of the consortia referred to in paragraph 1 or adopt the system referred to in paragraph 9, within sixty days from the date of establishment or the start of their own activity. It is also permitted for the subjects referred to in paragraph 5, who are members of one of the consortia referred to in paragraph 1, to establish new consortia or adopt the system referred to in the same paragraph 9, after the term referred to in paragraph 9, after at least two years from the date of adhesion to the previous consortium and without prejudice to the obligation to pay the contributions accrued during the period.

**Art. 234**
**National consortia for the recycling of waste from polyethylene goods**
1. In order to rationalize, organize, and manage the collection and treatment of waste from polyethylene goods destined for disposal, one or more consortia are established for the recycling of waste from polyethylene goods, excluding packaging as per Article 218, paragraph 1, letters a), b), c), d), e) and dd), goods, and related waste, as per Articles 227, paragraph 1, letters a), b) and c), and 231, as well as, insofar as they are considered durable goods, materials and pipes in polyethylene intended for construction, sewerage, and the transport of gas and water. The management systems adopted must comply with the principles of Article 237.
2. By decree of the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, in concert with the Minister of Production Activities, to be issued within sixty days from the date of entry into force of the fourth part of this decree, the types of polyethylene goods referred to in paragraph 1 are identified.
3. The consortia referred to in paragraph 1 have the legal personality of a private non-profit entity and are governed by a statute adopted in accordance with a model statute drawn up by the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory in concert with the Minister of Production Activities, to be published in the Official Gazette within one hundred and eighty days from the date of entry into force of the fourth part of this decree, in accordance with the principles of this decree and, in particular, those of efficiency, effectiveness, cost-effectiveness, and transparency, as well as of free competition in the sector's activities. The statute adopted by each consortium is transmitted within fifteen days to the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory who approves it in the following ninety days, with his provision adopted in concert with the Minister of Production Activities. If the Minister deems it not to approve the transmitted statute, for reasons of legitimacy or merit, he shall return it to the requesting consortium with the relative observations. Consortia already recognized under the previous legislation are required to adapt their statute in accordance with the new model statute within one hundred and twenty days of its publication in the Official Gazette. The ministerial decree of approval of the consortia's statute is published in the Official Gazette.
4. The following participate in the consortia:
a) producers and importers of polyethylene goods;
b) users and distributors of polyethylene goods;
c) recyclers and recoverers of waste from polyethylene goods.
5. Producers and importers of polyethylene raw materials for the production of polyethylene goods and companies that carry out the collection, transport, and storage of polyethylene goods may participate in the consortia as associate members. The methods of participation are defined within the statute referred to in paragraph 3.
6. Legal entities belonging to the categories referred to in paragraph 4 that are established or in any case begin one of the activities proper to the same categories after the entry into force of the fourth part of this decree shall join one of the consortia referred to in paragraph 1 or adopt the system referred to in paragraph 7, within sixty days from the date of establishment or the start of their own activity. It is also permitted for the subjects referred to in paragraphs 4 and 5, who are members of one of the consortia referred to in paragraph 1, the
---
establishment, subsequent to the term of paragraph 7, of new consortia or the adoption of the system of the same paragraph 7, after at least a biennium from the date of adhesion to the previous consortium and without prejudice to the obligation to pay the contributions accrued during the period.
7. Operators who do not provide for under paragraph 1 may within one hundred and twenty days from the publication in the Official Gazette of the model Statute pursuant to paragraph 2:
a) organize autonomously, also in an associated form, the management of waste from polyethylene goods throughout the national territory;
b) implement a system for the return of polyethylene goods at the end of their life cycle to send them for recycling and recovery activities.
In the aforementioned cases, the operators themselves must request from the Authority referred to in Article 207, upon transmission of suitable documentation, the recognition of the system adopted. To this end, the aforementioned operators must demonstrate that they have organized the system according to criteria of efficiency, effectiveness, and cost-effectiveness, that the system is effectively and autonomously functioning, and that it is capable of achieving, within the scope of the activities carried out, the objectives set by this article. The operators must also ensure that users and end-users are informed about the methods of the system adopted. The Authority, after acquiring the necessary evaluation elements, shall decide within ninety days of the request. In case of no response within the above-indicated term, the interested party asks the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory to adopt the relative substitute measures to be issued within the following sixty days. The Authority presents an annual summary report on all the investigations conducted.
8. The consortia of paragraph 1 have as their primary objective to favor the take-back of polyethylene-based goods at the end of their life cycle to send them for recycling and recovery activities. To this end, the consortia carry out the following tasks throughout the national territory:
a) they promote the management of the flow of polyethylene-based goods;
b) they ensure the collection, recycling, and other forms of recovery of waste from polyethylene goods;
c) they promote the valorization of non-reusable polyethylene fractions;
d) they promote user information, aimed at reducing the consumption of materials and favoring correct forms of collection and disposal;
e) they ensure the elimination of waste from polyethylene goods in cases where recycling is not possible or economically convenient, in compliance with anti-pollution provisions.
9. In the distribution of the members' products, the consortia may resort to forms of security deposit.
10. The consortia are required to guarantee the balance of their own financial management. The financial means for the functioning of the consortia are constituted by:
a) the proceeds from the activities carried out by the consortia;
b) the contributions of the participating subjects;
c) the asset management of the consortium fund;
d) the possible percentage recycling contribution as per paragraph 13.
11. The deliberations of the consortia's bodies, adopted in relation to the purposes of the fourth part of this decree and according to the statute, are binding on all participating subjects.
12. The consortia of paragraph 1 and the subjects of paragraph 7 shall annually transmit to the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory and to the Minister of Production Activities the preliminary and final budget within sixty days of their approval. The consortia of paragraph 1 and the subjects of paragraph 7, by May 31 of each year, shall present a technical report on the overall activity developed by themselves and by their individual members in the preceding solar year.
13. The Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory in concert with the Minister of Production Activities shall determine every two years with his own decree the minimum recycling objectives and, in case of failure to achieve the aforementioned objectives, may establish a percentage recycling contribution to be applied to the net amount of invoices issued by the producing and importing companies of polyethylene goods for the domestic market. The Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory in concert with the Minister of Production Activities shall determine the recycling objectives valid for the first two-year period within ninety days from the date of entry into force of the fourth part of this decree.
14. Ninety days after the publication in the official gazette of the decree approving the statute referred to in paragraph 3, anyone who, by reason of their activity, holds waste from polyethylene goods is obliged to deliver it to one of the recognized consortia, either directly or by delivery to subjects appointed by the consortia themselves, without prejudice to the provisions of paragraph 7. The obligation to deliver does not exclude the right for the holder to sell the waste from polyethylene goods to companies of another Member State of the European Community.

**Art. 235**
**National consortia for the collection and treatment of spent lead-acid batteries and lead-containing waste**
1. In order to rationalize and organize the management of spent lead-acid batteries and lead-containing waste, all companies referred to in art. 9-quinquies of decree-law no. 397 of 9 September 1988, converted, with amendments, by law no. 475 of 9 November 1988, as amended by paragraph 15 of this article, which do not adhere to the consortium referred to in the same article 9-quinquies, shall establish one or more consortia, which must adopt management systems compliant with the principles of article 237.
2. The consortia referred to in paragraph 1 have the legal personality of a private non-profit entity and, except as provided for in paragraph 17, are governed by a statute adopted in accordance with a model statute drawn up by the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory in concert with the Minister for Production Activities, to be published in the Official Gazette within one hundred and eighty days from the date of entry into force of the fourth part of this decree, in accordance with the principles of this decree and, in particular, with those of efficiency, effectiveness, cost-effectiveness, and transparency, as well as of free competition in the sector's activities. The statute adopted by each consortium is transmitted within fifteen days to the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory who approves it within the following ninety days. If the Minister deems it not to approve the transmitted statute, for reasons of legitimacy or merit, he shall return it to the requesting consortium with the relative observations. The ministerial decree approving the consortia's statute is published in the Official Gazette.
3. The consortia referred to in paragraph 1, at the same time as the communication referred to in article 189, paragraph 3, must transmit a copy of the same communication to the consortium referred to in art. 9-quinquies, of decree-law no. 397 of 9 September 1988, converted, with amendments, by law no. 475 of 9 November 1988, as amended by this decree. The same sanctions provided for the failure to communicate under the aforementioned article 189, paragraph 3, apply to the violation of this obligation.
4. The consortia shall carry out the following tasks throughout the national territory:
a) ensure the management of spent lead-acid batteries and lead-containing waste;
b) transfer the spent lead-acid batteries and lead-containing waste to the companies that carry out their recovery;
c) ensure their disposal, if recovery is not possible or economically convenient, in compliance with anti-pollution provisions;
d) promote market research and technical-scientific research actions for the technological improvement of the production, recovery, and disposal cycle;
e) promote the raising of public and consumer awareness on the issues of collection and disposal of spent lead-acid batteries and lead-containing waste.
5. The following shall participate in the consortia referred to in paragraph 1:
a) companies that carry out the recycling of spent lead-acid batteries and lead-containing waste through the production of refined secondary lead or lead alloy;
b) companies that carry out the manufacturing or importation of lead-acid batteries;
c) companies that carry out the collection of spent lead-acid batteries and lead-containing waste;
d) companies that carry out the replacement and sale of lead-acid batteries.
6. The participation quotas of the members are determined annually according to the criteria set out in paragraph 3-bis of art. 9-quinquies, of decree-law no. 397 of 9 September 1988, converted, with amendments, by law no. 475 of 9 November 1988, as amended by paragraph 16 of this article.
7. The resolutions of the bodies of the consortia referred to in this article, adopted in relation to the purposes of the fourth part of this decree and in accordance with the statute, are mandatory for all participating companies.

---
8. Legal entities belonging to the categories referred to in paragraph 5 that are established or in any case begin one of the activities proper to the same categories after the entry into force of the fourth part of this decree shall join one of the consortia referred to in paragraph 1 within sixty days from the date of establishment or the start of their activity. It is also permitted for the same subjects, who are members of one of the consortia referred to in paragraph 1, to establish new consortia, after at least a biennium from the date of adhesion to the previous consortium and without prejudice to the obligation to pay the contributions accrued during the period.
9. Ninety days after the date of publication in the Official Gazette of the ministerial decree approving the statute referred to in paragraph 2, anyone holding spent lead-acid batteries or lead-containing waste is obliged to deliver them to the consortia, either directly or by delivery to subjects appointed by the consortium or authorized, according to current legislation, to carry out the management activities of such waste, without prejudice to the provisions of paragraph 3. The obligation of delivery does not exclude the right of the holder to sell the spent batteries and lead-containing waste to companies of another Member State of the European Community.
10. In order to ensure the financial means for the consortia to carry out their tasks, a sales surcharge on batteries is established in relation to the weight content of lead, to be applied by the producers and importers of the batteries themselves, with the right of recourse against the purchasers in all subsequent stages of commercialization. The producers and importers shall pay the proceeds of the surcharge directly to the consortia.
11. By decree of the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory, in concert with the Minister for Production Activities, the following are determined: the surcharge referred to in paragraph 10, the percentage of costs to be covered by the application of this surcharge.
12. Anyone who, by reason of their activity and pending delivery pursuant to paragraph 9, holds spent batteries is obliged to store the batteries themselves in a suitable container compliant with the provisions in force on waste disposal.
13. The consortia referred to in paragraph 1 shall annually transmit to the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory and to the Minister for Production Activities the preliminary and final budgets within sixty days of their approval; furthermore, by May 31 of each year, these subjects shall present to the same Ministers a technical report on the overall activity developed by them and by their individual members in the preceding solar year.
14. To paragraph 2 of art. 9-quinquies of decree-law no. 397 of 9 September 1988, converted, with amendments, by law no. 475 of 9 November 1988, the following letter is added: [....].
15. Paragraph 3 of article 9-quinquies, of decree-law no. 397 of 9 September 1988, converted, with amendments, by law no. 475 of 9 November 1988, is replaced by the following: [....].
16. After paragraph 3 of article 9-quinquies, of decree-law no. 397 of 9 September 1988, converted, with amendments, by law no. 475 of 9 November 1988, the following is inserted: [....].
17. Within twenty-four months* from the date of entry into force of the fourth part of this decree, the Consortium referred to in Article 9-quinquies of decree-law no. 397 of 9 September 1988, converted, with amendments, by law no. 475 of 9 November 1988, shall adapt its statute to the principles contained in this decree and in particular to those of transparency, effectiveness, efficiency, and cost-effectiveness, as well as of free competition in the sector's activities. The adopted statute is transmitted within fifteen days to the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory who approves it, in concert with the Minister for Production Activities, in the following ninety days, subject to reasoned observations to which the said Consortium is required to adapt in the following sixty days. Should the said Consortium not comply within the prescribed terms, the amendments to the statute shall be made by decree of the Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory, in concert with the Minister for Production Activities.
18. For the achievement of the multiannual objectives of recovery and recycling, any management surpluses set aside by the consortia in the reserves constituting the net assets shall not contribute to the formation of income, provided that the prohibition of distribution, in any form, to the members of such surpluses and reserves is respected, even in the event of dissolution of the same consortia.
*Note: the original term of one hundred and eighty days was thus extended by effect of art. 5 of D.L. no. 300 of 28 December 2006 - so-called "Milleproroghe Decree" (G.U. no. 300 of 28/12/2006), as amended during conversion into L. no. 17/2007 (G.U. no. 47 of 26.2.2007, S.O. no. 48).

**Art. 236**
**National consortia for the management, collection, and treatment of used mineral oils**
1. In order to rationalize and organize the management of used mineral oils, to be obligatorily sent for regeneration aimed at the production of base oils, the companies referred to in paragraph 4 are required to participate in the fulfillment of the tasks provided for in paragraph 12 by joining the consortium referred to in art. 11 of legislative decree no. 95 of 27 January 1992, or one of the consortia to be established pursuant to paragraph 2. The consortia shall adopt management systems compliant with the principles of article 237.
2. Within twenty-four months* from the date of entry into force of the fourth part of this decree, the consortium referred to in article 11 of legislative decree no. 95 of 27 January 1992, shall adapt its statute to the principles contained in this decree and in particular to those of transparency, effectiveness, efficiency, and cost-effectiveness, as well as of free competition in the sector's activities. The adopted statute is transmitted within fifteen days to the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory who approves it in concert with the Minister of Production Activities in the following ninety days, subject to reasoned observations to which the Consortium is required to adapt in the following sixty days. Should the Consortium not comply within the prescribed terms, the amendments to the statute shall be made by decree of the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, in concert with the Minister of Production Activities.
