The Consortia referred to in paragraph 1 have the legal personality of a private non-profit entity and those other than the Consortium referred to in article 11 of legislative decree no. 95 of 27 January 1992, are governed by a statute adopted in accordance with a model statute drawn up by the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory in concert with the Minister of Production Activities, to be published in the Official Gazette within one hundred and eighty days from the date of entry into force of the fourth part of this decree, in accordance with the principles of this decree and, in particular, with those of efficiency, effectiveness, cost-effectiveness, and transparency, as well as of free competition in the sector's activities. The statute adopted by each consortium is transmitted within fifteen days to the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory who approves it in the following ninety days, with his provision adopted in concert with the Minister of Production Activities. If the Minister deems it not to approve the transmitted statute, for reasons of legitimacy or merit, he shall return it to the requesting Consortium with the relative observations. The ministerial decree of approval of the Consortia's statute is published in the Official Gazette.
3. The Consortia referred to in paragraph 2 must transmit to the Consortium referred to in art. 11 of legislative decree no. 95 of 27 January 1992, at the same time as the communication referred to in article 189, paragraph 3, a copy of the same communication. The sanctions of article 258 for the failure to communicate as per article 189, paragraph 3, apply to the violation of this obligation. Companies that eliminate used mineral oils through co-combustion and are duly authorized for this purpose and the other consortia referred to in this article are required to provide the Consortium referred to in article 11 of legislative decree no. 95 of 27 January 1992, with the technical data referred to in paragraph 12, letter h), so that this consortium annually communicates all the data collected on a national basis to the Ministries that exercise control, accompanied by an illustrative report.
4. All companies that:
a) produce virgin base oils;
b) produce base oils from the regeneration process;
c) place lubricating oils on the consumer market.
5. The participation quotas in the Consortia are determined annually in proportion to the quantities of finished lubricating oils that each member places on the consumer market in the preceding year, with respect to the total lubricants placed on the consumer market in the same year by all participants in the Consortium itself.
6. The deliberations of the organs of the Consortia, adopted in relation to the purposes of the part
---
fourth part of this decree and in accordance with the statute, are binding for all consortium members. The representation in the elective bodies of the Consortia is attributed to the extent of eighty percent to the companies that produce virgin base oils and place finished lubricating oils on the market, and to the extent of twenty percent to the companies that produce and place on the consumer market regenerated lubricating oils.
7. The consortia annually determine, with reference to the costs incurred in the year net of revenues for the fulfillment of the obligations of this article, the contribution per kilogram of lubricating oil that will be placed on the market in the following year. For the purposes of the fourth part of this decree, base and finished lubricating oils are considered placed on the market at the time of payment of the consumption tax.
8. The participating companies are required to pay the consortium the contributions owed by each of them according to the methods and terms established pursuant to paragraph 9.
9. The methods and terms for the assessment, collection, and payment of the contributions referred to in paragraph 8 are established by decree of the Minister of Economy and Finance, in concert with the Ministers of the Environment and Protection of the Territory and of Production Activities, to be published in the Official Gazette within one month of the approval of the consortium's statute.
10. The consortia referred to in paragraph 1 shall annually transmit to the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory and to the Minister of Production Activities the preliminary and final budgets within sixty days of their approval. The Consortia referred to in paragraph 1, by May 31 of each year, shall present to the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory and to the Minister of Production Activities a technical report on the overall activity developed by them and by their individual members in the preceding solar year.
11. The statute referred to in paragraph 2 provides, in particular, for the organs of the consortia and the relative methods of appointment.
12. The consortia shall carry out the following tasks for the entire national territory:
a) promote public awareness on collection issues;
b) ensure and incentivize the collection of used oils by taking them back from holders and authorized companies;
c) directly carry out the collection of used oils from holders who request it in areas where collection is difficult or economically disadvantageous;
d) select the collected used oils for their correct elimination through regeneration, combustion, or disposal;
e) transfer the collected used oils:
1) as a priority, for regeneration aimed at the production of base oils;
2) in case of effective technical, economic, and organizational constraints, for combustion or co-incineration;
3) in the absence of the requirements for use as per the preceding numbers, for disposal through incineration or permanent storage;
f) pursue and incentivize the study, experimentation, and implementation of new treatment processes and alternative uses;
g) operate in compliance with the principles of competition, free circulation of goods, cost-effectiveness of management, as well as the protection of health and the environment from any pollution of the air, water, and soil;
h) record and process all technical data relating to the collection and elimination of used oils and communicate them annually to the Consortium referred to in art. 11 of legislative decree no. 95 of 27 January 1992, so that this Consortium transmits them to the Ministries that exercise control, accompanied by an illustrative report;
i) guarantee to regenerators, within the limits of the regenerable used oils collected and the plant's production, the quantities of used oils requested at a fair price and, in any case, not exceeding the direct cost of collection;
l) ensure the disposal of used oils in cases where recovery is not possible or economically convenient, in compliance with the provisions against pollution.
13. The consortia may carry out their functions either directly or through mandates conferred on companies for specific and limited sectors of activity or specific territorial areas. The activity of the agents is carried out under the direction and responsibility of the consortia themselves.
14. Legal entities belonging to the categories referred to in paragraph 4 that are established or in any case begin one of the activities proper to the same categories after
---
the entry into force of the fourth part of this decree shall join one of the Consortia referred to in paragraph 1, within sixty days from the date of establishment or the start of their own activity. It is also permitted for the aforementioned subjects, members of one of the Consortia referred to in paragraph 1, to establish new Consortia, after at least a biennium from the date of adhesion to the preceding Consortium and without prejudice to the obligation to pay the contributions accrued during the period.
15. Ninety days after the date of publication in the Official Gazette of the decree approving the statute referred to in paragraph 2, anyone who holds used mineral oils is obliged to deliver them to the Consortia referred to in paragraph 1, directly or by delivery to subjects appointed by the consortium or authorized, according to current legislation, to carry out the management activities of such waste. The obligation of delivery does not exclude the right of the holder to sell the used mineral oils to companies of another Member State of the European Community.
16. For the achievement of the multiannual objectives of recovery and recycling, any management surpluses set aside by the consortia referred to in paragraph 1 in the reserves constituting the net assets shall not contribute to the formation of income, provided that the prohibition of distribution, in any form, to the members of such surpluses and reserves is respected, even in the event of dissolution of the same consortia.
*Note: the original term of one hundred and eighty days was thus extended by effect of art. 5 of D.L. no. 300 of 28 December 2006 - so-called "Milleproroghe Decree" (G.U. no. 300 of 28/12/2006), as amended during conversion into L. no. 17/2007 (G.U. no. 47 of 26.2.2007, S.O. no. 48).

**Art. 237**
**Guiding criteria for management systems**
1. The management systems adopted must, in any case, be open to the participation of all operators and designed in such a way as to ensure the principle of transparency, non-discrimination, non-distortion of competition, free circulation, as well as the maximum possible efficiency.

**TITLE IV - TARIFF FOR THE MANAGEMENT OF URBAN WASTE**

**Art. 238**
**Tariff for the management of urban waste**
1. Anyone who possesses or holds for any reason premises, or open areas for private or public use not constituting an accessory or appurtenance of the same premises, for any use, existing in the areas of the municipal territory, that produce urban waste, is required to pay a tariff. The tariff constitutes the consideration for the performance of the service of collection, recovery, and disposal of solid urban waste and also includes the costs indicated in art. 15 of legislative decree no. 36 of 13 January 2003. The tariff referred to in art. 49 of legislative decree no. 22 of 5 February 1997, is abolished from the date of entry into force of this article, except as provided for in paragraph 11.
2. The tariff for waste management is commensurate with the average ordinary quantities and qualities of waste produced per unit of surface area, in relation to the uses and type of activity carried out, on the basis of parameters, determined with the regulation referred to in paragraph 6, which also take into account income indices articulated by user groups and territories.
3. The tariff is determined, within three months from the date of entry into force of the decree referred to in paragraph 6, by the Area Authorities and is applied and collected by the subjects entrusted with the integrated management service on the basis of the criteria established by the regulation referred to in paragraph 6. The determination of the tariff also provides for the coverage of ancillary costs related to the management of urban waste such as, for example, the costs of street sweeping. If these costs are covered by the tariff, this must be highlighted in the financial plans and in the budgets of the subjects entrusted with the service.
4. The tariff is composed of a quota determined in relation to the essential components of the cost of the service, referring in particular to investments for the works and their related amortizations, as well as a quota related to the quantities of waste conferred to the service
---
provided and to the extent of the management costs, so that the full coverage of investment and operating costs is ensured.
5. The Area Authorities approve and present to the Authority referred to in Article 207 the financial plan and the related report prepared by the subject entrusted with the integrated management service. Within four years from the date of entry into force of the regulation referred to in paragraph 6, full coverage of the costs must be gradually ensured.
6. The Minister for the Environment and Protection of the Territory, in concert with the Minister for Production Activities, after consulting the State-Regions Conference and the autonomous provinces of Trento and Bolzano, the qualified representatives of the economic and social interests present in the Economic and Social Council for Environmental Policies (CESPA), and the interested parties, shall regulate, with a specific regulation to be issued within six months from the date of entry into force of the fourth part of this decree and in compliance with the provisions of this article, the general criteria on the basis of which the cost components are defined and the tariff is determined, also with reference to the reductions referred to in paragraph 7, while ensuring in any case the absence of charges for the interested authorities.
7. In determining the tariff, reductions may be provided for domestic users and for those used for seasonal or non-continuous use, duly documented and ascertained, which also take into account income indices articulated by user groups and territories. In this case, the financial plan must indicate the resources necessary to ensure the full coverage of the reduced revenues resulting from the reductions, according to the criteria established by the regulation referred to in paragraph 6.
8. The regulation referred to in paragraph 6 also takes into account the objectives of improving the productivity and quality of the service provided and the programmed inflation rate.
9. The possible modulation of the tariff takes into account the investments made by the municipalities or by the managers that are useful for the organization of the service.
10. A reduction coefficient is applied to the tariff, proportional to the quantities of assimilated waste that the producer demonstrates to have sent for recovery through a certificate issued by the subject who carries out the recovery activity of the waste itself.
11. Until the issuance of the regulation referred to in paragraph 6 and until the completion of the requirements for the application of the tariff, the existing regulatory disciplines shall continue to apply.
12. The voluntary and coercive collection of the tariff can be carried out according to the provisions of the decree of the President of the Republic of 29 September 1973, no. 602, through an agreement with the Revenue Agency.

**TITLE V - REMEDIATION OF CONTAMINATED SITES**

**Art. 239**
**Principles and scope of application**
1. This title regulates remediation and environmental restoration interventions for contaminated sites and defines the procedures, criteria, and methods for carrying out the necessary operations for the elimination of the sources of pollution and in any case for the reduction of the concentrations of polluting substances, in harmony with community principles and norms, with particular reference to the "polluter pays" principle.
2. Without prejudice to the discipline set forth in title 1 of the fourth part of this decree, the provisions of this title do not apply to:
a) the abandonment of waste regulated by the fourth part of this decree. In this case, if, following the removal, initiation of recovery, disposal of abandoned or uncontrollably deposited waste, an exceedance of the attention values is ascertained, it will be necessary to proceed with the characterization of the area for the purpose of any remediation and environmental restoration interventions to be carried out pursuant to this title;
b) remediation interventions governed by special laws, except within the limits of what is expressly referred to by the same or what is not regulated by them.
3. Remediation and environmental restoration interventions for areas characterized by diffuse pollution are regulated by the regions with specific plans, without prejudice to the competencies and procedures provided for sites subject to remediation of national interest and in any case in compliance with the general criteria of this title.

---
**Art. 240**
**Definitions**
1. For the purposes of applying this title, the following definitions apply:
a) site: the area or portion of territory, geographically defined and determined, understood in its various environmental matrices (soil, subsoil, and groundwater) and including any building and plant structures present;
b) contamination threshold concentrations (CSC): the contamination levels of the environmental matrices that constitute values above which the characterization of the site and the site-specific risk analysis are necessary, as identified in Annex 5 to the fourth part of this decree. In the case where the potentially contaminated site is located in an area affected by anthropic or natural phenomena that have caused the exceedance of one or more contamination threshold concentrations, these latter are assumed to be equal to the existing background value for all the exceeded parameters;
c) risk threshold concentrations (CSR): the contamination levels of the environmental matrices, to be determined on a case-by-case basis by applying the site-specific risk analysis procedure according to the principles illustrated in Annex 1 to the fourth part of this decree and on the basis of the results of the characterization plan, the exceedance of which requires safety measures and remediation. The concentration levels so defined constitute the acceptability levels for the site;
d) potentially contaminated site: a site in which one or more concentration values of the pollutants found in the environmental matrices are higher than the contamination threshold concentration values (CSC), pending the completion of the characterization and site-specific health and environmental risk analysis operations, which will allow the determination of the state of contamination or not on the basis of the risk threshold concentrations (CSR);
e) contaminated site: a site in which the risk threshold concentration values (CSR), determined by applying the risk analysis procedure referred to in Annex 1 to the fourth part of this decree on the basis of the results of the characterization plan, are exceeded;
f) uncontaminated site: a site in which the contamination found in the environmental matrices is lower than the contamination threshold concentration values (CSC) or, if higher, is still lower than the risk threshold concentration values (CSR) determined following the site-specific health and environmental risk analysis;
g) site with ongoing activity: a site in which productive activities, both industrial and commercial, are in operation, as well as the appurtenant areas and those used for ancillary economic activities, including maintenance and heritage protection activities for the purpose of the subsequent resumption of activities;
h) decommissioned site: a site where productive activities have ceased;
i) prevention measures: initiatives to counter an event, an act, or an omission that has created an imminent threat to health or the environment, understood as a sufficiently probable risk that damage to health or the environment will occur in the near future, in order to prevent or minimize the occurrence of such a threat;
l) remediation measures: any action or combination of actions, including mitigation or provisional measures aimed at repairing, restoring, or replacing damaged natural resources and/or services, or providing an equivalent alternative to such resources or services;
m) emergency safety measures: any immediate or short-term intervention, to be implemented in the emergency conditions referred to in letter t) in case of sudden contamination events of any nature, aimed at containing the diffusion of the primary sources of contamination, preventing their contact with other matrices present on the site, and removing them, pending any further remediation or operational or permanent safety measures;
n) operational safety measures: the set of interventions carried out in a site with ongoing activity aimed at ensuring an adequate level of safety for people and the environment, pending further permanent safety or remediation interventions to be carried out upon cessation of the activity. They also include the contamination containment interventions to be implemented on a transitional basis until the execution of the remediation or permanent safety measures, in order to prevent the diffusion of contamination.
---
within the same matrix or between different matrices. In such cases, suitable monitoring and control plans must be prepared to verify the effectiveness of the adopted solutions;
o) permanent safety measures: the set of interventions aimed at definitively isolating the sources of pollution with respect to the surrounding environmental matrices and ensuring a high and definitive level of safety for people and the environment. In such cases, monitoring and control plans and land use limitations with respect to the provisions of urban planning instruments must be provided;
p) remediation: the set of interventions aimed at eliminating the sources of pollution and polluting substances or reducing their concentrations present in the soil, subsoil, and groundwater to a level equal to or lower than the risk threshold concentration values (CSR);
q) restoration and environmental restoration: the interventions of environmental and landscape redevelopment, also constituting a complement to the remediation or permanent safety interventions, which allow the site to be recovered for its effective and definitive usability for the intended use in conformity with urban planning instruments;
r) diffuse pollution: the contamination or chemical, physical, or biological alterations of the environmental matrices determined by diffuse sources and not attributable to a single origin;
s) site-specific health and environmental risk analysis: site-specific analysis of the effects on human health deriving from prolonged exposure to the action of substances present in the contaminated environmental matrices, conducted with the criteria indicated in Annex 1 to the fourth part of this decree;
t) emergency conditions: events upon the occurrence of which the execution of emergency interventions is necessary, such as:
1) current or potential concentrations of vapors in confined spaces close to explosive levels or suitable to cause acute harmful effects to health;
2) presence of significant quantities of product in a separate phase on the ground or in surface water courses or in the aquifer;
3) contamination of wells for drinking water or agricultural purposes;
4) risk of fires and explosions.

**Art. 241**
**Regulation of agricultural areas**
1. The regulation relating to remediation, environmental restoration, and emergency, operational, and permanent safety measures for areas intended for agricultural production and livestock farming is adopted by decree of the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory in concert with the Ministers of Production Activities, Health, and Agricultural and Forestry Policies.

**Art. 242**
**Operational and administrative procedures**
1. Upon the occurrence of an event that is potentially capable of contaminating the site, the person responsible for the pollution shall, within twenty-four hours, implement the necessary prevention measures and immediately communicate this to the authorities pursuant to and with the methods of Article 304, paragraph 2. The same procedure applies to the identification of historical contaminations that may still pose risks of aggravating the contamination situation.
2. The person responsible for the pollution, having implemented the necessary prevention measures, shall carry out, in the areas affected by the contamination, a preliminary investigation on the parameters subject to the pollution and, if it is ascertained that the contamination threshold concentration (CSC) level has not been exceeded, shall proceed to restore the contaminated area, giving notice thereof, with a specific self-certification, to the municipality and the competent province for the territory within forty-eight hours of the communication. The self-certification concludes the notification procedure of this article, without prejudice to the verification and control activities by the competent authority to be carried out in the following fifteen days. In the case where the pollution is not attributable to a single event, the parameters to be evaluated must be identified on a case-by-case basis, based on the history of the site and the activities carried out there over time.
3. If the preliminary investigation referred to in paragraph 2 ascertains that the CSC has been exceeded even for a single parameter, the person responsible for the pollution shall immediately notify the municipality and the competent provinces for the territory, with a description of the prevention and emergency safety measures adopted. In the following thirty days, he shall present to the aforementioned administrations, as well as to the territorially competent region, the characterization plan with the requirements of Annex 2 to the fourth part of this decree. Within the following thirty days, the region, having convened the services conference, shall authorize the characterization plan with any supplementary prescriptions. The regional authorization constitutes consent for all works connected to the characterization, replacing any other authorization, concession, concert, agreement, or permit from the public administration.
4. On the basis of the results of the characterization, the site-specific risk analysis procedure is applied to the site for the determination of the risk threshold concentrations (CSR). The criteria for the application of the risk analysis procedure are reported in Annex 1 to the fourth part of this decree. Within six months of the approval of the characterization plan, the responsible party shall present the results of the risk analysis to the region. The services conference convened by the region, following the investigation carried out in contradiction with the responsible party, who is given at least twenty days' notice, shall approve the risk analysis document within sixty days of its receipt. This document is sent to the members of the services conference at least twenty days before the date set for the conference and, in the case of a majority decision, the resolution of adoption shall provide an adequate and analytical motivation with respect to the dissenting opinions expressed during the conference.
5. If the results of the risk analysis procedure show that the concentration of contaminants present on the site is lower than the risk threshold concentrations, the services conference, with the approval of the risk analysis document, shall declare the procedure positively concluded. In this case, the services conference may prescribe the implementation of a monitoring program on the site regarding the stabilization of the situation found in relation to the results of the risk analysis and the current land use destination. To this end, the responsible party, within sixty days of the above approval, shall send to the competent province and region for the territory a monitoring plan in which are identified:
a) the parameters to be monitored;
b) the frequency and duration of the monitoring.
6. The region, after consulting the province, shall approve the monitoring plan within thirty days of its receipt. The aforementioned term may be suspended once only, if the competent authority deems it necessary to request, by means of an adequately motivated act, documentary integrations or further details of the project, assigning a suitable term for compliance. In this case, the term for approval shall run from the receipt of the integrated project. At the end of the monitoring period, the responsible party shall communicate this to the region and the province, sending a technical report summarizing the results of the monitoring carried out. In the case where the monitoring activities reveal the exceedance of one or more of the risk threshold concentrations, the responsible party must initiate the remediation procedure of paragraph 7.
7. If the results of the risk analysis procedure show that the concentration of contaminants present on the site is higher than the risk threshold concentration values (CSR), the responsible party shall submit to the region, within the following six months from the approval of the risk analysis document, the operational project for the remediation or safety measures, operational or permanent, and, where necessary, the further measures of repair and environmental restoration, in order to minimize and reduce to an acceptable level the risk deriving from the state of contamination present on the site. The region, having acquired the opinion of the municipality and the interested province through a specific services conference and having heard the responsible party, shall approve the project, with any prescriptions and integrations, within sixty days of its receipt. This term may be suspended once only, if the region deems it necessary to request, by means of an adequately motivated act, documentary integrations or further details of the project, assigning a suitable term for compliance. In this hypothesis, the term for the approval of the project shall run from the presentation of the integrated project. For the sole purposes of the realization and operation of the plants and equipment necessary for the implementation of the operational project and for the time strictly necessary for its implementation
---
the same, the regional authorization referred to in this paragraph replaces for all purposes the authorizations, concessions, agreements, understandings, no-objections, opinions, and consents provided for by current legislation, including, in particular, those relating to the environmental impact assessment, where necessary, the management of excavated soil and rocks within the area subject to the intervention, and the discharge of water drawn from the aquifers. The authorization also constitutes a zoning variance and entails a declaration of public utility, urgency, and non-deferability of the works. With the project approval measure, the execution times are also established, also indicating any necessary prescriptions for the execution of the works, and the amount of the financial guarantees is fixed, in an amount not exceeding fifty percent of the estimated cost of the intervention, which must be provided in favor of the region for the correct execution and completion of the same interventions.
8. The criteria for the selection and execution of remediation and environmental restoration interventions, operational or permanent safety measures, as well as for the identification of the best available techniques at sustainable costs (B.A.T.N.E.E.C. - Best Available Technology Not Entailing Excessive Costs) pursuant to community regulations are reported in Annex 3 to the fourth part of this decree.
9. The operational safety measures, concerning contaminated sites with ongoing activities, guarantee adequate health and environmental safety and prevent further propagation of contaminants. The operational safety measure projects are accompanied by accurate plans for monitoring the effectiveness of the adopted measures and indicate whether, upon cessation of the activity, a remediation or permanent safety measure intervention will be necessary.
10. In the case of characterization, remediation, safety measures, and environmental restoration of sites with ongoing activities, the region, without prejudice to the obligation to guarantee the protection of public health and the environment, when approving the project, shall ensure that the said interventions are structured in such a way as to be compatible with the continuation of the activity.
11. In the case of events that occurred before the entry into force of the fourth part of this decree, which subsequently manifest themselves on that date in the absence of immediate risk to the environment and public health, the interested party shall communicate to the competent region, province, and municipality the existence of a potential contamination together with the site characterization plan, in order to determine its extent and extension with reference to the parameters indicated in the CSCs and shall apply the procedures of paragraphs 4 and following.
12. The investigations and preliminary activities are carried out by the province, which avails itself of the technical competence of the Regional Agency for Environmental Protection and coordinates with the other administrations.
13. The procedure for approving the characterization and the remediation project takes place in a Services Conference convened by the region and constituted by the administrations ordinarily competent to issue the permits, authorizations, and concessions for the realization of the interventions included in the plan and in the project. The relative documentation is sent to the members of the services conference at least twenty days before the date set for the discussion and, in the case of a majority decision, the resolution of adoption must provide an adequate and analytical motivation with respect to the dissenting opinions expressed during the conference. The province is responsible for issuing the certification of completed remediation. If the province does not proceed to issue this certification within thirty days of receiving the resolution of adoption, the region shall issue it.

**Art. 243**
**Groundwater**
1. Groundwater drawn from underground aquifers, within the scope of remediation interventions of a site, may be discharged, directly or after being used in production cycles in operation on the site itself, in compliance with the emission limits for industrial wastewater into surface waters as per this decree.
2. In derogation of the provisions of paragraph 1 of Article 104, for the sole purposes of aquifer remediation, the reinjection, after treatment, of groundwater into the same geological unit from which it was extracted is permitted, indicating the type of treatment, the qualitative-quantitative characteristics of the reinjected water, the methods of reinjection, and the safety measures for the portion of the aquifer affected by the extraction/reinjection system. The reinjected water must have undergone a treatment aimed at the remediation of the aquifer and must not contain other discharged waters or other dangerous substances, different in quality and quantity, from those present in the drawn water.

**Art. 244**
**Ordinances**
1. Public administrations that, in the exercise of their functions, identify sites in which they ascertain that the contamination levels are higher than the contamination threshold values, shall communicate this to the competent region, province, and municipality.
2. The province, having received the communication referred to in paragraph 1, after having carried out the appropriate investigations aimed at identifying the person responsible for the exceedance event and having heard the municipality, shall, with a motivated ordinance, order the person responsible for the potential contamination to proceed pursuant to this title.
3. The ordinance referred to in paragraph 2 is in any case also notified to the owner of the site for the purposes and effects of Article 253.
4. If the person responsible is not identifiable or does not take action and neither the owner of the site nor any other interested party takes action, the interventions that become necessary pursuant to the provisions of this title are adopted by the competent administration in accordance with the provisions of Article 250.

**Art. 245**
**Obligations of intervention and notification by parties not responsible for the potential contamination**
1. The procedures for safety, remediation, and environmental restoration interventions regulated by this title may in any case be initiated on the initiative of the interested non-responsible parties.
2. Without prejudice to the obligations of the person responsible for the potential contamination under Article 242, the owner or manager of the area who detects the exceedance or the concrete and current danger of exceedance of the contamination threshold concentrations (CSC) must notify the competent region, province, and municipality and implement the prevention measures according to the procedure of Article 242. The province, once it has received the above communications, shall take action, after consulting the municipality, to identify the responsible party in order to proceed with the remediation interventions. The owner or another interested party is in any case granted the right to intervene voluntarily at any time to carry out the necessary interventions within the site under their ownership or availability.
3. If the interested parties proceed pursuant to paragraphs 1 and 2 within six months from the date of entry into force of the fourth part of this decree, or have already done so previously, the start of the obligation for the remediation of sites for events prior to the entry into force of the fourth part of this decree will be defined by the competent region for the territory on the basis of the dangerousness of the site, determined in general by the regional plan for the remediation of polluted areas or by its possible excerpts, without prejudice in any case to the right of the interested parties to proceed with the interventions before the aforementioned deadline.

**Art. 246**
**Program agreements**
1. The subjects obliged to carry out the interventions of this title and the other interested subjects have the right to define the methods and timing for the execution of the interventions through specific program agreements stipulated, within six months of the approval of the risk analysis document of Article 242, with the competent administrations pursuant to the provisions of this title.
2. In the case where there are subjects who intend or are required to provide for the simultaneous remediation of a plurality of sites affecting the territory of multiple regions, the times and methods of intervention can be defined with specific program agreements stipulated, within twelve months of the approval of the risk analysis document of Article 242, with the interested regions.
3. In the case where there are subjects who intend or are required to provide for the simultaneous remediation of a plurality of sites located throughout the national territory or there are multiple subjects interested in the remediation of the same site of national interest, the times and methods of intervention can be defined with a program agreement to be stipulated, within eighteen months of the approval of the risk analysis document of Article 242, with the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory in concert with the Ministers of Health and of Production Activities, in agreement with the State-Regions Conference.

**Art. 247**
**Sites subject to seizure**
1. In the case where the polluted site is subject to seizure, the judicial authority that ordered it may authorize access to the site for the execution of safety, remediation, and environmental restoration interventions of the areas, also for the purpose of preventing the further propagation of pollutants and the consequent worsening of the environmental situation.

**Art. 248**
**Controls**
1. The documentation relating to the site characterization plan and the operational project, including the repair measures, the monitoring to be carried out, the use limitations, and the prescriptions possibly dictated pursuant to Article 242, paragraph 4, is transmitted to the competent province and Regional Agency for Environmental Protection for the purpose of carrying out controls on the conformity of the interventions with the approved projects.
2. The completion of remediation, permanent safety, and operational safety interventions, as well as their conformity to the approved project, are ascertained by the province through a specific certification based on a technical report prepared by the territorially competent Regional Agency for Environmental Protection.
3. The certification referred to in paragraph 2 constitutes a title for the release of the financial guarantees referred to in Article 242, paragraph 7.

**Art. 249**
**Small-scale contaminated areas**
1. For small-scale contaminated areas, the simplified intervention procedures reported in Annex 4 to the fourth part of this decree apply.

**Art. 250**
**Remediation by the administration**
1. If the parties responsible for the contamination do not directly carry out the fulfillments ordered by this title, or if they are not identifiable and neither the owner of the site nor other interested parties take action, the procedures and interventions of Article 242 are carried out ex officio by the territorially competent municipality and, if this does not take action, by the region, according to the order of priority established by the regional plan for the remediation of polluted areas, also using other public or private entities, identified as a result of specific public evidence procedures. In order to advance the sums for the aforementioned interventions, the regions may establish specific funds within their budget availability.

**Art. 251**
**Census and registry of sites to be remediated**
1. The regions, on the basis of the criteria defined by the Agency for the Protection of the Environment and for Technical Services (APAT), shall prepare the registry of sites subject to remediation procedures, which must contain:
a) the list of sites subject to remediation and environmental restoration intervention as well as the interventions carried out in the same sites;
b) the identification of the subjects to whom the remediation is incumbent;
c) the public entities that the region intends to use, in case of non-compliance by the obliged subjects, for the purposes of ex officio execution, without prejudice to the awarding of the necessary works through public tender or recourse to the procedures of Article 242.
2. If, following the site-specific risk analysis, an exceedance of the risk concentrations is ascertained, this situation is reported in the urban destination certificate, as well as in the cartography and in the implementation technical standards of the general urban planning instrument of the municipality and is communicated to the competent State Revenue Office.
3. To ensure the effectiveness of the collection and transfer of data and information, the Agency for the Protection of the Environment and for Technical Services (APAT) shall define, in collaboration with the regions and the regional agencies for environmental protection, the contents and structure of the essential data of the registry, as well as the methods for their transposition into information systems connected to the network of the National Environmental Information System (SINA).

**Art. 252**
**Sites of national interest**
1. Sites of national interest, for the purposes of remediation, are identifiable in relation to the characteristics of the site, the quantities and hazardousness of the pollutants present, the significance of the impact on the surrounding environment in terms of health and ecological risk, as well as prejudice to cultural and environmental assets.
2. The identification of sites of national interest is provided for by decree of the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, in agreement with the interested regions, according to the following principles and guiding criteria:
a) remediation interventions must concern areas and territories, including water bodies, of particular environmental value;
b) remediation must concern areas and territories protected pursuant to legislative decree no. 42 of 22 January 2004;
c) the health and environmental risk deriving from the detected exceedance of the risk threshold concentrations must be particularly high due to the density of the population or the extension of the interested area;
d) the socio-economic impact caused by the pollution of the area must be significant;
e) the contamination must constitute a risk to assets of historical and cultural interest of national relevance;
f) the interventions to be implemented must concern sites included in the territory of more than one region.
3. For the purposes of the perimeter definition of the site, the municipalities, provinces, regions, and other local authorities are consulted, ensuring the participation of the responsible parties as well as the owners of the areas to be remediated, if different from the responsible parties.
4. The remediation procedure of Article 242 for sites of national interest is attributed to the competence of the Ministry of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, after consulting the Ministry of Production Activities. The Ministry of the Environment and Protection of the Territory may also avail itself of the Agency for the Protection of the Environment and for Technical Services (APAT), the regional agencies for the protection of the environment of the interested regions, and the National Institute of Health, as well as other qualified public or private entities.
5. In the case where the responsible party does not take action or is not identifiable, or the owner of the contaminated site or another interested party does not take action, the interventions are prepared by the Ministry of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, availing itself of the Agency for the Protection of the Environment and for Technical Services (APAT), the National Institute of Health, and E.N.E.A., as well as other qualified public or private entities.
6. The authorization of the project and the related interventions replaces for all purposes the authorizations, concessions, agreements, understandings, no-objections, opinions, and consents provided for by current legislation, including, among others, those relating to the realization and operation of the plants and equipment necessary for their implementation. The authorization also constitutes a zoning variance and entails a declaration of public utility, urgency, and non-deferability of the works.
7. If the project provides for the realization of works subject to an environmental impact assessment procedure, the approval of the remediation project also includes such an assessment.
8. Pending the finalization of the authorization measure of the preceding paragraphs, once the technical investigation is completed, the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory may authorize, on a provisional basis, upon request of the interested party, where there are urgent reasons and without prejudice to the acquisition of the positive opinion of the environmental compatibility assessment, where provided, the start of the works for the realization of the related remediation interventions, according to the positively evaluated project, with any prescriptions, from the services conference convened by the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory. The provisional authorization produces the effects of Article 242, paragraph 7.
9. The area affected by the remediation of the former Strillale landfill (Grosseto) is qualified as a site of national interest under current legislation. A subsequent decree of the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory will provide for the perimeter definition of the aforementioned area.

**Art. 253**
**Real burdens and special privileges**
1. The interventions of this title constitute a real burden on the contaminated sites if carried out ex officio by the competent authority pursuant to Article 250. The real burden is registered following the approval of the remediation project and must be indicated in the urban destination certificate.
2. The costs incurred for the interventions of paragraph 1 are secured by a special real estate privilege on the same areas, pursuant to and for the effects of Article 2748, second paragraph, of the civil code. This privilege can also be exercised to the detriment of the rights acquired by third parties on the property.
3. The privilege and the repetition of the costs can be exercised, against the owner of the site who is not guilty of the pollution or the danger of pollution, only following a motivated measure of the competent authority which justifies, among other things, the impossibility of ascertaining the identity of the responsible party or which justifies the impossibility of exercising recourse actions against the same party or their ineffectiveness.
4. In any case, the owner not responsible for the pollution may be required to reimburse, on the basis of a motivated measure and in compliance with the provisions of law no. 241 of 7 August 1990, the costs of the interventions adopted by the competent authority only within the limits of the market value of the site determined following the execution of the same interventions. In the case where the owner not responsible for the pollution has spontaneously provided for the remediation of the polluted site, he has the right to recourse against the person responsible for the pollution for the costs incurred and for any greater damage suffered.
5. The remediation interventions of polluted sites may be assisted, on the basis of a specific legislative financing provision, by public contributions within the maximum limit of fifty percent of the related costs if there are pre-eminent public interests connected to needs of health and environmental protection or occupational needs. The provisions of paragraphs 1 and 2 do not apply to the aforesaid public contributions.

**TITLE VI - SANCTION SYSTEM AND TRANSITIONAL AND FINAL PROVISIONS**

**CHAPTER I - SANCTIONS**

**Art. 254**
**Special rules**
1. The sanctions provided for by special rules in force remain unaffected.

**Art. 255**
**Abandonment of waste**
1. Without prejudice to the provisions of Article 256, paragraph 2, anyone who, in violation of the provisions of Articles 192, paragraphs 1 and 2, 226, paragraph 2, and 231, paragraphs 1 and 2, abandons or deposits waste or introduces it into surface or underground waters is punished with an administrative pecuniary sanction from one hundred and five euros to six hundred and twenty euros. If the abandonment of waste on the ground concerns non-hazardous and non-bulky waste, the administrative pecuniary sanction from twenty-five euros to one hundred and fifty-five euros applies.
2. The holder of the collection center, the concessionaire, or the holder of the branch of the manufacturing house who violates the provisions of Article 231, paragraph 5, is punished with an administrative pecuniary sanction from two hundred and sixty euros to one thousand five hundred and fifty euros.
3. Anyone who does not comply with the Mayor's ordinance, as per Article 192, paragraph 3, or does not fulfill the obligation of Article 187, paragraph 3, is punished with imprisonment for up to one year. In the conviction sentence or in the sentence issued pursuant to Article 444 of the Code of Criminal Procedure, the benefit of the conditional suspension of the penalty may be subordinated to the execution of the provisions of the ordinance of Article 192, paragraph 3, or to the fulfillment of the obligation of Article 187, paragraph 3.

**Art. 256**
**Unauthorized waste management activities**
1. Anyone who carries out an activity of collection, transport, recovery, disposal, trade, and intermediation of waste without the prescribed authorization, registration, or communication of Articles 208, 209, 210, 211, 212, 214, 215, and 216 is punished:
a) with the penalty of arrest from three months to one year or with a fine from two thousand six hundred euros to twenty-six thousand euros if it concerns non-hazardous waste;
b) with the penalty of arrest from six months to two years and with a fine from two thousand six hundred euros to twenty-six thousand euros if it concerns hazardous waste.
2. The penalties of paragraph 1 apply to the owners of companies and the heads of entities that abandon or deposit waste in an uncontrolled manner or introduce it into surface or underground waters in violation of the prohibition of Article 192, paragraphs 1 and 2.
3. Anyone who creates or manages an unauthorized landfill is punished with the penalty of arrest from six months to two years and with a fine from two thousand six hundred euros to twenty-six thousand euros. The penalty of arrest from one to three years and a fine from five thousand two hundred euros to fifty-two thousand euros applies if the landfill is intended, even in part, for the disposal of hazardous waste. The conviction sentence or the sentence issued pursuant to Article 444 of the Code of Criminal Procedure entails the confiscation of the area on which the illegal landfill is located if it is owned by the author or accomplice of the crime, without prejudice to the obligations of remediation or restoration of the state of the places.
4. The penalties of paragraphs 1, 2, and 3 are reduced by half in the cases of non-compliance with the prescriptions contained or referred to in the authorizations, as well as in the cases of lack of the requirements and conditions required for the registrations or communications.
5. Anyone who, in violation of the prohibition of Article 187, carries out unauthorized waste mixing activities, is punished with the penalty of paragraph 1, letter b).
6. Anyone who carries out temporary storage at the place of production of hazardous medical waste, in violation of the provisions of Article 227, paragraph 1, letter b), is punished with the penalty of arrest from three months to one year or with the penalty of a fine from two thousand six hundred euros to twenty-six thousand euros. The administrative pecuniary sanction from two thousand six hundred euros to fifteen thousand five hundred euros applies for quantities not exceeding two hundred liters or equivalent quantities.
7. Anyone who violates the obligations of Articles 231, paragraphs 7, 8, and 9, 233, paragraphs 12 and 13, and 234, paragraph 14, is punished with an administrative pecuniary sanction from two hundred and sixty euros to one thousand five hundred and fifty euros.
8. The subjects of Articles 233, 234, 235, and 236 who do not fulfill the participation obligations provided therein are punished with an administrative pecuniary sanction from eight thousand euros to forty-five thousand euros, without prejudice in any case to the obligation to pay the past contributions. Until the adoption of the decree of Article 234, paragraph 2, the sanctions of this paragraph are not applicable to the subjects of the same Article 234.
9. The sanctions of paragraph 8 are reduced by half in the case of adhesion made within the sixtieth day from the expiry of the term to fulfill the participation obligations provided for by Articles 233, 234, 235, and 236.

**Art. 257**
**Remediation of sites**
1. Anyone who causes the pollution of the soil, subsoil, surface waters, or groundwater with the exceedance of the risk threshold concentrations is punished with the penalty of arrest from six months to one year or with a fine from two thousand six hundred euros to twenty-six thousand euros, if they do not provide for remediation in accordance with the project approved by the competent authority within the procedure of Articles 242 and following. In case of failure to make the communication of Article 242, the transgressor is punished with the penalty of arrest from three months to one year or with a fine from one thousand euros to twenty-six thousand euros.
2. The penalty of arrest from one year to two years and the penalty of a fine from five thousand two hundred euros to fifty-two thousand euros applies if the pollution is caused by hazardous substances.
3. In the conviction sentence for the contravention of paragraphs 1 and 2, or in the sentence issued pursuant to Article 444 of the Code of Criminal Procedure, the benefit of the conditional suspension of the penalty may be subordinated to the execution of emergency, remediation, and environmental restoration interventions.
4. The observance of the projects approved pursuant to Articles 242 and following constitutes a condition of non-puni-shability for the environmental crimes contemplated by other laws for the same event and for the same polluting conduct of paragraph 1.

**Art. 258**
**Violation of communication obligations, keeping of mandatory registers, and forms**
1. The subjects of Article 189, paragraph 3, who do not make the communication prescribed therein or make it in an incomplete or inaccurate manner are punished with an administrative pecuniary sanction from two thousand six hundred euros to fifteen thousand five hundred euros; if the communication is made within the sixtieth day from the expiry of the term established pursuant to law no. 70 of 25 January 1994, the administrative pecuniary sanction from twenty-six euros to one hundred and sixty euros applies.
2. Anyone who omits to keep or keeps in an incomplete manner the loading and unloading register of Article 190, paragraph 1, is punished with an administrative pecuniary sanction from two thousand six hundred euros to fifteen thousand five hundred euros. If the register relates to hazardous waste, the administrative pecuniary sanction from fifteen thousand five hundred euros to ninety-three thousand euros applies, as well as the ancillary administrative sanction of suspension from one month to one year from the position held by the person responsible for the infringement and from the position of administrator.
3. In the case of companies that employ fewer than 15 employees, the minimum and maximum measures of paragraph 2 are reduced respectively from one thousand and forty euros to six thousand two hundred euros for non-hazardous waste and from two thousand and seventy euros to twelve thousand four hundred euros for hazardous waste. The number of employees is calculated with reference to the number of employees employed on average full-time during a year, while part-time and seasonal workers represent fractions of annual work units; for the aforesaid purposes, the year to be considered is that of the last approved financial year, preceding the moment of ascertainment of the infringement.
4. Anyone who transports waste without the form of Article 193 or indicates incomplete or inaccurate data in the same form is punished with an administrative pecuniary sanction from one thousand six hundred euros to nine thousand three hundred euros. The penalty of art. 483 of the penal code applies in the case of transport of hazardous waste. This latter penalty also applies to those who, in the preparation of a waste analysis certificate, provide false indications on the nature, composition, and chemical-physical characteristics of the waste and to those who use a false certificate during transport.
5. If the indications of paragraphs 1 and 2 are formally incomplete or inaccurate but the data reported in the communication to the cadastre, in the loading and unloading registers, in the identification forms of the transported waste, and in the other accounting records kept by law allow for the reconstruction of the due information, the administrative pecuniary sanction from two hundred and sixty euros to one thousand five hundred and fifty euros applies. The same penalty applies if the indications of paragraph 43 are formally incomplete or inaccurate but contain all the elements to reconstruct the information due by law, as well as in cases of failure to send to the competent authorities and failure to keep the registers of Article 190, paragraph 1, or the form of Article 193.

**Art. 259**
Illicit trafficking of waste
1. Anyone who carries out a shipment of waste constituting illicit traffic pursuant to art. 26 of Regulation (EEC) no. 259 of 1 February 1993, or carries out a shipment of waste listed in Annex II of the said regulation in violation of Article 1, paragraph 3, letters a), b), c), and d), of the same regulation is punished with a fine from one thousand five hundred and fifty euros to twenty-six thousand euros and with arrest for up to two years. The penalty is increased in the case of shipment of hazardous waste.
2. The conviction sentence, or that issued pursuant to Article 444 of the Code of Criminal Procedure, for the crimes relating to the illicit traffic of paragraph 1 or to the illicit transport of Articles 256 and 258, paragraph 4, mandatorily entails the confiscation of the means of transport.

**Art. 260**
**Organized activities for the illicit trafficking of waste**
1. Anyone who, for the purpose of obtaining an unjust profit, with multiple operations and through the preparation of means and continuous organized activities, cedes, receives, transports, exports, imports, or in any case manages illegally large quantities of waste is punished with imprisonment from one to six years.
2. If it concerns highly radioactive waste, the penalty of imprisonment from three to eight years applies.
3. The conviction entails the accessory penalties of Articles 28, 30, 32-bis, and 32-ter of the penal code, with the limitation of art. 33 of the same code.
4. The judge, with the conviction sentence or with that issued pursuant to Article 444 of the Code of Criminal Procedure, orders the restoration of the state of the environment and may subordinate the granting of the conditional suspension of the penalty to the elimination of the damage or danger to the environment.

**Art. 261**
**Packaging**
1. Producers and users who do not comply with the collection obligation of Article 221, paragraph 2, or do not adopt, as an alternative, management systems pursuant to the same Article 221, paragraph 3, letters a) and c), are punished with an administrative pecuniary sanction equal to six times the sums due to CONAI, without prejudice in any case to the obligation to pay the past contributions.
2. Packaging producers who do not organize a system for the fulfillment of the obligations of Article 221, paragraph 3, and do not adhere to the consortia of Article 223, nor adopt a system for the return of their own packaging pursuant to Article 221, paragraph 3, letters a) and c), are punished with an administrative pecuniary sanction from fifteen thousand five hundred euros to forty-six thousand five hundred euros. The same penalty applies to users who do not comply with the obligation of Article 221, paragraph 4.
3. The violation of the prohibitions of Article 226, paragraphs 1 and 4, is punished with an administrative pecuniary sanction from five thousand two hundred euros to forty thousand euros. The same penalty applies to anyone who places on the domestic market packaging lacking the requirements of Article 219, paragraph 5.
4. The violation of the provision of Article 226, paragraph 3, is punished with an administrative pecuniary sanction from two thousand six hundred euros to fifteen thousand five hundred euros.

**Art. 262**
**Competence and jurisdiction**
1. Without prejudice to the other provisions of law no. 689 of 24 November 1981, regarding the ascertainment of administrative offenses, the province in whose territory the violation was committed is responsible for the imposition of the administrative pecuniary sanctions provided for by the fourth part of this decree, with the exception of the sanctions provided for by Article 261, paragraph 3, in relation to the prohibition of Article 226, paragraph 1, for which the municipality is competent.
2. Against the injunction orders relating to the administrative sanctions of paragraph 1, the opposition judgment of art. 23 of law no. 689 of 24 November 1981 is available.
3. For the criminal proceedings pending at the date of entry into force of the fourth part of this decree, the judicial authority, if it does not have to issue a decree of dismissal or a sentence of acquittal, shall order the transmission of the documents to the Entities indicated in paragraph 1 for the application of the administrative sanctions.

**Art. 263**
**Proceeds from administrative pecuniary sanctions**
1. The proceeds of the administrative pecuniary sanctions for the violations of the provisions of the fourth part of this decree are devolved to the provinces and are intended for the exercise of control functions in environmental matters, except for the proceeds of the administrative pecuniary sanctions of Article 261, paragraph 3, in relation to the prohibition of Article 226, paragraph 1, which are devolved to the municipalities.

**CHAPTER II - TRANSITIONAL AND FINAL PROVISIONS**

**Art. 264**
**Repeal of norms**
1. As of the date of entry into force of the fourth part of this decree, the following are or remain repealed, excluding the provisions for which this decree provides for their continued validity:
a) law no. 366 of 20 March 1941;
b) the decree of the President of the Republic no. 915 of 10 September 1982;
c) decree-law no. 397 of 9 September 1988, converted, with amendments, by law no. 475 of 9 November 1988, with the exception of Article 9 and Article 9-quinquies as reformulated by this decree. In order to ensure that there is no solution of continuity in the transition from the pre-existing legislation to that provided for by the fourth part of this decree, the implementing provisions of art. 9-quinquies, of decree-law no. 397 of 9 September 1988, converted, with amendments, by law no. 475 of 9 November 1988, shall continue to apply until the date of entry into force of the corresponding implementing provisions provided for by the fourth part of this decree;
d) decree-law no. 361 of 31 August 1987, converted, with amendments, by law no. 441 of 29 October 1987, with the exception of articles 1, 1-bis, 1-ter, 1-quater, and 1-quinquies;
e) decree-law no. 527 of 14 December 1988, converted, with amendments, by law no. 45 of 10 February 1988;
f) art. 29-bis of decree-law no. 331 of 30 August 1993, converted, with amendments, by law no. 427 of 29 October 1993;
g) paragraphs 3, 4, and 5, second period, of art. 103 of legislative decree no. 285 of 30 April 1992;
h) art. 5, paragraph 1, of the decree of the President of the Republic of 8 August 1994, published in the official gazette no. 251 of 26 October 1994;
i) legislative decree no. 22 of 5 February 1997. In order to ensure that there is no solution of continuity in the transition from the pre-existing legislation to that provided for by the fourth part of this decree, the implementing provisions of the said legislative decree no. 22 of 5 February 1997, shall continue to apply until the date of entry into force of the corresponding implementing provisions provided for by the fourth part of this decree;
l) art. 14 of decree-law no. 138 of 8 July 2002, converted, with amendments, by article 14 of law no. 178 of 8 August 2002;
m) article 9, paragraph 2-bis, of law no. 342 of 21 November 2000, last period, from the words: "the subjects referred to in article 38, paragraph 3, letter a)" to the word: "CONAI";
n) article 19 of legislative decree no. 504 of 30 December 1992;
o) articles 4, 5, 8, 12, 14, and 15 of legislative decree no. 95 of 27 January 1992. All authorizations granted, at the date of entry into force of the fourth part of this decree, pursuant to the current legislation, including legislative decree no. 22 of 5 February 1997, legislative decree no. 95 of 27 January 1992, and decree no. 392 of 16 May 1996, published in the official gazette no. 173 of 25 July 1996, remain valid for the management of used oils, until the achievement or denial of those requested pursuant to this decree and for a period in any case not exceeding a triennium from its date of entry into force. In order to ensure that there is no solution of continuity in the transition from the pre-existing legislation to that provided for by the fourth part of this decree, the implementing provisions of art. 11 of legislative decree no. 95 of 27 January 1992, shall continue to apply until the date of entry into force of the corresponding implementing provisions provided for by the fourth part of this decree;
p) art. 19 of law no. 93 of 23 March 2001.
2. The Government, pursuant to art. 17, paragraph 2, of law no. 400 of 23 August 1988, shall adopt, within sixty days from the date of entry into force of the fourth part of this decree, on the proposal of the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory in concert with the Minister of Production Activities, after the opinion of the competent Parliamentary Commissions, which shall express themselves within thirty days from the transmission of the relative draft to the Chambers, a specific regulation with which the further normative acts incompatible with the provisions of the fourth part of this decree are identified, which are repealed with effect from the date of entry into force of the same regulation.

**Art. 265**
**Transitional provisions**
1. The existing regulatory and technical standards that regulate the collection, transport, and disposal of waste remain in force until the adoption of the corresponding specific standards adopted in implementation of the fourth part of this decree. In order to ensure that there is no solution of continuity in the transition from the pre-existing legislation to that provided for by the fourth part of this decree, public administrations, in the exercise of their respective competences, shall adapt the pre-existing implementing legislation to the discipline contained in the fourth part of this decree, in compliance with what is established by article 264, paragraph 1, letter i). Any reference to toxic and harmful waste shall continue to be understood as referring to hazardous waste.
2. Pending the specific regulatory and technical standards on waste transport, as per article 195, paragraph 2, letter l), and without prejudice to the provisions of legislative decree no. 182 of 24 June 2003 on waste produced by ships and cargo residues, waste is assimilated to goods as regards the regulatory regime on transport by sea and the discipline of loading, unloading, transfer, deposit, and handling operations in port areas. In particular, hazardous waste is assimilated to dangerous goods.
3. The Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, in concert with the Minister of Education, University and Research and with the Minister of Production Activities, shall identify with a specific decree the forms of promotion and incentive for research and development of new remediation technologies at universities, as well as at companies and their consortia.
4. Without prejudice to the interventions carried out at the date of entry into force of the fourth part of this decree, within one hundred and eighty days from that date, an adequate technical report may be submitted to the competent authority in order to reshape the already authorized remediation objectives on the basis of the criteria defined by the fourth part of this decree. The competent authority shall examine the documentation and arrange the necessary variations to the project.
5. By decree of the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory in concert with the Minister of Production Activities, the methods, prerequisites, and economic effects are regulated for the hypothesis in which the subjects adhering to the existing consortia establish or adhere to new consortia or to alternative forms, in conformity with the model statute types approved by the same Ministers, without this resulting in new or greater burdens on public finance.
6. The steel and metallurgical companies operating at the date of entry into force of the fourth part of this decree and subject to the discipline of legislative decree no. 59 of 18 February 2005, are authorized on a transitional basis, upon presentation of the relative application, and until the release or final denial of the same authorization, to use, employing them in their production cycle, the ferrous scrap identified by code GA 430 of Annex II (green list of waste) of Regulation (EC) no. 259 of 1 February 1993 and the non-ferrous scrap identified by equivalent codes of the same Annex.

**Art. 266**
**Final provisions**
1. The sanitary facilities referred to in art. 4, paragraph 2, letter g), of law no. 847 of 29 September 1964, include the works, constructions, and plants intended for the disposal, recycling, or destruction of urban, special, hazardous, solid, and liquid waste, for the remediation of polluted areas.
2. The implementation of the provisions of the fourth part of this decree must not result in new or greater burdens or lower revenues for the State.
3. The expenses for the indemnity and for the economic treatment of the personnel of art. 9 of decree-law no. 397 of 9 September 1988, converted, with amendments, by law no. 475 of 9 November 1988, remain at the expense of the Ministry of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, except as provided for in the following period. The economic treatment remains at the expense of the institutions of origin, upon agreement with the same, in the case where the personnel carries out activities of common interest.
4. Waste from maintenance or health care activities is considered produced at the headquarters or domicile of the subject who carries out such activities.
5. The provisions of articles 189, 190, 193, and 212 do not apply to the collection and transport activities of waste carried out by subjects authorized to carry out the same activities in an itinerant form, limited to the waste that is the object of their trade.
6. Without prejudice to the effects of the sanctioning measures adopted with final acts, from the date of publication of this decree, the provisions imposing the obligations of articles 48, paragraph 2, and 51, paragraph 6-ter, of legislative decree no. 22 of 5 February 1997, as well as the sanctioning provisions provided for by the same article 51, paragraphs 6-bis, 6-ter, and 6-quinquies, do not apply, also with reference to cases that occurred after 31 March 2004.
7. With a subsequent decree, adopted by the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory in concert with the Ministers of Infrastructure and Transport, Production Activities, and Health, the discipline for the administrative simplification of the procedures relating to materials, including excavated earth and rocks, from small construction sites whose production does not exceed six thousand cubic meters of material, is dictated.

**PART FIVE - RULES ON AIR PROTECTION AND REDUCTION OF ATMOSPHERIC EMISSIONS**

**TITLE I - PREVENTION AND LIMITATION OF ATMOSPHERIC EMISSIONS FROM PLANTS AND ACTIVITIES**

**Art. 267**
**Scope of application**
1. This title, for the purposes of prevention and limitation of atmospheric pollution, applies to plants, including civil thermal plants not regulated by title II, and to activities that produce atmospheric emissions and establishes emission values, prescriptions, sampling and analysis methods for emissions, and criteria for the evaluation of the conformity of the measured values to the limit values.
2. Plants regulated by legislative decree no. 133 of 11 May 2005, implementing Directive 2000/76/EC on the incineration of waste, are excluded from the scope of application of the fifth part of this decree.
3. It remains established, for plants subject to integrated environmental authorization, what is provided for by legislative decree no. 59 of 18 February 2005; for such plants, the integrated environmental authorization replaces the authorization for emissions provided for by this title.
4. In order to allow the achievement of the objectives deriving from the Kyoto Protocol and to favor in any case the reduction of atmospheric emissions of polluting substances, the legislation of the fifth part of this decree intends to determine the implementation of all the most appropriate actions aimed at promoting the use of electricity produced by production plants powered by renewable sources pursuant to the community and national legislation in force and, in particular, of Directive 2001/77/EC and of legislative decree no. 387 of 29 December 2003, determining its priority dispatching. In particular:
a) measures aimed at favoring the production of electricity through renewable sources and at the same time developing the production base of clean technologies, with particular reference to Southern Italy, may be promoted by the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory in concert with the Ministers of Production Activities and for Development and Territorial Cohesion;
b) by decree of the Minister of Production Activities in concert with the Ministers of the Environment and Protection of the Territory and of Economy and Finance, to be issued within thirty days from the date of entry into force of the fifth part of this decree, the fees of the members of the Observatory of art. 16 of legislative decree no. 387 of 29 December 2003 are determined, to be applied from the date of appointment, within the limits of the resources of article 16, paragraph 6, of the same legislative decree and without new or greater burdens on public finance;
c) the green certificates accrued for energy produced pursuant to art. 1, paragraph 71, of law no. 239 of 23 August 2004, may be used to fulfill the obligation of art. 11 of legislative decree no. 79 of 16 March 1999, only after all the green certificates accrued by the producers of electricity produced from renewable sources as defined by art. 2, paragraph 1, letter a), of legislative decree no. 387 of 2003 have been canceled;
d) in order to extend the validity period of the green certificates, in art. 20, paragraph 5, of legislative decree no. 387 of 29 December 2003, the words "eight years" are replaced by the words "twelve years".

**Art. 268**
**Definitions**
1. For the purposes of this title, the following definitions apply:
a) atmospheric pollution: any modification of the atmospheric air, due to the introduction into it of one or more substances in quantities and with characteristics such as to harm or constitute a danger to human health or to the quality of the environment or such as to harm material goods or compromise the legitimate uses of the environment;
b) emission: any solid, liquid, or gaseous substance introduced into the atmosphere that may cause atmospheric pollution;
c) channelled emission: emission of a gaseous effluent carried out through one or more specific points;
d) diffuse emission: emission other than that falling under letter c); for the activities of Article 275, diffuse emissions also include the solvents contained in the products, without prejudice to the different indications contained in Part III of Annex III to the fifth part of this decree;
e) technically channellable emission: diffuse emission that must be channelled on the basis of the best available techniques or in the presence of situations or zones that require particular protection;
f) total emissions: the sum of diffuse emissions and channelled emissions;
g) gaseous effluent: the gaseous discharge, containing solid, liquid, or gaseous emissions; its volumetric flow rate is expressed in cubic meters per hour reported to normal conditions (Nm3/hour), after deduction of the water vapor content, unless otherwise established by the fifth part of this decree;
