h) plant: the machinery or system or the set of machinery or systems consisting of a fixed structure and having functional autonomy as it is intended for a specific activity; the specific activity for which the plant is intended may constitute the phase of a larger production cycle;
i) plant prior to 1988: a plant which, on 1 July 1988, was in operation or built in all its parts or authorized pursuant to the previous legislation;
l) plant prior to 2006: a plant that does not fall under the definition of letter i) and that, at the date of entry into force of the fifth part of this decree, is authorized pursuant to the decree of the President of the Republic no. 203 of 24 May 1988, provided that it is in operation or put into operation within the following twenty-four months; plants prior to 1988 whose authorization has been updated pursuant to art. 11 of the decree of the President of the Republic no. 203 of 24 May 1988 are also considered prior to 2006;
m) new plant: a plant that does not fall under the definitions of letters i) and l);
n) operator: the natural or legal person who has decision-making power over the installation or operation of the plant or, in the cases provided for by Article 269, paragraphs 10, 11, and 12, and by Article 275, the natural or legal person who has decision-making power over the exercise of the activity;
o) competent authority: the region or the autonomous province or the different authority indicated by regional law as the competent authority for the issuance of the authorization for emissions and for the adoption of the other measures provided for by this title; for off-shore platforms and for off-shore liquefied natural gas regasification terminals, the competent authority is the Ministry of the Environment and Protection of the Territory; for plants subject to integrated environmental authorization and for the fulfillments connected to it, the competent authority is the one that issues such authorization;
p) competent authority for control: the authority to which the regional law attributes the task of carrying out, on an ordinary basis, the checks regarding compliance with the authorization and the provisions of this title, without prejudice to the competences of the judicial police bodies; for plants subject to integrated environmental authorization and for the controls connected to it, the competent authority for control is that provided for by the legislation that regulates such authorization;
q) emission limit value: the emission factor, the concentration, the percentage, or the mass flow of polluting substances in the emissions that must not be exceeded;
r) emission factor: ratio between the mass of polluting substance emitted and a specific unit of measure of product or service;
s) concentration: ratio between the mass of polluting substance emitted and the volume of the gaseous effluent; for combustion plants, the emission values expressed as concentration (mg/Nm3) are calculated considering, unless otherwise established by the fifth part of this decree, a reference volumetric oxygen content of 3 percent by volume of the gaseous effluent for liquid and gaseous fuels, of 6 percent by volume for solid fuels, and of 15 percent by volume for gas turbines;
t) percentage: ratio between the mass of polluting substance emitted and the mass of the same substance used in the production process, multiplied by one hundred;
u) mass flow: mass of polluting substance emitted per unit of time;
v) emission relevance threshold: mass flow, for a single pollutant, measured upstream of any abatement systems, and in the most severe operating conditions of the plant, below which the emission limit values do not apply;
z) normal conditions: a temperature of 273.15 K and a pressure of 101.3 kPa;
aa) best available techniques: the most efficient and advanced stage in the development of activities and their methods of operation which indicate the practical suitability of particular techniques for providing in principle the basis for emission limit values and other permit conditions designed to prevent and, where that is not practicable, to reduce emissions; for this purpose, it is understood by:
1) techniques: both the technology used and the way in which the installation is designed, built, maintained, operated, and decommissioned;
2) available: techniques developed on a scale which allows implementation in the relevant industrial sector, under economically and technically viable conditions, taking into consideration the costs and advantages, whether or not the techniques are used or produced in the national territory, as long as they are reasonably accessible to the operator;
3) best: the most effective in achieving a high general level of protection of the environment as a whole;
bb) start-up period: unless otherwise provided for in the authorization, the time in which the plant, following the supply of energy, fuels, or materials, is brought from a condition in which it does not carry out the activity for which it is intended, or carries it out in a process load situation lower than the technical minimum, to a condition in which this activity is carried out in a process load situation equal to or greater than the technical minimum;
cc) shutdown period: unless otherwise provided for in the authorization, the time in which the plant, following the interruption of the supply of energy, fuels, or materials, not due to a malfunction, is brought from a condition in which it carries out the activity for which it is intended in a process load situation equal to or greater than the technical minimum to a condition in which this function is carried out in a process load situation lower than the technical minimum or is not carried out;
dd) process load: the percentage level of production with respect to the nominal capacity of the plant;
ee) technical minimum: the minimum process load compatible with the operation of the plant in a steady state;
ff) combustion plant: any technical apparatus in which fuels are oxidized in order to use the heat thus produced;
gg) large combustion plant: a combustion plant with a rated thermal input of not less than 50 MW;
hh) rated thermal input of the combustion plant: the product of the lower calorific value of the fuel used and the maximum flow rate of fuel burned at the single combustion plant, as declared by the manufacturer, expressed in thermal watts or its multiples;
ii) organic compound: any compound containing at least the element carbon and one or more of the following elements: hydrogen, halogens, oxygen, sulfur, phosphorus, silicon, or nitrogen, with the exception of carbon oxides and inorganic carbonates and bicarbonates;
ll) volatile organic compound (VOC): any organic compound having at 293.15 K a vapor pressure of 0.01 kPa or more, or having a corresponding volatility under particular conditions of use. For the purposes of the fifth part of this decree, the fraction of creosote which at a temperature of 293.15 K has a vapor pressure greater than 0.01 kPa is considered as a VOC;
mm) organic solvent: any VOC used alone or in combination with other agents for the purpose of dissolving raw materials, products, or waste, without undergoing chemical transformations, or used as a cleaning agent to dissolve contaminants or as a solvent, a dispersion medium, a viscosity adjuster, a surface tension adjuster, a plasticizer, or a preservative;
nn) nominal capacity: the maximum daily mass of organic solvents used for the activities of Article 275, carried out under normal operating conditions and as a function of the product capacity for which the activities are designed;
oo) solvent consumption: the total quantity of organic solvents used for the activities of Article 275 per civil year or for any other twelve-month period, minus any VOC recovered for reuse;
pp) maximum theoretical solvent consumption: the solvent consumption calculated on the basis of the nominal capacity referred to, unless otherwise established by the authorization, for three hundred and thirty days per year in the case of continuous cycle activities and two hundred and twenty days per year for other activities;
qq) reuse of organic solvents: the use of organic solvents produced by an activity and subsequently recovered for the purpose of being used by the same for any technical or commercial purpose, including use as a fuel;
rr) consumption threshold: the solvent consumption expressed in tons/year established by Part II of Annex III to the fifth part of this decree, for the activities provided therein;
ss) refineries: mineral oil refineries subject to authorization pursuant to law no. 239 of 23 August 2004;
tt) fuel distribution plants: plants where fuel is dispensed to the tanks of motor vehicles from storage plants;
uu) petrol: any petroleum derivative, with or without additives, corresponding to the following customs codes: NC 2710 1131 - 2710 1141 - 2710 1145 - 2710 1149 - 2710 1151 - 2710 1159 or having a Reid vapor pressure of 27.6 kilopascals or more, ready for use as fuel for motor vehicles, with the exception of liquefied petroleum gas (LPG);
vv) terminal: any structure used for loading and unloading petrol into/from a road tanker, rail tanker, or ship tanker, including the storage plants present at the site of the structure;
zz) storage plant: any fixed tank used for the storage of fuel;
aaa) loading plant: any plant at a terminal where petrol can be loaded into mobile tanks. Loading plants for road tankers include one or more loading gantries;
bbb) loading gantry: any structure at a terminal by which petrol can, at any given time, be loaded into a single road tanker;
ccc) temporary vapor storage: the temporary storage of vapors in a fixed-roof storage plant at a terminal before transfer and subsequent recovery at another terminal. The transfer of vapors from one storage plant to another at the same terminal is not considered temporary vapor storage for the purposes of the fifth part of this decree;
ddd) mobile tank: a tank with a capacity greater than 1 m3, transported by road, by rail, or by navigable waterway and used for the transfer of petrol from one terminal to another or from a terminal to a fuel distribution plant;
eee) road tanker: a vehicle used for the road transport of petrol which includes one or more permanently mounted tanks or tanks forming an integral part of the chassis or one or more removable tanks.

**Art. 269**
**Authorization for atmospheric emissions**
1. Without prejudice to what is established by Article 267, paragraph 3, by paragraphs 14 and 16 of this article, and by Article 272, paragraph 5, for all plants that produce emissions, an authorization must be requested pursuant to the fifth part of this decree.
2. The operator who intends to install a new plant or transfer a plant from one location to another shall submit an authorization application to the competent authority, accompanied by:
a) the project of the plant in which the specific activity for which the plant is intended is described, the techniques adopted to limit the emissions and the quantity and quality of such emissions, the operating methods and the quantity, type, and product characteristics of the fuels intended for use, as well as, for plants subject to this condition, the technical minimum defined through the plant parameters that characterize it, and
b) by a technical report describing the overall production cycle in which the specific activity for which the plant is intended is inserted and indicating the period foreseen between commissioning and reaching full operational capacity.
3. For the purpose of issuing the authorization, the competent authority shall convene, within thirty days of receiving the request, a services conference pursuant to Articles 14 and following of Law no. 241 of 7 August 1990, during which a simultaneous examination of the interests involved in other administrative proceedings is also carried out, in particular, in the proceedings conducted by the municipality pursuant to the decree of the President of the Republic no. 380 of 6 June 2001, and the royal decree no. 1265 of 27 July 1934. Any integrations of the application must be transmitted to the competent authority within thirty days of the request; if the competent authority does not decide within a period of one hundred and twenty days or, in case of integration of the authorization application, within one hundred and fifty days of receiving the application itself, the operator may, within the following sixty days, request the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory to provide, notifying this request also to the competent authority. The Minister shall decide on the request, in concert with the Ministers of Health and of Production Activities, after consulting the interested municipality, within ninety days or, in the cases provided for by Article 281, paragraph 1, within one hundred and fifty days of receiving it; once this term has elapsed, art. 2, paragraph 5, of Law no. 241 of 7 August 1990 shall apply.
4. The authorization shall establish, pursuant to Articles 270 and 271:
a) for emissions that are technically channellable, the methods of capture and channelling;
b) for channelled emissions or for which channelling has been ordered, the emission limit values, the prescriptions, the sampling and analysis methods, the criteria for evaluating the conformity of the measured values to the limit values, and the frequency of the controls under the operator's responsibility;
c) for diffuse emissions, specific prescriptions aimed at ensuring their containment.
5. The authorization shall establish the period that must elapse between the commissioning and the reaching of full operational capacity of the plant. The commissioning must be communicated to the competent authority at least fifteen days in advance. The authorization shall establish the date by which the data relating to the emissions made in a continuous period of controlled operation of a duration not less than ten days, starting from the reaching of full operational capacity, and the duration of this period, as well as the number of samplings to be carried out, must be communicated to the competent authority.
6. The competent authority for control shall carry out the first check on compliance with the authorization within six months of the date of reaching full operational capacity of the plant.
7. The authorization issued pursuant to this article has a duration of fifteen years. The renewal application must be submitted at least one year before the expiry date.
In the absence of a decision on the renewal application for the authorization issued pursuant to this article, the operation of the plant may continue even after the expiry of the authorization if the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory has been requested to provide for it pursuant to paragraph 3, and has not yet made a decision. The updating of the authorization pursuant to paragraph 8 entails the start of a new fifteen-year period only in the case of a substantial modification.
8. The operator who intends to subject a plant to a modification, which involves a variation of what is indicated in the project or in the technical report of paragraph 2 in the authorization of paragraph 3 or in the authorization issued pursuant to the decree of the President of the Republic no. 203 of 24 May 1988, or in the documents provided for by art. 12 of that decree, including those relating to the operating methods or the fuels used, shall notify the competent authority or, if the modification is substantial, shall submit an application for updating pursuant to this article. If the modification for which communication has been given is substantial, the competent authority shall order the operator to submit an application for updating the authorization, to which the provisions of this article apply. If the modification is not substantial, the competent authority shall, where necessary, update the existing authorization. If the competent authority does not express itself within sixty days, the operator may proceed with the execution of the non-substantial communicated modification, without prejudice to the power of the competent authority to provide for it subsequently, within six months of receiving the communication. A substantial modification is intended as one that involves an increase or a qualitative variation of the emissions or that alters the technical conditions for their channelling. This paragraph also applies to those who intend to modify an activity authorized pursuant to paragraphs 10, 11, 12, and 13. What is provided for by Article 275, paragraph 11, remains unaffected.
9. The competent authority for control is authorized to carry out at the plants all the inspections it deems necessary to ascertain compliance with the authorization.
10. Without prejudice to what is provided for by Article 275, whoever intends to carry out, in a non-occasional manner, painting activities in a place adapted for this purpose and in the absence of a plant shall submit a specific application to the competent authority, unless the activity falls among those provided for by Article 272, paragraph 1. The competent authority shall evaluate whether, pursuant to Article 270, paragraphs 1 and 2, the emissions produced by such activities must be channelled through the creation of a plant.
11. In the case where the channelling of emissions is ordered pursuant to paragraph 10, the limit values and prescriptions of Article 271, contained in the authorizations issued in accordance with this article, shall apply, or, if the activity falls among those provided for by Article 272, paragraph 2, the limit values and prescriptions contained in the general authorizations regulated therein shall apply. In the case where the channelling of emissions is not ordered, the authorization shall establish specific prescriptions aimed at ensuring the containment of the diffuse emissions produced by the activity; the provisions of this article, excluding those that may refer only to channelled emissions, shall apply to such authorization.
12. The provisions of paragraphs 10 and 11 also apply to whoever intends to carry out, in a non-occasional manner and in a place adapted for this purpose, in the absence of a plant, activities of processing, transformation, or conservation of agricultural materials, which produce emissions, or activities of production, manipulation, transport, loading, unloading, or storage of dusty materials, unless such activities fall among those provided for by Article 272, paragraph 1. For activities involving dusty materials, the norms of Part I of Annex V to the fifth part of this decree shall apply.
13. If a place is adapted, in the absence of a fixed structure, for the non-occasional exercise of the activities provided for in paragraphs 10 or 12, carried out therein on an occasional basis by multiple subjects, the authorization is requested by the manager of the place. For the purposes of this paragraph, manager means the subject who exercises decision-making power over the methods and conditions of use of that area by whoever carries out the activity.
14. The following plants are not subject to authorization:
a) combustion plants, including cogeneration generator sets, with a nominal thermal input of less than 1 MW, powered by biomass as per Annex X to the fifth part of this decree, by diesel oil, as such or in emulsion, or by biodiesel;
b) combustion plants powered by fuel oil, as such or in emulsion, with a nominal thermal input of less than 0.3 MW;
c) combustion plants powered by methane or LPG, with a nominal thermal input of less than 3 MW;
d) combustion plants, located within waste disposal plants, powered by landfill gas, residual gases from purification processes, and biogas, with a nominal thermal input not exceeding 3 MW, if the recovery activity is subject to the simplified authorization procedures provided for by the fourth part of this decree and such procedures have been completed;
e) combustion plants powered by biogas as per Annex X to the fifth part of this decree, with a total nominal thermal input of less than or equal to 3 MW;
f) cogeneration generator sets powered by methane or LPG, with a nominal thermal input of less than 3 MW;
g) cogeneration generator sets powered by petrol with a nominal thermal input of less than 1 MW;
h) combustion plants connected to the storage activities of petroleum products operating for less than 2200 hours per year, with a nominal thermal input of less than 5 MW if powered by methane or LPG and less than 2.5 MW if powered by diesel;
i) emergency and safety plants, analysis and research laboratories, pilot plants for tests, research, experimentation, identification of prototypes. This exemption does not apply in the case of emission of carcinogenic, toxic for reproduction or mutagenic substances or substances of particularly high toxicity and cumulativeness, as identified by Part II of Annex I to the fifth part of this decree.
15. The competent authority may provide, with its own general measure, that the operators of the plants of paragraph 14 shall communicate to the same, in advance, the date of commissioning of the plant or the start of the activity.
16. The storage plants for mineral oils, including liquefied gases, are not subject to authorization. The operators are in any case required to adopt appropriate measures to contain diffuse emissions and to respect any further prescriptions possibly ordered, for the same purposes, with a specific measure by the competent authority.

**Art. 270**
**Channelling of emissions**
1. In the authorization phase, the competent authority shall verify if the diffuse emissions of a plant or of a fixed machine with functional autonomy are technically channellable on the basis of the best available techniques and on the basis of the relevant prescriptions of Annex I to the fifth part of this decree and, in this case, shall order their capture and channelling.
2. In the presence of particular situations of health risk or zones that require particular environmental protection, the competent authority shall order the capture and channelling of diffuse emissions pursuant to paragraph 1 even if the identified technique does not satisfy the availability requirement of Article 268, paragraph 1, letter aa), number 2).
3. By decree of the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, in concert with the Ministers of Production Activities and of Health, the criteria to be used for the verification of paragraphs 1 and 2 shall be established.
4. If multiple plants with similar technical and constructive characteristics, having emissions with homogeneous chemical-physical characteristics and located in the same place, are intended for specific identical activities, the competent authority, taking into account the technical and economic conditions, may consider them as a single plant.
5. In the case of channelled emissions or for which channelling has been ordered, each plant or fixed machine with functional autonomy, also identified pursuant to paragraph 4, must have a single emission point, without prejudice to what is provided for in paragraphs 6 and 7. Unless otherwise provided for by other provisions of this title, the emission limit values apply to each emission point.
6. Where it is not technically possible to ensure compliance with paragraph 5, the competent authority may authorize a new plant or fixed machine with functional autonomy having multiple emission points. In this case, the emission limit values expressed as mass flow, emission factor, and percentage refer to the complex of emissions of the plant or of the fixed machine with functional autonomy, and those expressed as concentration refer to the emissions of the single points, without prejudice to the application of Article 271, paragraph 10.
7. Where it is not technically possible to ensure compliance with paragraph 5, the competent authority may authorize the channelling of the emissions of multiple new plants or fixed machines with functional autonomy into one or more common emission points, also belonging to plants prior to 2006 and 1988, provided that the emissions of all the plants or of all the fixed machines with functional autonomy present homogeneous chemical-physical characteristics. In this case, the most severe of the emission limit values expressed as concentration provided for the single plants or fixed machines with functional autonomy applies to each common emission point.
8. The plants prior to 2006 and 1988 shall adapt to what is provided for in paragraph 5 or, where this is not technically possible, to what is provided for in paragraphs 6 and 7 within three years following the first renewal of the authorization carried out pursuant to Article 281, paragraph 1. For the purposes of the application of paragraphs 4, 5, 6, and 7, the competent authority shall also take into account the documentation prepared by the commission of Article 281, paragraph 9.

**Art. 271**
**Emission limit values and prescriptions**
1. Annex I to the fifth part of this decree establishes the emission limit values, with the indication of a maximum value and a minimum value, and the prescriptions for the operation of plants prior to 1988 and of all the plants of Article 269, paragraph 14, except for those of letter d). The emission limit values and the prescriptions established in Annex I apply to new plants and to plants prior to 2006 exclusively in the cases expressly provided for by that Annex. Annex V to the fifth part of this decree establishes specific prescriptions for the emissions of dust from activities of production, manipulation, transport, loading, unloading, or storage of dusty materials and for the emissions in the form of gas or vapor deriving from activities of processing, transport, transfer, and storage of liquid organic substances.
2. With a specific decree, adopted pursuant to Article 281, paragraph 5, Annex I to the fifth part of this decree shall be integrated with the setting of limit values and prescriptions for the operation of new plants and those prior to 2006. With this decree, the same Annex I is also updated. Until the adoption of this decree, the methods previously in use shall apply for plants prior to 1988 and 2006, and for new plants, the methods established by the competent authority on the basis of the relevant CEN technical standards or, where these are not available, of the relevant ISO technical standards, or, where these are also not available, on the basis of the relevant national or international technical standards.
3. The region or the autonomous province may establish, by law or by general provision, on the basis of the best available techniques, emission limit values between the minimum and maximum values set by Annex I to the fifth part of this decree. The region or the autonomous province may also establish, for the purposes of evaluating the extent of the dilution of emissions, characteristic flow rates for specific types of plants.
4. The plans and programs provided for by art. 8 of legislative decree no. 351 of 4 August 1999, and by art. 3 of legislative decree no. 183 of 21 May 2004, may establish emission limit values and prescriptions, also concerning the construction or operating conditions of the plant, more severe than those set by Annex I to the fifth part of this decree and by the legislation of paragraph 3, provided that this is necessary for the achievement of the limit values and target values of air quality. Until the issuance of such plans and programs, the emission limit values and the prescriptions contained in the plans adopted pursuant to art. 4 of the decree of the President of the Republic no. 203 of 24 May 1988 shall continue to apply.
5. The plans and programs of paragraph 4 may establish emission limit values and prescriptions for new plants or plants prior to 2006 even before the adoption of the decree of paragraph 2.
6. For each of the plants for which the application of Article 269 is submitted, the authorization establishes the emission limit values and the prescriptions on the basis of the values and prescriptions set by Annex I to the fifth part of this decree, by the legislation of paragraph 3, and by the plans and programs relating to air quality. The prescriptions aimed at ensuring the containment of diffuse emissions are established on the basis of the best available techniques and on the basis of the relevant provisions of Annexes I and V to the fifth part of this decree. For substances for which emission values are not set, the authorization establishes specific limit values with reference to those provided for similar substances in terms of chemistry and having similar effects on health and the environment.
7. In the case where the legislation of paragraph 3 and the plans and programs relating to air quality do not establish emission limit values, the maximum value established by Annex I to the fifth part of this decree must not in any case be exceeded in the authorization.
8. For new plants or for plants prior to 2006, until the adoption of the decree of paragraph 2, the authorization establishes the emission limit values and the prescriptions on the basis of the values and prescriptions set in the plans and programs of paragraph 5 and on the basis of the best available techniques. In the authorization, the minimum emission values that Annex I sets for plants prior to 1988 must not in any case be exceeded. The prescriptions aimed at ensuring the containment of diffuse emissions are established on the basis of the best available techniques and of Annex V to the fifth part of this decree. The last period of paragraph 6 applies.
9. Without prejudice to what is provided for in paragraph 8, the authorization may establish emission limit values more severe than those set by Annex I to the fifth part of this decree, by the legislation of paragraph 3, and by the plans and programs relating to air quality:
a) upon renewal, on the basis of the best available techniques, also taking into account the relationship between the costs and the overall benefits;
b) for zones of particular natural value, identified within the plans and programs adopted pursuant to Articles 8 and 9 of legislative decree no. 351 of 4 August 1999, or of art. 3 of legislative decree no. 183 of 21 May 2004, or of art. 4 of the decree of the President of the Republic no. 203 of 24 May 1988.
10. In the case provided for by Article 270, paragraph 6, the authorization may provide that the emission limit values refer to the weighted average of the emissions of polluting substances that are equal or belong to the same class and have homogeneous chemical characteristics, coming from the different emission points of the plant. The total mass flow of the plant must not be greater than what it would be if the emission limit values were applied to the single emission points.
11. The emission limit values and the reference volumetric oxygen content refer to the volume of gaseous effluent reported to normal conditions, after deduction, unless otherwise indicated in Annex I to the fifth part of this decree, of the volumetric content of water vapor.
12. Unless otherwise indicated in Annex I to the fifth part of this decree, the reference volumetric oxygen content is that deriving from the process. If in the emission the volumetric oxygen content is different from the reference one, the measured concentrations must be corrected using the following formula:
E = EM * (21 - O2) / (21 - O2M)
where:
EM = measured concentration
E = concentration
O2 M = measured oxygen content
O2 = reference oxygen content
13. The emission limit values refer to the quantity of emission diluted to the extent that is unavoidable from a technological and operational point of view. In case of further dilution of the emission, the measured concentrations must be corrected using the following formula:
E = EM * PM / P
where:
PM = measured flow rate
EM = measured concentration
P = flow rate of gaseous effluent diluted to the extent that is unavoidable from a technological and operational point of view
E = concentration referred to P
14. Unless otherwise established by the fifth part of this decree, the emission limit values apply to periods of normal operation of the plant, understood as the periods in which the plant is in operation, excluding the start-up and shutdown periods and the periods in which malfunctions occur such as not to allow compliance with the values themselves. The authorization may establish specific prescriptions for these start-up and shutdown periods and for the eventuality of such malfunctions and identify further transitional periods in which the emission limit values do not apply. If a malfunction occurs such as not to allow compliance with emission limit values, the competent authority must be informed within the following eight hours and may order the reduction or cessation of activities or other prescriptions, without prejudice to the obligation of the operator to proceed with the functional restoration of the plant in the shortest possible time. The operator is in any case required to take all appropriate precautions to minimize emissions during the start-up and shutdown phases. Periods of oscillation that occur regularly in the performance of the plant's function do not in any case constitute start-up or shutdown periods.
15. For the large combustion plants of Article 273 and for the plants of Article 275, this article applies with reference to the emission limit values provided therein.
16. For plants subject to integrated environmental authorization, the limit values and prescriptions of this article apply for the purpose of issuing such authorization, without prejudice to the power of the competent authority to establish more severe limit values and prescriptions.
17. Annex VI to the fifth part of this decree establishes the criteria for evaluating the conformity of the measured values to the emission limit values. With a specific decree pursuant to Article 281, paragraph 5, the aforesaid Annex VI shall be integrated, providing for specific sampling and analysis methods for emissions as well as methods capable of guaranteeing the quality of the continuous emission monitoring systems. Until the adoption of such decree, the methods previously in use shall apply for plants prior to 1988 and 2006, and for new plants, the methods established by the competent authority on the basis of the relevant CEN technical standards or, where these are not available, of the relevant ISO technical standards, or, where these are also not available, on the basis of the relevant national or international technical standards.

**Art. 272**
**Plants and activities under derogation**
1. The competent authority may provide, with its own general measure, that the operators of the plants or activities listed in Part I of Annex IV to the fifth part of this decree shall communicate to the same that they fall within this list and, in advance, the date of commissioning of the plant or the start of the activity, unless otherwise provided for by the same Annex. The aforesaid list, referring to plants or activities whose emissions are scarcely relevant for the purposes of atmospheric pollution, may be updated and integrated as provided for by Article 281, paragraph 5, also on the proposal of the regions, the autonomous provinces, and the representative associations of productive categories.
2. For specific categories of plants, identified in relation to the type and methods of production, the competent authority may adopt specific general authorizations, for each single category of plants, in which the emission limit values, the prescriptions, the adaptation times, the sampling and analysis methods, and the frequency of the controls are established. The emission limit values and the prescriptions are established in accordance with Article 271, paragraphs 6 and 8. The competent authority must in any case proceed with the adoption of such general authorizations, within two years from the date of entry into force of the fifth part of this decree, for the plants and activities of Part II of Annex IV to the fifth part of this decree. In case of failure to adopt the general authorization, within the prescribed term, the same is issued with a specific decree of the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory and the operators of the interested plants communicate their adhesion to the competent authority; the power of this authority to subsequently adopt new general authorizations, the adhesion to which entails, for the interested subject, the lapse of that adopted by the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, is without prejudice. The operators of the plants for which a general authorization has been adopted may in any case submit an authorization application pursuant to Article 269.
3. The operator of the plants or activities of paragraph 2 shall submit to the competent authority, at least forty-five days before the installation of the plant or the start of the activity, an application for adhesion to the general authorization. The competent authority may, with its own measure, deny the adhesion in the case where the requirements provided for by the general authorization are not respected or in the presence of particular situations of health risk or zones that require particular environmental protection. The general authorization establishes the requirements of the application for adhesion and may provide, for the plants and activities of Part II of Annex IV to the fifth part of this decree, specific simplified application models, in which the quantities and qualities of the emissions are deductible from the quantities of raw and auxiliary materials used. The competent authority shall proceed, every fifteen years, to the renewal of the general authorizations adopted pursuant to this article. For the general authorizations issued pursuant to the decree of the President of the Council of Ministers of 21 July 1989 and the decree of the President of the Republic of 25 July 1991, the first renewal is carried out within fifteen years from the date of entry into force of the fifth part of this decree or, if such authorizations are not compliant with the provisions of this title, within one year from the same date. In all cases of renewal, the operation of the plant or activity may continue if the operator, within sixty days of the adoption of the new general authorization, submits an application for adhesion accompanied, where necessary, by an adaptation project and if the competent authority does not deny the adhesion. In case of failure to submit the application within the foreseen term, the plant or activity is considered in operation without authorization for emissions.
4. The provisions of paragraphs 2 and 3 do not apply:
a) in the case of emission of carcinogenic, toxic for reproduction, or mutagenic substances or of substances of particularly high toxicity and cumulativeness, as identified by Part II of Annex I to the fifth part of this decree, or
b) in the case where the substances or preparations classified by legislative decree no. 52 of 3 February 1997, as carcinogenic, mutagenic, or toxic for reproduction, due to their VOC content, and to which risk phrases R45, R46, R49, R60, R61 have been assigned, are used in the plant or in the activity.
5. This title, with the exception of what is provided for in paragraph 1, does not apply to the plants and activities listed in Part I of Annex IV to the fifth part of this decree. This title also does not apply to plants intended for national defense nor to emissions from vents and air changes exclusively used for the protection and safety of work environments. The relevant provisions of Articles 276 and 277 apply exclusively to fuel distribution plants.

**Art. 273**
**Large combustion plants**
1. Annex II to the fifth part of this decree establishes, in relation to large combustion plants, the emission limit values, including those for multi-fuel plants, the methods for monitoring and controlling emissions, the criteria for verifying compliance with the limit values, and the hypotheses of abnormal operation or malfunction of the plants.
2. The emission limit values of Part II, sections 1 to 5, letter B, and section 6 of Annex II to the fifth part of this decree apply to new large combustion plants.
3. The emission limit values of Part II, sections 1 to 5, letter A, and section 6 of Annex II to the fifth part of this decree apply to large combustion plants prior to 2006 starting from 1 January 2008. Until that date, Articles 3, paragraph 1, 6, paragraph 2, and 14, comma 3, nonch gli Allegati 4, 5, 6 e 9 del decreto del Ministro dell'ambiente 8 maggio 1989. Sono fatti salvi i diversi termini previsti nel suddetto Allegato II.
4. Ai grandi impianti di combustione anteriori al 1988 i valori limite di emissione di cui alla parte II, sezioni da 1 a 5, lettera A, e sezioni 6 e 7 dell'Allegato II alla parte quinta del presente decreto si applicano a partire dal 1 gennaio 2008. Fino a tale data si applicano i valori limite di emissione per il biossido di zolfo, gli ossidi di azoto, le polveri e per i metalli e loro composti previsti dal decreto del Ministro dell'ambiente 12 luglio 1990, o contenuti nelle autorizzazioni rilasciate ai sensi del decreto del Presidente della

---
Republic of May 24, 1988, no. 203, as well as the prescriptions relating to the anomalies of the abatement plants established in Annex II, part A, letter E, of the same ministerial decree. Until that date, the maximums and the emission reduction objectives, set in part V of Annex II to the fifth part of this decree, also apply. The different terms provided for in that Annex II are without prejudice.
5. The operators of the large combustion plants referred to in paragraph 4 may be exempted from the obligation to observe the emission limit values provided for in part II, sections 1 to 5, letter A, and section 6 of Annex II to the fifth part of this decree, on the basis of the procedure governed by part I of the same Annex II.
6. For the purposes of adapting the plants referred to in paragraphs 3 and 4 to the emission limit values provided for therein, the operator, within the scope of the request for integrated environmental authorization, shall present to the competent authority a technical report containing the description of the plant, the technologies adopted to prevent pollution, and the quality and quantity of the emissions, from which compliance with the prescriptions of this title results, or an adaptation project aimed at respecting the same.
7. For plants with a nominal thermal power of 50 MW, the technical report or the adaptation project referred to in paragraph 6 must be submitted by August 1, 2007 and, in case of approval, the competent authority shall, pursuant to Article 269, update the existing authorizations.
8. In addition to what is provided for in Article 271, paragraph 14, the emission limit values do not apply to large combustion plants in cases of abnormal operation provided for in part I of Annex II to the fifth part of this decree, in compliance with the conditions provided therein.
9. In the event that the competent authority, when issuing the authorization, considers that two or more combustion plants, new or prior to 2006, also with a nominal thermal power of less than 50 MW, are installed at the same time and in such a way that the gaseous effluents, taking into account the technical and economic conditions, can be channelled towards a single chimney, the same considers the set of these new plants as a single plant whose nominal thermal power is equal to the sum of the nominal thermal powers of these plants. This provision applies only if the sum of the thermal powers is greater than or equal to 50 MW.
10. If a combustion plant is expanded with the construction of an additional plant having a nominal thermal power of 50 MW or more, to this additional plant, excluding the cases provided for in part I, paragraph 3, points 3.3 and 3.4, of Annex II to the fifth part of this decree, the emission limit values established in the same Annex II, sections 1 to 5, letter B, apply, as a function of the total thermal power of the two plants.
11. In the case where a large combustion plant is subject to modifications qualified as substantial by the current legislation on integrated environmental authorization, the emission limit values established in part II, sections 1 to 5, letter B, and section 6 of Annex II to the fifth part of this decree apply.
12. Without prejudice to what is provided for by the current legislation on integrated environmental authorization, for new plants or in the case of modifications pursuant to paragraph 11, the authorization application must be accompanied by a specific study concerning the technical and economic feasibility of the combined generation of heat and electricity. In the case where this feasibility is ascertained, also in light of elements other than those contained in the study, the competent authority, taking into account the market and distribution situation, shall condition the issuance of the authorization measure to the immediate or deferred realization of this solution.
13. After January 1, 2008, for combustion plants with a nominal thermal power of less than 50MW and for other plants excluded from the scope of application of the fifth part of this decree, which are part of a refinery, the emission limit values of part IV, paragraph 1, of Annex I to the fifth part of this decree shall continue to apply, without prejudice to what is provided for by the current legislation on integrated environmental authorization, calculated as a weighted ratio between the sum of the masses of pollutants emitted and the sum of the emission volumes of all the refinery's plants, including those falling within the scope of application of this article.
14. In case of realization of large combustion plants that could cause significant prejudice to the environment of another Member State of the European Community, the competent authority shall inform the Ministry of the Environment and Protection of the Territory for

---
the fulfillment of the obligations of the convention on the assessment of environmental impact in a transboundary context, stipulated in Espoo on 25 February 1991, ratified by law no. 640 of 3 November 1994.
15. The provisions of this article apply to combustion plants intended for the production of energy, with the exception of those that directly use the products of combustion in manufacturing processes. The following are particularly excluded:
a) plants in which the products of combustion are used for direct heating, drying, or any other treatment of objects or materials, such as reheating furnaces or heat treatment furnaces;
b) post-combustion plants, i.e., any technical device for the purification of gaseous effluent by combustion, which is not operated as an independent combustion plant;
c) catalytic cracking catalyst regeneration devices;
d) hydrogen sulfide to sulfur conversion devices;
e) reactors used in the chemical industry;
f) batteries of coke ovens;
g) cowpers of blast furnaces;
h) any technical device used for the propulsion of a vehicle, a ship, or an aircraft;
i) gas turbines used on off-shore platforms and on off-shore liquefied natural gas regasification plants;
l) gas turbines authorized before the date of entry into force of the fifth part of this decree, without prejudice to the provisions expressly referring to them;
m) plants powered by diesel, petrol, or gas engines.

**Art. 274**
**Collection and transmission of data on emissions from large combustion plants**
1. The Ministry of the Environment and Protection of the Territory shall transmit to the European Commission, every three years, a report concerning the emissions of sulfur dioxide, nitrogen oxides, and dust from all large combustion plants referred to in the fifth part of this decree, in which the emissions of the refineries are separately indicated. This report is transmitted for the first time by 31 December 2007 in relation to the three-year period that begins on 1 January 2004 and, subsequently, within twelve months of the end of each subsequent three-year period under examination. The Ministry of the Environment and Protection of the Territory shall also transmit to the European Commission, upon request, the annual data relating to the emissions of sulfur dioxide, nitrogen oxides, and dust from the individual combustion plants.
2. Starting from 1 January 2008, the Ministry of the Environment and Protection of the Territory shall submit a report to the European Commission each year concerning the plants prior to 1988 for which the exemption provided for in Article 273, paragraph 5, has been granted, indicating the used and unused times that have been authorized for the remaining operating period of the plants. To this end, the competent authority, if different from the Ministry of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, shall communicate to this Ministry the aforementioned exemptions at the same time as they are granted.
3. The Ministry of the Environment and Protection of the Territory shall submit a report to the European Commission each year regarding the cases in which the derogations of part II, sections 1 and 4, letter A, paragraph 2, of Annex II to the fifth part of this decree are applied, and the derogations of the notes of letters A and B of the same Annex II, part II, section 1. To this end, the competent authority, if different from the Ministry of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, shall communicate to this Ministry the aforementioned derogations at the same time as their application.
4. By 31 May of each year, starting from 2006, the operators of large combustion plants shall communicate to the Agency for the Protection of the Environment and for Technical Services (APAT), with the methods provided for in part III of Annex II to the fifth part of this decree, the total emissions, relating to the previous year, of sulfur dioxide, nitrogen oxides, and dust, determined in accordance with the prescriptions of part IV of Annex II to the fifth part of this decree, as well as the total annual quantity of energy produced respectively from biomass, from other solid fuels, from liquid fuels, from natural gas, and from other gases, referred to the net calorific value, and the characterization of the emission abatement systems. In case of failure to

---
communication of the data and information referred to in this paragraph, the Ministry of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, also for the purposes of what is provided for by art. 650 of the penal code, shall order the non-compliant operator to comply.
5. The Agency for the Protection of the Environment and for Technical Services (APAT), on the basis of the information referred to in paragraph 4, shall prepare a report in which the emissions of sulfur dioxide, nitrogen oxides, and dust from all large combustion plants referred to in the fifth part of this decree are reported. This report must indicate the total annual emissions of sulfur dioxide, nitrogen oxides, and dust, and the total annual quantity of energy produced respectively from biomass, from other solid fuels, from liquid fuels, from natural gas, and from other gases, referred to the net calorific value. At least two months before the deadline provided for in paragraph 1 for the transmission of the data to the European Commission, the Agency for the Protection of the Environment and for Technical Services (APAT) shall transmit to the Ministry of the Environment and Protection of the Territory the aforementioned report, as well as the disaggregated data relating to each plant.
6. The data referred to in paragraph 4 shall be collected and sent in electronic format. To this end, the procedures indicated on the website of the Ministry of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, where available, must be observed. The report referred to in paragraph 5, as well as the disaggregated data collected by the Agency for the Protection of the Environment and for Technical Services (APAT) shall be made available to the competent authorities on the website of the Ministry of the Environment and Protection of the Territory.

**Art. 275**
**VOC emissions**
1. Annex III to the fifth part of this decree establishes, with regard to volatile organic compound emissions, the emission limit values, the methods for monitoring and controlling emissions, the criteria for evaluating the conformity of the measured values to the limit values, and the methods for preparing the solvent management plan.
2. If in the same place one or more activities identified in part II of Annex III to the fifth part of this decree, which individually exceed the solvent consumption thresholds established therein, are carried out by means of one or more plants or machinery and non-fixed systems or manual operations, the limit values for channelled emissions and for diffuse emissions of the same Annex III, part III, or the total emission limit values of that Annex III, parts III and IV, as well as the prescriptions provided therein, shall apply to each of these activities. This provision also applies to activities which, in the same place, are directly and technically connected to the activities identified in the aforementioned Annex III, part II, and which may influence VOC emissions. The exceedance of the solvent consumption thresholds is evaluated with reference to the maximum theoretical solvent consumption authorized. The activities referred to in part II of Annex III to the fifth part of this decree include the cleaning of equipment and do not include the cleaning of products, without prejudice to the different provisions provided therein.
3. For the purposes of what is provided for in paragraph 2, the limit values for channelled emissions apply to each plant that produces such emissions, and the limit values for diffuse emissions apply to the sum of the non-channelled emissions of all the plants, of all the machinery and non-fixed systems, and of all the operations.
4. The operator who intends to carry out the activities referred to in paragraph 2 shall submit to the competent authority an authorization application in accordance with what is provided for in part I of Annex III to the fifth part of this decree. For this purpose, Article 269 shall apply, with the exception of paragraphs 2 and 4. In addition to the cases provided for by Article 269, paragraph 8, the authorization application must also be submitted by the operator of the activities who, as a result of a modification of the maximum theoretical solvent consumption, falls within those of paragraph 2.
5. The authorization covers the plants, machinery and non-fixed systems, and manual operations that carry out the activities of paragraph 2 and establishes, on the basis of that paragraph, the limit values that must be respected. Article 270 applies for capture and channelling. For emissions produced by machinery and non-fixed systems or by manual operations, paragraphs 10, 11, and 13 of Article 269 apply.
6. The authorization indicates the maximum theoretical solvent consumption and the total annual emission resulting from the application of the limit values of paragraph 2, identified on the

---
basis of this consumption, as well as the frequency of updating the management plan referred to in part V of Annex III to the fifth part of this decree.
7. Compliance with the emission limit values provided for in paragraph 2 is ensured through the application of the best available techniques and, in particular, by using raw materials with a low or zero content of organic solvents, optimizing the operation and management of the activities and, where necessary, installing suitable abatement devices, in order to minimize the emissions of volatile organic compounds.
8. If the activities of paragraph 2 are carried out by one or more plants authorized before March 13, 2004, or by such plants jointly with machinery and non-fixed systems or manual operations, the emissions must be adapted to the relevant prescriptions of Annex III to the fifth part of this decree and to the other prescriptions of this article by October 31, 2007, or, in case of adaptation to what is provided for by the same Annex III, part IV, within the dates established therein. Without prejudice to what is established by the current legislation on integrated environmental authorization, the adaptation is carried out on the basis of the projects submitted to the competent authority pursuant to the ministerial decree of January 14, 2004, no. 44. The plants thus authorized are considered to be prior to 2006. In case of failure to submit the project or of denial of the approval of the project by the competent authority, the activities are considered to be in operation without authorization. The adaptation terms provided for in this paragraph also apply to the plants of paragraph 20, in operation on March 12, 2004, whose operators adhere to the general authorization provided for therein within six months of the entry into force of the fifth part of this decree or have previously adhered to the general authorizations adopted pursuant to art. 9 of the decree of the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory of January 16, 2004, no. 44.
9. If the activities of paragraph 2 are carried out exclusively by machinery and non-fixed systems or by manual operations, in operation before the entry into force of the fifth part of this decree, the emissions must be adapted to the relevant prescriptions of Annex III to the fifth part of this decree and to the other prescriptions of this article by October 31, 2007. To this end, the authorization of paragraph 4 must be requested within six months of the date of entry into force of the fifth part of this decree. In case of failure to submit the request within this term, the activities are considered to be in operation without authorization.
10. Authorizations issued before March 13, 2004, which achieve greater containment of volatile organic compound emissions than that obtainable with the application of the indications of parts III and VI of Annex III to the fifth part of this decree, are without prejudice. In this case, the sampling and analysis methods previously in use remain valid. The right of the operator to request the competent authority to review these authorizations on the basis of the provisions of the fifth part of this decree is without prejudice.
11. The authorization application referred to in paragraph 4 must also be submitted by the operator of the activities referred to in paragraph 2, carried out pursuant to paragraphs 8 and 9, where the same are subject to substantial modifications. The authorization prescribes that the emissions of the plants, systems and non-fixed machinery, and manual operations subject to substantial modification:
a) are immediately adapted to the prescriptions of this article or
b) are adapted to the prescriptions of this article by October 31, 2007, if the total emissions of all the activities carried out by the operator in the same place do not exceed those that occur in the case of application of letter a).
12. If the operator proves to the competent authority that, despite using the best available technique, it is not possible to respect the limit value for diffuse emissions, this authority may authorize derogations from this limit value, provided that this does not entail risks to human health or the environment.
13. In the cases provided for in part III of Annex III to the fifth part of this decree, the competent authority may exempt the operator from applying the prescriptions established therein if the emissions cannot be channelled pursuant to Article 270, paragraphs 1 and 2. In this case, what is provided for in part IV of Annex III to the fifth part of this decree applies, unless the operator proves to the competent authority that compliance with this Annex is not, in the specific case, technically and economically feasible and that the plant uses the best available technique.
14. The competent authority shall communicate to the Ministry of the Environment and Protection of the Territory,

---
in the report referred to in paragraph 18, the derogations authorized pursuant to paragraphs 12 and 13.
15. If two or more activities carried out in the same place individually exceed the thresholds of paragraph 2, the competent authority may:
a) apply the limit values provided for by that paragraph to each single activity or
b) apply a total emission value, referring to the sum of the emissions of these activities, not higher than that which would be obtained by applying what is provided for in letter a); this option does not extend to the emissions of the substances indicated in paragraph 17.
16. The operator who, in the cases provided for by paragraph 8, uses an abatement device that allows compliance with an emission limit value of 50 mgC/Nm3, in case of combustion, and 150 mgC/Nm3, in all other cases, must respect the limit values for channelled emissions of part III of Annex III to the fifth part of this decree by April 1, 2013, provided that the total emissions do not exceed those that would have been produced in case of application of the prescriptions of part III of Annex III to the fifth part of this decree.
17. Part I of Annex III to the fifth part of this decree establishes specific emission limit values for substances characterized by particular risks to health and the environment.
18. The competent authorities shall transmit to the Ministry of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, every three years and by April 30, starting from 2005, a report on the application of this article, in accordance with what is provided for by decision 2002/529/EC of June 27, 2002 of the European Commission. A copy of the report is sent by the competent authorities to the region or autonomous province. The Ministry of the Environment and Protection of the Territory sends this information to the European Commission.
19. For VOC emissions from plants prior to 1988, regulated by this article, the limit values and prescriptions of Annex I to the fifth part of this decree shall apply until the dates provided for in paragraphs 8 and 9 or until the date of effective adaptation of the plants, if earlier.
20. The operators of closed-cycle plants for dry cleaning of fabrics and furs, excluding furs, and of closed-cycle laundries, for which the competent authority has not adopted general authorizations, shall communicate to such authorities their adhesion to the authorization of part VII of Annex III to the fifth part of this decree. The power of the same authorities to subsequently adopt new general authorizations, pursuant to Article 272, the adhesion to which entails, for the interested party, the lapse of that provided for in part VII of Annex III to the fifth part of this decree with respect to the territory to which such new authorizations refer, is without prejudice. The prescriptions of part I, paragraph 3, points 3.2, 3.3, and 3.4 of Annex III to the fifth part of this decree do not apply to such activities.
21. The following constitutes a substantial modification, pursuant to this article:
a) for small-scale activities, a modification of the maximum theoretical solvent consumption that entails an increase in volatile organic compound emissions by more than twenty-five percent;
b) for all other activities, a modification of the maximum theoretical solvent consumption that entails an increase in volatile organic compound emissions by more than ten percent;
c) any modification which, in the opinion of the competent authority, could have significant negative effects on human health or the environment;
d) any modification of the maximum theoretical solvent consumption that entails a change in the applicable limit values;
22. For small-scale activities, pursuant to paragraph 21, the activities referred to in part III, points 1, 3, 4, 5, 8, 10, 13, 16, or 17 of Annex III to the fifth part of this decree having a maximum theoretical solvent consumption less than or equal to the lower of the consumption thresholds indicated therein in the third column and the other activities of part III of the same Annex III having a maximum theoretical solvent consumption of less than 10 tons per year are intended.

**Art. 276**
**Control of VOC emissions resulting from the storage of gasoline and its distribution from terminals to distribution plants**
1. Annex VII to the fifth part of this decree establishes the prescriptions that

---
must be respected for the control of VOC emissions relating to:
a) storage plants at terminals;
b) gasoline loading plants at terminals;
c) plants used for the temporary storage of vapors at terminals;
d) mobile tanks and road tankers;
e) storage plants at fuel distribution plants;
f) equipment for gasoline transfer operations at distribution plants and at terminals where temporary vapor storage is permitted.
2. For the purposes of this article, storage plants are understood to be fixed tanks used for the storage of gasoline. For such storage plants located at terminals, the relevant prescriptions of Annex VII to the fifth part of this decree constitute the measures that operators must adopt pursuant to Article 269, paragraph 16. With a specific provision, the competent authority may grant derogations from these prescriptions, relating to cladding obligations, where necessary for the protection of areas of particular value from a landscape perspective.
3. For the purposes of this article, distribution plants are understood to be plants where gasoline is dispensed to the tanks of all motor vehicles from storage plants.
4. In terminals within which a quantity of gasoline of less than 10,000 tons/year is handled and whose construction was authorized before December 3, 1997, pursuant to the legislation in force at the time of authorization, the loading plants shall adapt to the provisions of part II, paragraph 2, of Annex VII to the fifth part of this decree by May 17, 2010. Until the date of adaptation, the accessibility of loading operations must be guaranteed also for road tankers with top loading. For the quantity handled, the maximum total annual quantity of gasoline loaded into mobile tanks from the terminal's storage plants in the three years preceding May 17, 2000 is intended.
5. The prescriptions of part II, point 3.2, of Annex VII to the fifth part of this decree apply to road tankers tested after November 17, 2000 and extend to other road tankers starting from May 17, 2010. These prescriptions do not apply to road tankers with calibrated compartments, tested after January 1, 1990 and equipped with a device that guarantees complete vapor tightness during the loading phase. For such road tankers with calibrated compartments, the accessibility of loading operations at the terminal's storage plants must be permitted.

**Art. 277**
**Recovery of VOCs produced during the refuelling of motor vehicles at fuel distribution plants**
1. The distributors of fuel distribution plants must be equipped with vapor recovery systems for gasoline that are produced during the refuelling of motor vehicles. The distribution plants and the vapor recovery systems must comply with the relevant prescriptions of Annex VIII to the fifth part of this decree, relating to efficiency requirements, construction requirements, installation requirements, periodic checks, and documentation obligations.
2. For the purposes of this article, the following definitions apply:
a) distribution plants: any plant where gasoline is dispensed to the tanks of motor vehicles from storage plants;
b) storage plants: the fixed tanks used for the storage of gasoline at distribution plants;
c) dispenser: any apparatus intended for the dispensing of gasoline; the dispenser must be equipped with a suitable dispensing pump capable of drawing from the storage plants or, alternatively, be connected to a centralized pumping system; if inserted in a fuel distribution plant in relation to the public, the dispenser must also be equipped with a suitable device for indicating and calculating the quantities of gasoline dispensed;
d) vapor recovery system: the set of devices designed to prevent the emission into the atmosphere of VOCs during the refuelling of motor vehicles. This set of devices includes dispensing nozzles designed for vapor recovery, coaxial or twin flexible hoses, splitters for separating the vapor line from the fuel dispensing line, internal connections to the dispensers, underground lines for the passage of vapors to the tanks, and all the equipment and

---
devices to ensure the functioning of the plants in conditions of safety and efficiency.
3. The component devices of the vapor recovery systems must be approved by the Ministry of the Interior, to which the manufacturer submits a specific request accompanied by the necessary documentation to identify the devices and by the certification referred to in paragraph 2, point 2.3, of Annex VIII to the fifth part of this decree. For the purpose of issuing the approval, the Ministry of the Interior verifies the conformity of the devices to the efficiency requirements of paragraph 1 and to the fire safety requirements of the ministerial decree of July 31, 1934. In case of no decision, the approval is considered denied.
4. The component devices of the vapor recovery systems that have been approved by the competent authorities of other countries belonging to the European Union may be used to equip the distributors of the distribution plants, subject to recognition by the Ministry of the Interior, to which the manufacturer submits a specific request, accompanied by the necessary documentation to identify the devices, by the test certifications issued by the competent foreign authorities, and by a sworn translation into Italian of these documents and certifications. For the purpose of recognition, the Ministry of the Interior verifies the transmitted documents and certifications and the conformity of the devices to the fire safety requirements of the ministerial decree of July 31, 1934. In case of no decision, the recognition is considered denied.
5. During the refuelling of motor vehicles, the operators of the distribution plants must keep the vapor recovery systems of paragraph 1 in operation.

**Art. 278**
**Powers of ordinance**
1. In case of non-compliance with the prescriptions contained in the authorization, without prejudice to the application of the sanctions of Article 279 and the precautionary measures ordered by the judicial authority, the competent authority proceeds, according to the seriousness of the infringement:
a) to a warning, with the assignment of a term within which the irregularities must be eliminated;
b) to a warning and the simultaneous suspension of the authorized activity for a determined period, where situations of danger to health or the environment arise;
c) to the revocation of the authorization and the closure of the plant or the cessation of the activity, in case of failure to adapt to the prescriptions imposed with the warning or if the repeated non-compliance with the prescriptions contained in the authorization determines situations of danger or damage to health or the environment.

**Art. 279**
**Sanctions**
1. Whoever begins to install or operate a plant and who carries out an activity in the absence of the prescribed authorization or continues the operation of the plant or activity with an expired, lapsed, suspended, revoked authorization or after the order of closure of the plant or cessation of the activity is punished with the penalty of arrest from two months to two years or a fine from two hundred and fifty-eight euros to one thousand and thirty-two euros. Whoever subjects a plant to a substantial modification without the authorization provided for by Article 269, paragraph 8, is punished with the penalty of arrest up to six months or a fine up to one thousand and thirty-two euros; whoever subjects a plant to a non-substantial modification without making the communication provided for by the said Article 269, paragraph 8, is punished with a fine up to one thousand euros.
2. Whoever, in the exercise of a plant or an activity, violates the emission limit values or the prescriptions established by the authorization, by Annex I to the fifth part of this decree, by the plans and programs, or by the legislation of Article 271, or the prescriptions otherwise imposed by the competent authority pursuant to this title is punished with arrest up to one year or a fine up to one thousand and thirty-two euros.
3. Whoever puts a plant into operation or begins to carry out an activity without having given the prior communication prescribed pursuant to Article 269, paragraph 5 or paragraph 15, or pursuant to Article 272, paragraph 1, is punished with arrest up to one year or with a fine up to one thousand and thirty-two euros.

---
4. Whoever fails to communicate to the competent authority the data relating to emissions pursuant to Article 269, paragraph 5, is punished with arrest up to six months or with a fine up to one thousand and thirty-two euros.
5. In the cases provided for in paragraph 2, the penalty of arrest up to one year always applies if the exceedance of the emission limit values also determines the exceedance of the air quality limit values provided for by the current legislation.
6. Whoever, in the cases provided for by Article 281, paragraph 1, fails to take all necessary measures to avoid an increase, even temporary, of emissions is punished with the penalty of arrest up to one year or a fine up to one thousand and thirty-two euros.
7. For the violation of the prescriptions of Article 276, in the case where the same is not subject to the sanctions provided for in paragraphs 1 to 6, and for the violation of the prescriptions of Article 277, an administrative pecuniary sanction from fifteen thousand four hundred and ninety-three euros to one hundred and fifty-four thousand nine hundred and thirty-seven euros applies. The region or the different authority indicated by the regional law shall impose this sanction, pursuant to Articles 17 and following of law no. 689 of 24 November 1981. The suspension of the existing authorizations is always ordered in case of recidivism.

**Art. 280**
**Repeals**
1. The following are repealed, excluding the provisions for which this decree provides for their continued validity and without prejudice to what is established by art. 14 of legislative decree no. 351 of 4 August 1999:
a) the decree of the President of the Republic no. 203 of 24 May 1988;
b) art. 4 of law no. 413 of 4 November 1997;
c) art. 12, paragraph 8, of legislative decree no. 387 of 29 December 2003;
d) the decree of the Minister of the Environment no. 105 of 10 March 1987;
e) the decree of the Minister of the Environment of 8 May 1989;
f) the decree of the President of the Council of Ministers of 21 July 1989;
g) the decree of the Minister of the Environment of 12 July 1990;
h) the decree of the President of the Republic of 25 July 1991;
i) the decree of the Minister of the Environment of 21 December 1995;
l) the decree of the Minister of the Environment of 16 May 1996;
m) the decree of the Minister of the Environment no. 76 of 20 January 1999;
n) the decree of the Minister of the Environment no. 107 of 21 January 2000;
o) the decree of the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory no. 44 of 16 January 2004.

**Art. 281**
**Transitional and final provisions**
1. The operators of plants authorized, also provisionally or tacitly, pursuant to the decree of the President of the Republic no. 203 of 24 May 1988, with the exclusion of those equipped with a general authorization which are subject to the discipline of Article 272, paragraph 3, must submit an authorization application pursuant to Article 269 within the terms indicated below. The regions and autonomous provinces shall adopt, in compliance with these terms, specific calendars for the submission of applications; in case of failure to adopt the calendars, the authorization application must in any case be submitted within the terms established by this paragraph. The failure to submit the application within the terms, including those set by the calendars, entails the lapse of the previous authorization. If the application is submitted within the terms, the operation of the plants may be continued until the decision of the competent authority; in case of no decision within the terms provided for by Article 269, paragraph 3, the operation may be continued until the expiry of the term provided for the decision of the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory who has been requested to provide for it pursuant to the same article. In the case of plants authorized provisionally or tacitly, the operator must adopt, until the decision of the competent authority, all the necessary measures to avoid an increase, even temporary, of emissions. The authorization application of this paragraph must be submitted within the following terms:
a) between the date of entry into force of the fifth part of this decree and 31 December 2010, for plants prior to 1988;
b) between 1 January 2011 and 31 December 2014, for plants prior to 2006 that were authorized before 1 January 2000;
c) between 1 January 2015 and 31 December 2018, for plants prior to 2006 that were authorized after 31 December 1999.
2. The operators of plants and activities in operation at the date of entry into force of the fifth part of this decree that fall within the scope of application of this title and did not fall within the scope of application of the decree of the President of the Republic no. 203 of 24 May 1988, shall adapt to the provisions of this title within three years from that date and, in the case where they are subject to authorization for emissions, shall submit the relative application, pursuant to Article 269 or pursuant to Article 272, paragraphs 2 and 3, at least eighteen months before the adaptation deadline. In case of failure to submit the application within the provided term, the plant or activity is considered in operation without authorization for emissions. If the application is submitted within the provided term, the operation may be continued until the decision of the competent authority; in case of no decision within the terms provided for by Article 269, paragraph 3, the operation may be continued until the expiry of the term provided for the decision of the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory who has been requested to provide for it pursuant to the same article. For the plants, the authorization establishes the limit values and prescriptions:
a) pursuant to Article 271, paragraphs 6 and 9, if the plant was built before 1988 in accordance with the legislation in force at the time;
b) pursuant to Article 271, paragraphs 8 and 9, if the plant must be built pursuant to Article 269, paragraphs 10 or 12, or was built between 1988 and the entry into force of the fifth part of this decree in accordance with the legislation in force at the time.
3.
