For plants in operation at the date of entry into force of the fifth part of this decree that fall within the scope of application of this title and that fell within the scope of application of law no. 615 of 13 July 1966, of the decree of the President of the Republic no. 1391 of 22 December 1970, or of title II of the decree of the President of the Council of Ministers of 8 March 2002, the competent authority shall adopt the general authorizations of Article 272, paragraph 2, within fifteen months from that date. In case of failure to adopt the general authorization, within the prescribed term, the same is issued with a specific decree of the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory and the operators of the interested plants communicate their adhesion to the competent authority; the power of this authority to subsequently adopt new general authorizations, pursuant to Article 272, the adhesion to which entails, for the interested party, the lapse of that adopted by the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, is without prejudice.
4. The operators of plants and activities that fell within annexes 1 and 2 of the decree of the President of the Republic of 25 July 1991 and that, by effect of the fifth part of this decree, are required to obtain a specific authorization for emissions, shall submit the relative request within fifteen months of the entry into force of the fifth part of this decree; in this case, if the plant is subject to Article 275, the competent authority shall issue the authorization on the basis of the projects submitted pursuant to paragraph 8 of the same article, with the terms provided for in Article 269, paragraph 3, starting from the date of entry into force of the fifth part of this decree. In case of failure to submit the application within the provided term, the plant or activity is considered in operation without authorization for emissions. If the application is submitted within the provided term, the operation of such plants or activities may be continued until the decision of the competent authority; in case of no decision within the terms provided for by Article 269, paragraph 3, the operation may be continued until the expiry of the term provided for the decision of the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory who has been requested to provide for it pursuant to the same article.
5. The integration and modification of the annexes to the fifth part of this decree shall be carried out by the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, with the methods of Article 3, paragraph 2, in concert with the Minister of Health and with the Minister of Production Activities, after consulting the Unified Conference of Article 8 of legislative decree no. 281 of 28 August 1997. The adoption of such acts shall also be carried out in concert with the Minister of Agricultural and Forestry Policies, with regard to emissions from agricultural activities, and in concert with the Ministers of the Interior, of Infrastructure and Transport, and of Economy and Finance, with regard to the modification of Annexes VII and VIII to the fifth part of this decree. Annex I and Annex VI to the fifth part of this decree are integrated and modified for the first time within one year of the entry into force of the fifth part of the same decree.
6. The modification and integration of the Annexes to the fifth part of this decree, in order to implement the community directives for the parts in which they involve modifications of the executive modalities and of the technical characteristics established by the current rules, shall be carried out pursuant to art. 13 of law no. 11 of 4 February 2005.
7. The authorization applications, the measures adopted by the competent authority, and the results of the control activities, pursuant to this title, as well as the lists of authorized activities in the possession of the competent authority, are made available to the public pursuant to the provisions of legislative decree no. 195 of 19 August 2005.
8. The State, the regions, the autonomous provinces, and the provinces shall organize their respective inventories of emission sources. The criteria for the elaboration of these inventories are established by decree of the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, in concert with the Minister of Production Activities and with the Minister of Health.
9. By decree of the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, in concert with the Minister of Economy and Finance, a commission for the collection, processing, and dissemination, among the competent authorities, of the data and information relevant for the application of the fifth part of this decree and for the evaluation of the best available techniques of Article 268, paragraph 1, letter aa), is established, without charges on public finance. The commission is composed of a representative appointed by the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, with the functions of president, a representative appointed by the Minister of Production Activities, a representative appointed by the Minister of Health, and five representatives appointed by the Unified Conference of Article 8 of legislative decree no. 281 of 28 August 1997. One or more representatives of each region or autonomous province may participate in the meetings of the Commission. The establishing decree also regulates the operating methods of the commission, including the frequency of the meetings, and the methods of participation of subjects other than the components. No compensation, allowances, emoluments of any kind, or expense reimbursements are due to the members of the commission and to the other subjects who participate in its meetings.
10. Without prejudice to the powers established by Article 271 in the adoption of the plans and programs provided for therein and in the issuance of the authorization, in the presence of particular situations of health risk or zones that require particular environmental protection, the regions and autonomous provinces, with a general measure, after agreement with the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory and with the Minister of Health, for what concerns them, may establish emission limit values and prescriptions, also concerning the construction or operating conditions of the plants, more severe than those set by the annexes to this title, provided that this is necessary for the achievement of the limit values and target values of air quality.

**TITLE II - CIVIL THERMAL PLANTS**

**Art. 282**
**Scope of application**
1. This title regulates, for the purposes of prevention and limitation of atmospheric pollution, civil thermal plants with a nominal thermal power lower than the relevant thresholds established by Article 269, paragraph 14. Civil thermal plants with a nominal thermal power equal to or greater than these thresholds and civil thermal plants that use steam coal, metallurgical coke, gas coke, anthracite, anthracitic products, or mixtures of anthracite and anthracitic products, with a nominal thermal power greater than 3 MW, are subject to the provisions of Title I.

**Art. 283**
**Definitions**
1. For the purposes of this title, the following definitions apply:
a) thermal plant: plant intended for the production of heat consisting of one or more heat generators and a single system for the distribution and utilization of this heat, as well as specific regulation and control devices;
b) heat generator: any combustion device powered by fuels for the purpose of producing hot water or steam, consisting of a firebox, a heat exchanger, and a burner;
c) firebox: part of a heat generator in which the combustion process takes place;
d) civil thermal plant: thermal plant whose heat production is intended, also in non-residential buildings, for the heating or air conditioning of environments or for the heating of water for hygienic and sanitary uses; the civil thermal plant is centralized if it serves all the units of the building or of several buildings and is individual in other cases;
e) nominal thermal power of the plant: the sum of the nominal thermal powers of the individual fireboxes constituting the plant;
f) nominal thermal power of the firebox: the product of the lower calorific value of the fuel used and the maximum flow rate of fuel burned within the firebox, expressed in thermal watts or its multiples;
g) threshold value: nominal thermal power of the plant equal to 0.035MW;
h) modification of the plant: any intervention that involves a variation of the data contained in the report of Article 284 or in the documentation submitted pursuant to Articles 9 and 10 of law no. 615 of 13 July 1966;
i) competent authority: the municipalities with a population greater than forty thousand inhabitants and, in the remaining part of the territory, the provinces;
l) installer: the subject indicated in art. 108 of the decree of the President of the Republic no. 380 of 6 June 2001;
m) person responsible for the operation and maintenance of the plant: the subject indicated in art. 11, paragraph 1, of the decree of the President of the Republic no. 412 of 26 August 1993;
n) operation of a thermal plant: the set of operations necessary to ensure correct combustion in the fireboxes and the adaptation of the thermal plant's regime to the heat demand.

**Art. 284**
**Report of installation or modification**
1. In case of installation or modification of a civil thermal plant with a nominal thermal power greater than the threshold value, a specific report, prepared by the installer using the form in part I of Annex IX to the fifth part of this decree and made available by him to the person required to transmit it, must be transmitted to the competent authority within ninety days of the intervention. For installations and modifications subsequent to the term provided for by Article 286, paragraph 4, this report is accompanied by the documentation relating to the verification carried out pursuant to the same article. The report is transmitted by the person responsible for the operation and maintenance of the plant. In the case of individual thermal plants, if the person responsible for the operation and maintenance is not the owner or the possessor or their delegate, the report is transmitted by the owner or, if different, by the possessor and is made available by him to the person responsible for the operation and maintenance.
2. For civil thermal plants with a nominal thermal power greater than the threshold value, in operation at the date of entry into force of the fifth part of this decree, a specific report, prepared by the person responsible for the operation and maintenance of the plant using the form in part I of Annex IX to the fifth part of this decree, accompanied by the documents attached to the plant logbook pursuant to Article 286, paragraph 2, must be transmitted to the competent authority within one year of that date. The report is transmitted by the person responsible for the operation and maintenance of the plant. In the case of individual thermal plants, if the person responsible for the operation and maintenance is not the owner or the possessor or their delegate, the report is made available to the owner or, if different, to the possessor, who shall carry out the transmission. This paragraph does not apply to civil thermal plants for which the procedure provided for by Articles 9 and 10 of law no. 615 of 13 July 1966 has been completed.

**Art. 285**
**Technical characteristics**
1. Civil thermal plants with a nominal thermal power greater than the threshold value must comply with the technical characteristics provided for in part II of Annex IX to the fifth part of this decree relevant to the type of fuel used.

**Art. 286**
**Emission limit values**
1. The atmospheric emissions of civil thermal plants with a nominal thermal power greater than the threshold value must respect the limit values provided for in part III of Annex IX to the fifth part of this decree.
2. The emission values of the plants of paragraph 1 must be checked at least annually by the person responsible for the operation and maintenance of the plant during the normal control and maintenance operations. The measured values, with an indication of the relative dates, the measurement methods used, and the subject who carried out the measurement, must be attached to the plant logbook provided for by the decree of the President of the Republic of 26 August 1993, no. 412. This annual check of the emission values is not required in the cases provided for in part III, section 1 of Annex IX to the fifth part of this decree. The documents attesting to the performance of the maintenance necessary to guarantee compliance with the emission limit values provided for by the report of Article 284 must also be attached to the plant logbook.
3. For the purposes of sampling, analysis, and evaluation of the emissions of the thermal plants of paragraph 1, the methods provided for in part III of Annex IX to the fifth part of this decree apply.
4. As of one hundred and eighty days from the date of entry into force of the fifth part of this decree, the installer, at the time of the installation or modification of the plant, shall verify compliance with the emission limit values provided for by this article.

**Art. 287**
**Authorization to operate**
1. The personnel assigned to the operation of civil thermal plants with a nominal thermal power greater than 0.232 MW must be in possession of an operating license issued by the provincial Labour Inspectorate, at the end of a course for the operation of thermal plants, after passing the final exam. The licenses can be issued to persons aged no less than eighteen years. At each provincial Labour Inspectorate, a register of those authorized to operate thermal plants is compiled and updated, a copy of which is also kept at the competent authority and at the provincial command of the fire brigade.
2. The provisions of art. 11, paragraph 3, of the decree of the President of the Republic of 26 August 1993, no. 412 remain unaffected.
3. For the purposes of paragraph 1, two grades of authorization are provided. The first-grade license authorizes the operation of thermal plants for which the certificate of authorization for the operation of steam generators under the royal decree of 12 May 1927, no. 824, is required, and the second-grade license authorizes the operation of other plants. The first-grade license also authorizes the operation of plants for which the second-grade license is required.
4. The possession of an authorization certificate of any grade for the operation of steam generators, pursuant to the royal decree of 12 May 1927, no. 824, allows the issuance of the license without the need for the exam referred to in paragraph 1.
5. The license can be revoked at any time by the provincial Labour Inspectorate in case of irregular operation of the plant. To this end, the competent authority communicates to the Inspectorate the cases of irregular operation ascertained. The measure of suspension or revocation of the certificate of authorization for the operation of steam generators pursuant to articles 31 and 32 of the royal decree of 12 May 1927, no. 824, has no effect on the license referred to in this article.
6. The decree of the Minister for Labour and Social Security of 12 August 1968 establishes the discipline of the courses and exams referred to in paragraph 1 and of the revisions of the licenses. The modification and integration of this decree are provided for by decree of the Minister of Labour and Social Policies.

**Art. 288**
**Controls and sanctions**

---
1. The installer who, on the occasion of the installation or modification of a civil thermal plant, does not prepare the report referred to in Article 284, paragraph 1, or prepares an incomplete report, and the person required to transmit this report who, having received it, does not transmit it to the competent authority within the prescribed terms, is punished with an administrative pecuniary sanction from five hundred and sixteen euros to two thousand five hundred and eighty-two euros. The same sanction punishes the person responsible for the operation and maintenance of the plant who does not prepare the report referred to in Article 284, paragraph 2, or prepares an incomplete report, and the person required to transmit this report who, having received it, does not transmit it to the competent authority within the prescribed terms.
2. In case of operation of a civil thermal plant not compliant with the technical characteristics of Article 285, the following are punished with an administrative pecuniary sanction from five hundred and sixteen euros to two thousand five hundred and eighty-two euros:
a) the installer, where they are required to prepare the report of Article 284, paragraph 1;
b) the person responsible for the operation and maintenance of the plant, where they are required to prepare the report of Article 284, paragraph 2.
3. In the case where the plant does not respect the emission limit values of Article 286, paragraph 1, the following are punished with an administrative pecuniary sanction from five hundred and sixteen euros to two thousand five hundred and eighty-two euros:
a) the person responsible for the operation and maintenance, in all cases where the plant is not subject to the verification obligation of Article 286, paragraph 4;
b) the installer and the person responsible for the operation and maintenance, if compliance with the limit values has not been verified pursuant to Article 286, paragraph 4, or has not been declared in the report of Article 284, paragraph 1;
c) the installer, if compliance with the limit values has been verified pursuant to Article 286, paragraph 4, and declared in the report of Article 284, paragraph 1, and if from the plant logbook it appears that the controls and maintenance prescribed by the fifth part of this decree and by the decree of the President of the Republic of 26 August 1993, no. 412, are regularly carried out, provided that the duration established for the life cycle of the plant has not been exceeded;
d) the person responsible for the operation and maintenance, if compliance with the limit values has been verified pursuant to Article 286, paragraph 4, and declared in the report of Article 284, paragraph 1, and if from the plant logbook it does not appear that the prescribed controls and maintenance are regularly carried out or the duration established for the life cycle of the plant has been exceeded.
4. With an administrative pecuniary sanction from five hundred and sixteen euros to two thousand five hundred and eighty-two euros, the person responsible for the operation and maintenance of the plant who does not carry out the annual check of the emissions pursuant to Article 286, paragraph 2, or does not attach the data provided therein to the plant logbook, is punished.
5. Without prejudice to the application of the sanctions provided for in the preceding paragraphs and the sanctions provided for the production of false declarations or false attestations, the competent authority, where it ascertains that the plant does not respect the technical characteristics of Article 285 or the emission limit values of Article 286, shall, with its own measure, order the offender to proceed with the adaptation within a determined period beyond which the plant cannot be used. In case of non-compliance with the measure adopted by the competent authority, art. 650 of the penal code applies.
6. The competent authority referred to in Article 283, paragraph 1, letter i), or the different authority indicated by the regional law, shall impose the administrative sanctions provided for in this article, pursuant to Articles 17 and following of law no. 689 of 24 November 1981.
7. Whoever operates a civil thermal plant with a nominal thermal power greater than 0.322 MW without being in possession, where prescribed, of the license of Article 287 is punished with a fine from fifteen euros to forty-six euros.
8. The controls relating to compliance with this title are carried out by the competent authority, with a frequency of at least biennial, also using external organizations with specific technical competence, within the limits of the resources available under current legislation. By decree of the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, in concert with the Minister of Production Activities and the Minister of Health, the requirements of these organizations are identified. Until the adoption of this decree, the requirements provided for by art. 11, paragraph 19, of the decree of the President of the Republic of 26 August 1993, no. 412, shall apply.

---
**Art. 289**
**Repeals**
1. The following are repealed, excluding the provisions for which this decree provides for further validity: law no. 615 of 13 July 1966, and the decree of the President of the Republic no. 1391 of 22 December 1970.

**Art. 290**
**Transitional and final provisions**
1. The modification and integration of Annex IX to the fifth part of this decree shall be carried out with the methods provided for by Article 281, paragraph 5.
2. The installation of centralized civil thermal plants may be imposed by municipal building regulations with regard to building renovation interventions and new construction interventions if this measure is identified by the plans and programs provided for by art. 8 of legislative decree no. 351 of 4 August 1999, as necessary for the achievement of air quality limit values.
3. Law no. 615 of 13 July 1966, the decree of the President of the Republic no. 1391 of 22 December 1970, and title II of the decree of the President of the Council of Ministers of 8 March 2002 shall continue to apply to the civil thermal plants of Article 281, paragraph 3, until the date on which the adaptation ordered by the authorizations issued pursuant to Article 281, paragraph 2, is carried out.

**TITLE III - FUELS**

**Art. 291**
**Scope of application**
1. This title regulates, for the purposes of the prevention and limitation of atmospheric pollution, the product characteristics of the fuels that can be used in the plants of titles I and II of the fifth part of this decree, including civil thermal plants with a thermal power lower than the threshold value, and the product characteristics of marine gas oil. This title also establishes the conditions for the use of fuels, including the prescriptions aimed at optimizing the combustion efficiency, and the methods for measuring the product characteristics.

**Art. 292**
**Definitions**
1. For the purposes of this title, unless otherwise provided, the definitions of title I and title II of the fifth part of this decree apply.
2. In addition to the definitions of paragraph 1, the following definitions apply:
a) heavy fuel oil: any liquid fuel derived from petroleum of CN code 2710 1951 - 2710 1969 or any liquid fuel derived from petroleum, excluding gas oil as per letters b) and d), which, due to its distillation limits, falls into the category of heavy oils intended for use as fuel and of which less than sixty-five percent by volume, including losses, distils at 250 C according to the ASTM D86 method, even if the percentage of the distillate at 250 C cannot be determined according to the aforementioned method;
b) gas oil: any liquid fuel derived from petroleum of CN code 2710 1945 - 2710 1949, or any liquid fuel derived from petroleum which, due to its distillation limits, falls into the category of middle distillates intended for use as a combustible or fuel and of which at least eighty-five percent by volume, including losses, distils at 350 C according to the ASTM D86 method;
c) ASTM method: the methods established by the "American Society for Testing and Materials" in the 1976 edition of the definitions and standard specifications for petroleum and lubricating products;
d) marine gas oil: any fuel for marine use that corresponds to the definition of letter b) or that has a viscosity or density that falls within the viscosity or density limits defined for marine distillates in the table of ISO 8217-1996, with the exclusion of that used for vessels intended for internal navigation, for which the provisions of legislative decree no. 66 of 21 March 2005 apply, and with the exclusion of that used by ships that come directly from a country not belonging to the European Union;
e) internal navigation: navigation on lakes, rivers, canals, and other internal waters.
f) tax warehouses: plants where the fuels covered by the fifth part of this decree, subject to excise duty, are manufactured, processed, held, received, or dispatched; this definition also includes fuel production plants.
g) fuel subject to excise duty: fuel to which the fiscal regime of excise duties applies.

**Art. 293**
**Permitted fuels**
1. In the plants regulated by title I and title II of the fifth part of this decree, including civil thermal plants with a thermal power lower than the threshold value, only the fuels provided for these categories of plants by Annex X to the fifth part of this decree may be used, under the conditions provided therein. For the plants of part I, letters e) and f), of Annex IV to the fifth part of this decree, the prescriptions of Annex X to the fifth part of this decree relating to the plants regulated by title II of the fifth part of this decree apply. Marine gas oil must comply with what is provided for in part I, section 3, of Annex X to the fifth part of this decree.
2. By decree of the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, in concert with the Ministers of Production Activities and of Health, upon authorization of the European Commission, maximum limit values for the sulfur content in heavy fuel oils or in gas oil, including marine gas oil, may be established, higher than those set in Annex X to the fifth part of this decree if, due to a sudden change in the supply of crude oil, petroleum products, or other hydrocarbons, it is not possible to respect these limit values.

**Art. 294**
**Prescriptions for combustion efficiency**
1. In order to optimize combustion efficiency, the plants regulated by title I of the fifth part of this decree, with a nominal thermal power of 6 MW or more, must be equipped with temperature detectors in the gaseous effluent as well as an analyzer for the continuous measurement and recording of free oxygen and carbon monoxide. The aforesaid parameters must be detected in the gaseous effluent at the outlet of the plant. These plants must also be equipped, where technically feasible, with automatic regulation of the air-fuel ratio. For the purposes of applying this paragraph, reference is made to the nominal thermal power of each single plant even in cases where multiple plants are considered, pursuant to Article 270, paragraph 4, or Article 273, paragraph 9, as a single plant.
2. Paragraph 1 does not apply to combustion plants in possession of an authorization for atmospheric emissions or an integrated environmental authorization in which an emission limit value into the atmosphere for carbon monoxide is prescribed.
3. In order to optimize combustion efficiency, the plants regulated by title II of the fifth part of this decree, with a total thermal power of 1.5 MW or more, must be equipped with temperature detectors in the gaseous effluents as well as an analyzer for the continuous measurement and recording of free oxygen and carbon monoxide. The aforesaid parameters must be detected in the gaseous effluent at the outlet of the firebox.

**Art. 295**
**Collection and transmission of data relating to the sulfur content of certain liquid fuels**
1. In order to allow the preparation of the report referred to in paragraph 4, the control of the characteristics of heavy fuel oil, gas oil, and marine gas oil produced or imported, and destined for commercialization on the national market, is carried out by the customs chemical laboratories or, where established, by the customs offices in whose area the customs chemical laboratories operate. Sampling is carried out with an adequate frequency and according to methods that ensure the representativeness of the samples with respect to the controlled fuel. By March 31 of each year, the results of these checks carried out during the previous year are made available to the Agency for the Protection of the Environment and for Technical Services (APAT) and to the Ministry of the Environment and Protection of the Territory.
2. By March 31 of each year, the operators of the tax warehouses that import the fuels of paragraph 1 from third countries or receive them from member countries of the European Union and the operators of the plants for the production of the same fuels shall send to the Agency for the Protection of the Environment and for Technical Services (APAT) and to the Ministry of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, observing the methods and using the forms indicated in part I, section 3, appendix 1, of Annex X to the fifth part of this decree, the data concerning the quantities and sulfur content of such fuels produced or imported, and destined for commercialization on the national market, during the previous year. The data refer to the fuels stored in the tanks in which they are subject to assessment aimed at verifying their quantity and quality for fiscal classification purposes. By March 31 of each year, the operators of the large combustion plants that import heavy fuel oil from third countries or receive it from member countries of the European Union shall send to the Agency for the Protection of the Environment and for Technical Services (APAT) and to the Ministry of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, observing the methods and using the forms indicated in part I, section 3, appendix 1 of Annex X to the fifth part of this decree, the data concerning the quantities of heavy fuel oil imported in the previous year and the relative sulfur content.
3. By March 31 of each year, the operators of the plants of part I, section 3, point 1.2, of Annex X to the fifth part of this decree shall send to the Agency for the Protection of the Environment and for Technical Services (APAT) and to the Ministry of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, observing the methods and using the forms indicated by that section in appendix 2, the data concerning the quantities and sulfur content of the heavy fuel oil used during the previous year.
4. By May 31 of each year, the Agency for the Protection of the Environment and for Technical Services (APAT), on the basis of the results of the controls of paragraph 1 and the data of paragraphs 2 and 3, shall transmit to the Ministry of the Environment and Protection of the Territory a report on the sulfur content of the fuels of paragraph 1 produced, imported, and used in the previous civil year and on the cases of application of the derogations of part I, section 3, point 1.2, of Annex X to the fifth part of this decree.
5. By June 30 of each year, the Ministry of the Environment and Protection of the Territory shall send to the European Commission a document prepared on the basis of the report of paragraph 4.
6. Fuels destined for transformation before final combustion and fuels used for transformation purposes in the refining industry are not subject to this article.

**Art. 296**
**Sanctions**
1. Whoever carries out the combustion of materials or substances not compliant with the prescriptions of this title, where the same do not constitute waste pursuant to current legislation, is punished:
a) in the case of combustion carried out at the plants of title I of the fifth part of this decree, with arrest for up to two years or with a fine from two hundred and fifty-eight euros to one thousand and thirty-two euros;
b) in the case of combustion carried out at the plants of title II of the fifth part of this decree, including civil thermal plants with a thermal power lower than the threshold value, with an administrative pecuniary sanction from two hundred euros to one thousand euros; for this sanction, to be imposed pursuant to Article 288, paragraph 6, the payment in a reduced measure of art. 16 of law no. 689 of 24 November 1981 does not apply; the sanction does not apply if, from the documentation relating to the purchase of such materials or substances, product characteristics compliant with those of the fuels permitted in the plant result, without prejudice to the application of art. 515 of the penal code and the other crimes provided for by current legislation for those who carried out the marketing.
2. The sanction provided for in paragraph 1, letter b), also applies to those who carry out the combustion of marine gas oil not compliant with the prescriptions of this title. In this case, the competent authority for the imposition is the region or the different authority indicated by the

---
regional law.
3. The controls on compliance with the provisions of this title are carried out, for the plants of title I of the fifth part of this decree, by the authority of Article 268, paragraph 1, letter p), and for the plants of title II of the fifth part of this decree, by the authority of Article 283, paragraph 1, letter i).
4. In case of non-compliance with the prescriptions of Article 294, the operator of the plants regulated by title I of the fifth part of this decree is punished with arrest for up to one year or with a fine up to one thousand and thirty-two euros. For the plants regulated by title II of the fifth part of this decree, the sanction provided for by Article 288, paragraph 2, applies; the same sanction, in case of non-compliance with the prescriptions of Article 294, applies to the person responsible for the operation and maintenance if the case provided for in the last period of Article 284, paragraph 2, occurs.
5. In case of failure to transmit the data of Article 295, paragraphs 2 and 3, within the prescribed terms, the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, also for the purposes of what is provided for by art. 650 of the penal code, orders the non-compliant subjects to comply.

**Art. 297**
**Repeals**
1. The following are repealed, excluding the provisions for which this decree provides for further validity: art. 2, paragraph 2, of law no. 349 of 8 July 1986, the decree of the President of the Council of Ministers no. 395 of 7 September 2001, the decree of the President of the Council of Ministers of 8 March 2002, and art. 2 of decree-law no. 22 of 7 March 2002, converted, with modifications, by law no. 82 of 6 May 2002.

**Art. 298**
**Transitional and final provisions**
1. The provisions of this title relating to the plants regulated by title I of the fifth part of this decree apply to the civil thermal plants of Article 281, paragraph 3, starting from the date on which the adaptation ordered by the authorizations issued pursuant to Article 281, paragraph 2, is carried out.
2. The modification and integration of Annex X to the fifth part of this decree shall be carried out with the methods provided for by Article 281, paragraphs 5 and 6. The integration of this Annex shall be carried out for the first time within one year of the entry into force of the fifth part of this decree.

**PART SIX - RULES ON COMPENSATORY PROTECTION AGAINST DAMAGE TO THE ENVIRONMENT**

**TITLE I - SCOPE OF APPLICATION**

**Art. 299**
**Ministerial competencies**
1. The Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory shall exercise the functions and tasks pertaining to the State in the matter of protection, prevention, and repair of damage to the environment, through the General Directorate for environmental damage established at the Ministry of the Environment and Protection of the Territory by art. 34 of decree-law no. 4 of 10 January 2006, and the other competent ministerial offices.
2. The ministerial action is normally carried out in collaboration with the regions, with the local authorities, and with any public law entity deemed suitable.
3. The ministerial action is carried out in compliance with the current community legislation on the prevention and repair of environmental damage, the competencies of the regions, the autonomous provinces of Trento and Bolzano, and the local authorities with the application of the constitutional principles of subsidiarity and loyal collaboration.
4. For the purposes related to the identification, ascertainment, and quantification of environmental damage, the Ministry of the Environment and Protection of the Territory shall avail itself, in

---
a conventional regime, of public and private entities of high and proven technical-scientific qualification operating in the territory, within the limits of the existing availabilities.
5. Within sixty days from the date of entry into force of this decree, the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, with his own decree, in concert with the Ministers of Economy and Finance and of Production Activities, shall establish the criteria for the preliminary activities aimed at the ascertainment of environmental damage and for the collection of the sum due for patrimonial equivalent pursuant to title III of the sixth part of this decree. The related charges are borne by the person responsible for the damage.
6. For the purposes of implementing the provisions contained in this article, the Minister of Economy and Finance is authorized to make, with his own decrees, the necessary budget variations.

**Art. 300**
**Environmental damage**
1. Environmental damage is any significant and measurable deterioration, direct or indirect, of a natural resource or of the utility ensured by the latter.
2. Pursuant to Directive 2004/35/EC, environmental damage is the deterioration, in comparison to the original conditions, caused:
a) to the species and natural habitats protected by the national and community legislation of law no. 157 of 11 February 1992, containing rules for the protection of wild fauna, which transposes Council directives 79/409/EEC of 2 April 1979; 85/411/EEC of the Commission of 25 July 1985 and 91/244/EEC of the Commission of 6 March 1991 and implements the conventions of Paris of 18 October 1950 and of Bern of 19 September 1979, and of the decree of the President of the Republic no. 357 of 8 September 1997, containing a regulation implementing Directive 92/43/EEC on the conservation of natural and semi-natural habitats, as well as of wild flora and fauna, as well as to the protected natural areas of law no. 394 of 6 December 1991, and subsequent implementing rules;
b) to inland waters, by actions that have a significant negative impact on the ecological, chemical, and/or quantitative status or on the ecological potential of the waters concerned, as defined in Directive 2000/60/EC, with the exception of the negative effects to which art. 4, paragraph 7, of that directive applies;
c) to coastal waters and to those included in the territorial sea by the aforementioned actions, even if carried out in international waters;
d) to the land, by any contamination that creates a significant risk of harmful effects, even indirect, on human health as a result of the introduction into the soil, on the soil, or in the subsoil of substances, preparations, organisms, or harmful microorganisms for the environment.

**Art. 301**
**Implementation of the precautionary principle**
1. In application of the precautionary principle of Article 174, paragraph 2, of the EC Treaty, in case of dangers, even only potential, for human health and for the environment, a high level of protection must be ensured.
2. The application of the principle of paragraph 1 concerns the risk that can in any case be identified following a preliminary objective scientific assessment.
3. The interested operator, when the aforementioned risk emerges, must inform without delay, indicating all the relevant aspects of the situation, the municipality, the province, the region, or the autonomous province in whose territory the harmful event is foreseen, as well as the Prefect of the province who, within the following twenty-four hours, shall inform the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory.
4. The Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, in application of the precautionary principle, has the right to adopt at any time prevention measures, pursuant to Article 304, which are:
a) proportional with respect to the level of protection to be achieved;
b) non-discriminatory in their application and consistent with similar measures already adopted;
c) based on the examination of the potential advantages and burdens;
d) updatable in the light of new scientific data.
5. The Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory shall promote public information on the negative effects of a product or a process and, taking into account the

---
financial resources provided for by current legislation, may finance research programs, order the use of environmental certification systems, and take any other initiative aimed at reducing the risks of environmental damage.

**Art. 302**
**Definitions**
1. The conservation status of a species is considered favorable when:
a) data relating to its population show that it is maintaining itself, in the long term, as a viable component of its natural habitats;
b) the natural area of the species is not being reduced nor will it likely be reduced in the foreseeable future;
c) there is, and will likely continue to exist, a sufficiently large habitat to maintain its population in the long term.
2. The conservation status of a natural habitat is considered favorable when:
a) its natural area and the zones enclosed therein are stable or increasing;
b) the specific structures and functions necessary for its long-term maintenance exist and will likely continue to exist in the foreseeable future; and
c) the conservation status of its typical species is favorable, pursuant to paragraph 1.
3. For "waters" all the waters to which the third part of this decree applies are intended.
4. "Operator" means any person, natural or legal, public or private, who exercises or controls a professional activity having environmental relevance or who in any case exercises decision-making power over the technical and financial aspects of this activity, including the holder of the permit or authorization to carry out said activity.
5. "Professional activity" means any action, whether or not for profit, carried out in the course of an economic, industrial, commercial, artisanal, agricultural, and service provision activity, public or private.
6. "Emission" means the release into the environment, as a result of human activity, of substances, preparations, organisms, or microorganisms.
7. "Imminent threat" of damage means a sufficiently high probability that specific environmental damage is about to occur.
8. "Prevention measures" means the measures taken to react to an event, an act, or an omission that has created an imminent threat of environmental damage, in order to prevent or minimize this damage.
9. "Restoration," also "natural," means: in the case of waters, protected species, and habitats, the return of the natural resources or damaged services to their original conditions; in the case of damage to the land, the elimination of any risk of harmful effects on human health and environmental integrity. In any case, the restoration must consist of the redevelopment of the site and its ecosystem, through any action or combination of actions, including mitigation or provisional measures, aimed at repairing, restoring or, if deemed admissible by the competent authority, replacing damaged natural resources or natural services.
10. "Natural resources" means protected species and natural habitats, water, and land.
11. "Services" and "services of natural resources" mean the functions performed by a natural resource for the benefit of other natural resources and/or the public.
12. "Original conditions" means the conditions, at the time of the damage, of the natural resources and services that would have existed if the environmental damage had not occurred, estimated on the basis of the best available information.
13. "Costs" means the economic charges justified by the need to ensure correct and effective implementation of the provisions of the sixth part of this decree, including the costs for assessing environmental damage or an imminent threat thereof, for planning alternative interventions, for supporting administrative, legal, and works implementation expenses, the costs of data collection and other general costs, as well as the costs of control and surveillance.

**Art. 303**
**Exclusions**
1. The sixth part of this decree:
a) does not concern environmental damage or the imminent threat of such damage caused by:
1) acts of armed conflict, sabotage, acts of hostility, civil war, insurrection;

---
2) natural phenomena of an exceptional, inevitable, and uncontrollable nature;
b) does not apply to environmental damage or an imminent threat of such damage caused by an incident for which liability or compensation falls within the scope of one of the international conventions listed in Annex 1 to the sixth part of this decree to which the Italian Republic has acceded;
c) does not prejudice the right of the transgressor to limit their liability in accordance with national legislation that implements the convention on the limitation of liability for maritime claims (LLMC) of 1976, or the Strasbourg convention on the limitation of liability in inland navigation (CLNI) of 1988;
d) does not apply to nuclear risks related to the environment nor to the imminent threat of such damage caused by activities governed by the Treaty establishing the European Atomic Energy Community or caused by an incident or an activity for which liability or compensation falls within the scope of one of the international instruments listed in Annex 2 to the sixth part of this decree;
e) does not apply to activities carried out in conditions of necessity and having as their exclusive purpose national defense, international security, or protection from natural disasters;
f) does not apply to damage caused by an emission, an event, or an incident that occurred before the date of entry into force of the sixth part of this decree;
g) does not apply to damage in relation to which more than thirty years have passed since the emission, event, or incident that caused it;
h) does not apply to environmental damage or the imminent threat of such damage caused by pollution of a diffuse nature, if it has not been possible to ascertain in any way a causal link between the damage and the activity of individual operators;
i) does not apply to situations of pollution for which the procedures relating to remediation have actually been started, or remediation of the sites has been started or has occurred in compliance with the rules in force on the matter, unless environmental damage persists after such remediation.

**TITLE II - ENVIRONMENTAL PREVENTION AND RESTORATION**

**Art. 304**
**Prevention action**
1. When environmental damage has not yet occurred, but there is an imminent threat that it will, the interested operator shall, within twenty-four hours and at their own expense, adopt the necessary prevention and safety measures.
2. The operator must precede the interventions of paragraph 1 with a specific communication to the municipality, the province, the region, or the autonomous province in whose territory the harmful event is foreseen, as well as to the Prefect of the province who, within the following twenty-four hours, shall inform the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory. This communication must cover all the relevant aspects of the situation, and in particular the operator's general information, the characteristics of the interested site, the environmental matrices presumably involved, and the description of the interventions to be carried out. The communication, as soon as it is received by the municipality, immediately enables the operator to carry out the interventions of paragraph 1. If the operator does not carry out the interventions of paragraph 1 and the communication of this paragraph, the authority in charge of control or in any case the Ministry of the Environment and Protection of the Territory shall impose an administrative sanction of not less than one thousand euros nor more than three thousand euros for each day of delay.
3. The Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, at any time, has the right to:
a) ask the operator to provide information on any imminent threat of environmental damage or on suspected cases of such imminent threat;
b) order the operator to adopt the specific prevention measures considered necessary, specifying the methodologies to be followed;
c) adopt the necessary prevention measures himself.
4. If the operator does not comply with the obligations provided for in paragraph 1 or paragraph 3, letter b), or if he cannot be identified, or if he is not required to bear the costs under

---
of the sixth part of this decree, the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory has the right to adopt the necessary measures for the prevention of the damage himself, approving the note of expenses, with the right of recourse exercisable against whoever has caused or contributed to causing the expenses themselves, if identified within five years of the payment being made.

**Art. 305**
**Environmental restoration**
1. When environmental damage has occurred, the operator must communicate without delay all relevant aspects of the situation to the authorities of Article 304, with the effects provided for therein, and, if applicable, to the other competent state authorities, in any case interested. The operator also has the obligation to immediately adopt:
a) all practicable initiatives to control, contain, eliminate, or manage in another way, with immediate effect, any factor of damage, in order to prevent or limit further environmental prejudice and harmful effects on human health or further deterioration to services, also on the basis of the specific instructions formulated by the competent authorities regarding the necessary prevention measures to be adopted;
b) the necessary restoration measures of Article 306.
2. The Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, at any time, has the right to:
a) ask the operator to provide information on any damage that has occurred and on the measures he has immediately adopted pursuant to paragraph 1;
b) adopt, or order the operator to adopt, all appropriate initiatives to control, contain, eliminate, or manage in another way, with immediate effect, any factor of damage, in order to prevent or limit further environmental prejudice and harmful effects on human health or further deterioration to services;
c) order the operator to take the necessary restoration measures;
d) adopt the said measures himself.
3. If the operator does not comply with the obligations provided for in paragraph 1 or paragraph 2, letter b) or c), or if he cannot be identified or is not required to bear the costs under the sixth part of this decree, the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory has the right to adopt these measures himself, approving the note of expenses, with the right of recourse exercisable against whoever has caused or in any case contributed to causing the expenses themselves, if identified within five years of the payment being made.

**Art. 306**
**Determination of measures for environmental restoration**
1. The operators shall identify the possible measures for environmental restoration that are compliant with Annex 3 to the sixth part of this decree and present them for approval to the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory without delay and in any case no later than thirty days from the harmful event, unless he has already adopted urgent measures, pursuant to Article 305, paragraphs 2 and 3.
2. The Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory shall decide which restoration measures to implement, in order to ensure, where possible, the achievement of complete environmental restoration, and shall evaluate the opportunity to reach an agreement with the interested operator in compliance with the procedure of art. 11 of law no. 241 of 7 August 1990.
3. If a plurality of cases of environmental damage has occurred and the competent authority is not able to ensure the simultaneous adoption of the necessary restoration measures, it may decide which environmental damage should be repaired on a priority basis. For the purposes of this decision, the competent authority shall take into account, among other things, the nature, extent, and severity of the various cases of environmental damage in question, as well as the possibility of natural restoration.
4. In environmental restoration activities, risks to human health are given priority consideration.
5. The Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory invites the subjects of Articles 12 and 7, paragraph 4, of Directive 2004/35/EC, as well as the subjects on whose properties the restoration measures are to be carried out, to present their observations within ten days and takes them into consideration in the ordinance. In cases of motivated, extreme urgency, the invitation may be included in the ordinance, which in that case may undergo appropriate reforms or be revoked taking into account the state of the works in progress.

---
**Art. 307**
**Notification of preventive and restoration measures**
1. The decisions that impose measures of precaution, prevention, or restoration, adopted pursuant to the sixth part of this decree, are adequately motivated and communicated without delay to the interested operator with an indication of the means of appeal available to him and the relative terms.

**Art. 308**
**Costs of prevention and restoration activities**
1. The operator shall bear the costs of the state initiatives for prevention and environmental restoration adopted according to the provisions of the sixth part of this decree.
2. Without prejudice to paragraphs 4, 5, and 6, the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory shall recover, also through real or bank guarantees on first demand and with the exclusion of the benefit of prior enforcement, from the operator who has caused the damage or the imminent threat, the expenses incurred by the State in relation to the actions of precaution, prevention, and restoration adopted in accordance with the sixth part of this decree.
3. The Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory shall decide not to recover all the costs if the necessary expense is greater than the recoverable amount or if the operator cannot be identified.
4. The costs of the actions of precaution, prevention, and restoration adopted in accordance with the provisions of the sixth part of this decree are not borne by the operator if he can prove that the environmental damage or the imminent threat of such damage:
a) was caused by a third party and occurred despite the existence of strictly suitable safety measures;
b) is a consequence of compliance with a mandatory order or instruction issued by a public authority, other than those issued as a result of an emission or an incident attributable to the operator; in this case, the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory shall adopt the necessary measures to allow the operator to recover the costs incurred.
5. The operator is not required to bear the costs of the actions referred to in paragraph 5 undertaken in accordance with the provisions of the sixth part of this decree if he demonstrates that he is not attributable for intentional or negligent conduct and that the preventive intervention for the protection of the environment was caused by:
a) an emission or an event expressly permitted by an authorization granted pursuant to the current legislative and regulatory provisions implementing the legislative measures adopted by the European Community referred to in Annex 5 of the sixth part of this decree, applicable on the date of the emission or event and in full compliance with the conditions provided therein;
b) an emission or an activity or any other way of using a product in the course of an activity that the operator demonstrates was not considered a probable cause of environmental damage according to the state of scientific and technical knowledge at the time of the release of the emission or the execution of the activity.
6. The measures adopted by the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory in implementation of the provisions of the sixth part of this decree leave unprejudiced the liability and the compensatory obligation of the interested transgressor.

**Art. 309**
**Request for state intervention**
1. The regions, the autonomous provinces, and the local authorities, also associated, as well as the natural or legal persons who are or who could be affected by the environmental damage or who have a legitimating interest in participating in the procedure relating to the adoption of the measures of precaution, prevention, or restoration provided for by the sixth part of this decree, may present to the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, by depositing them at the Prefectures - Territorial Offices of the Government, reports and observations, accompanied by documents and information, concerning any case of environmental damage or imminent threat of environmental damage and request state intervention for the protection of the environment in accordance with the sixth part of this decree.
2. The non-governmental organizations that promote the protection of the environment, of which

---
art. 13 of law no. 349 of 8 July 1986, are recognized as holders of the interest referred to in paragraph 1.
3. The Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory shall evaluate the requests for intervention and the observations attached to them concerning cases of damage or threat of environmental damage and shall inform without delay the requesting subjects of the measures taken in this regard.
4. In case of an imminent threat of damage, the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, in extreme urgency, shall act on the reported damage even before having responded to the requesters pursuant to paragraph 3.

**Art. 310**
**Appeals**
1. The subjects referred to in Article 309, paragraph 1, are entitled to take action, according to general principles, for the annulment of the acts and measures adopted in violation of the provisions of the sixth part of this decree as well as against the failure to act of the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory and for compensation for the damage suffered due to the delay in the activation, by the same Minister, of the measures of precaution, prevention, or containment of environmental damage.
2. In the case of paragraph 1, the appeal to the administrative judge, in exclusive jurisdiction, may be preceded by an opposition filed with the Ministry of the Environment and Protection of the Territory or sent to its headquarters by registered mail with return receipt within thirty days of notification, communication, or full knowledge of the act. In case of inaction by the Minister, a similar opposition may be proposed within the aforesaid term starting from the expiry of the thirtieth day following the filing of the opposition with the Ministry of the Environment and Protection of the Territory.
3. If the opposition has been submitted and not yet the appeal to the administrative judge, the latter is admissible within sixty days from the receipt of the decision to reject the opposition or from the thirty-first day following the submission of the opposition if the Minister has not ruled.
4. The right of the interested party to appeal in an extraordinary manner to the President of the Republic within one hundred and twenty days of notification, communication, or full knowledge of the act or measure that is considered illegal and harmful remains unaffected.

**TITLE III - COMPENSATION FOR ENVIRONMENTAL DAMAGE**

**Art. 311**
**Action for compensation in specific form and for patrimonial equivalent**
1. The Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory shall act, also by exercising civil action in criminal proceedings, for compensation for environmental damage in specific form and, if necessary, for patrimonial equivalent, or shall proceed pursuant to the provisions of the sixth part of this decree.
2. Anyone who, by carrying out an illegal act, or by omitting due activities or behaviors, in violation of the law, of a regulation, or of an administrative provision, with negligence, incompetence, imprudence, or violation of technical standards, causes damage to the environment, altering, deteriorating, or destroying it in whole or in part, is obliged to restore the previous situation and, in its absence, to compensation for patrimonial equivalent towards the State.
3. The Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory shall provide for the quantification of the damage in application of the criteria set out in Annexes 3 and 4 of the sixth part of this decree. The Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory shall provide for the ascertainment of compensatory liability and for the collection of the sums due for patrimonial equivalent with the procedures of title III of the sixth part of this decree.

**Art. 312**
**Preliminary investigation for the issuance of the ministerial ordinance**
1. The preliminary investigation for the issuance of the ministerial ordinance of Article 313 shall take place pursuant to law no. 241 of 7 August 1990.

---
2. The Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, for the ascertainment of the facts, for the identification of the transgressors, for the implementation of measures to protect the environment and for the compensation for damages, may delegate the Prefect competent for the territory and avail himself, also through specific agreements, of the collaboration of the district State Attorney's Offices, the State Forestry Corps, the Carabinieri, the State Police, the Finance Guard, and any other public entity with adequate competence.
3. The Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, for the ascertainment of the causes of the damage and for its quantification, to be carried out in application of the provisions contained in Annexes 3 and 4 to the sixth part of this decree, may order, in compliance with the principle of contradiction with the interested operator, a specific technical consultancy carried out by the ministerial offices, by those of paragraph 2 or, taking into account the financial resources provided for by current legislation, by independent professionals.
4. The Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, in order to carry out documentary inspections, verifications, and searches, including in computer equipment, and any other survey deemed useful for the ascertainment of the harmful fact and for the identification of the transgressors, may order the access of his own appointees to the site affected by the harmful fact. The appointees who carry out the access must be provided with a specific authorization indicating its purpose, issued by the head of the office on which they depend. For access to premises that are used as a dwelling or for the exercise of professional activities, it is necessary for the Administration to obtain the authorization of the competent judicial authority. In any case, the holder of the activity or his delegate must be informed of the access to the places of this paragraph, who has the right to be present, also with the assistance of a trusted defender, and to ask for his statements to be recorded.
5. In case of serious indications that suggest that books, registers, documents, writings, and other evidence of the harmful fact are in premises other than those indicated in paragraph 4, the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory may request authorization for the search of these premises from the competent judicial authority.
6. The authorization of the competent judicial authority is in any case necessary to proceed, during the access, to personal searches and to the forced opening of sealed envelopes, bags, safes, furniture, closets, and the like, and for the examination of documents and the request for information regarding which professional secrecy has been invoked.
7. A report must be drawn up for each access, from which the inspections and surveys carried out, the requests made to the interested party or his representative, and the responses received, as well as his statements, must result. The report must be signed by the interested party or his representative or must indicate the reason for the failure to sign. The interested party has the right to have a copy.
8. The documents and writings may be seized only if it is not possible to reproduce them or to easily record their relevant content in the report, as well as in case of failure to sign or contestation of the content of the report; however, the agents may always acquire data with their own instruments from mechanized, telematic, electronic, and similar systems.

**Art. 313**
**Ordinance**
1. If, at the end of the preliminary investigation of Article 312, a fact has been ascertained that has caused environmental damage and the person responsible has not activated the restoration procedures pursuant to title V of the fourth part of this decree or pursuant to Articles 304 and following, the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, with an immediately enforceable ordinance, shall order those who, on the basis of the said ascertainment, have been found responsible for the fact, the environmental restoration by way of compensation in specific form within a fixed term.
2. If the person responsible for the fact that has caused environmental damage does not provide for the restoration in whole or in part within the ordered term, or the restoration is in whole or in part impossible, or excessively burdensome pursuant to Article 2058 of the civil code, the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, with a subsequent ordinance, shall order the payment, within sixty days of notification, of a sum equal to the economic value of the ascertained or residual damage, by way of compensation for pecuniary equivalent.

---
3. With regard to compensation for damage in specific form, the ordinance is issued against the person responsible for the harmful act as well as, jointly and severally, against the person in whose effective interest the conduct causing the damage was held or who objectively benefited from it, avoiding, according to the completed investigation, the economic burden necessary to prepare, in a preventive manner, the works, equipment, precautions, and to maintain the behaviors provided for as mandatory by the applicable rules.
4. The ordinance is adopted within the peremptory term of one hundred and eighty days starting from the communication to the subjects of paragraph 3 of the start of the investigation, and in any case within the term of forfeiture of two years from the notice of the fact, unless the environmental restoration is in progress by the care and expense of the transgressor. In this case, the same terms start from the unjustified suspension of the restoration works or from their conclusion in case of incomplete repair of the damage. The Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory shall provide for the attestations concerning the suspension of the works and their incompleteness with a specific act of ascertainment.
5. Within the terms provided for by paragraphs 1 and 3 of art. 2947 of the civil code, the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory may adopt further measures against subsequently identified transgressors.
6. In the case of damage caused by subjects subject to the jurisdiction of the Court of Auditors, the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, instead of ordering the payment of the compensation for patrimonial equivalent, shall send a report to the Regional Prosecutor's Office at the jurisdictional Section of the Court of Auditors competent for the territory.
7. In the case of occurred compensation for the damage, new interventions involving an increase in costs for the interested operator are excluded, following a concurrent action by an authority other than the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory. The right of the subjects damaged by the fact that produced environmental damage, in their health or in their property, to take legal action against the person responsible for the protection of their rights and interests remains unaffected.

**Art. 314**
**Content of the ordinance**
1. The ordinance contains the specific indication of the fact, commissive or omissive, contested, as well as the elements of fact considered relevant for the identification and quantification of the damage and the sources of evidence for the identification of the transgressors.
2. The ordinance shall fix a term, also agreed upon with the transgressor in application of art. 11 of law no. 241 of 7 August 1990, for the restoration of the state of the places at his expense, in any case not less than two months and not more than two years, unless a further extension is to be defined in consideration of the extent of the necessary works.
3. The quantification of the damage must include the prejudice caused to the environmental situation with particular reference to the cost necessary for its restoration. Where the exact quantification of the damage not compensable in specific form, or part of it, is not motivably possible, the damage for patrimonial equivalent is presumed, until proven otherwise, to amount to not less than three times the sum corresponding to the administrative pecuniary sanction, or to the criminal sanction, in concrete applied. If a custodial sentence has been served, for the purpose of quantifying the damage of this article, the conversion between it and the sum to be charged as compensation for the damage takes place by calculating four hundred euros for each day of custodial sentence.
4. In case of a conviction sentence in criminal proceedings or the issuance of the measure of Article 444 of the Code of Criminal Procedure, the chancellery of the judge who issued the sentence or the measure shall transmit a copy of the same to the Ministry of the Environment and Protection of the Territory within five days of their publication.
5. The regions, the autonomous provinces, and the other territorial entities, for the purpose of compensation for environmental damage, shall communicate to the Ministry of the Environment and Protection of the Territory the administrative sanctions, within ten days of their imposition.
6. The ministerial ordinances of Articles 304, paragraph 3, and 313 indicate the means of appeal and the relative terms.

**Art. 315**

---
**Effects of the ordinance on judicial action**
1. The Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory who has adopted the ordinance of Article 313 may neither propose nor proceed further in the judgment for compensation for environmental damage, without prejudice to the possibility of intervention as an aggrieved person in the criminal judgment.

**Art. 316**
**Appeal against the ordinance**
1. The transgressor, within the peremptory term of sixty days from the communication of the ordinance of Article 313, may appeal to the regional administrative Tribunal, in exclusive jurisdiction, competent in relation to the place where the environmental damage occurred.
2. The transgressor may precede the jurisdictional action with the opposition appeal of Article 310, paragraphs 2 and 3.
3. The transgressor may also appeal to the President of the Republic within one hundred and twenty days of the receipt of the notification or communication of the ordinance or of its full knowledge.

**Art. 317**
**Collection of credits and revolving fund**
1. For the collection of the sums constituting credit of the State pursuant to the provisions of the sixth part of this decree, in the amount determined by the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory or by the judge, the norms of legislative decree no. 112 of 13 April 1999 apply.
2. In the ordinance or in the sentence, it may be ordered, upon request of the interested party who is in difficult economic conditions, that the amounts due be paid in monthly installments not exceeding the number of twenty; each installment cannot in any case be less than five thousand euros.
3. At any time, the debt can be extinguished by a single payment.
4. The failure to pay even a single installment on its due date entails the obligation to pay the remaining amount in a single solution.
5. The sums deriving from the collection of credits in favor of the State for the compensation of environmental damage regulated by the sixth part of this decree, including those deriving from the enforcement of guarantees in favor of the State, assumed as a guarantee of the same compensation, are paid into the State budget, to be reallocated within sixty days, by decree of the Minister of Economy and Finance, to a revolving fund established within a specific basic forecast unit of the budget forecast of the Ministry of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, in order to finance, also by way of advance and, in the latter case, to the maximum extent of ten percent of the expenditure:
a) urgent interventions for the perimeter definition, characterization, and securing of polluted sites, with priority for the areas for which compensation for environmental damage has taken place;
b) decontamination, remediation, and environmental restoration interventions of the areas for which compensation for environmental damage has taken place;
c) remediation and environmental restoration interventions provided for in the national program for the remediation and environmental restoration of polluted sites;
d) activities of the research centers in the field of reductions of greenhouse gas emissions and global climate change.
6. By decree of the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory, adopted in concert with the Minister of Economy and Finance, the operating and access methods to the aforesaid revolving fund are regulated, including the procedures for the recovery of the sums granted by way of advance.

**Art. 318**
**Transitional and final rules**
1. Pending the adoption of the decree of Article 317, paragraph 6, the decree of the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory of 14 October 2003 shall continue to apply.
2. The following are repealed:
a) art. 18 of law no. 349 of 8 July 1986, with the exception of paragraph 5;

---
b) art. 9, paragraph 3, of legislative decree no. 267 of 18 August 2000;
c) art. 1, paragraphs 439, 440, 441, 442, and 443 of law no. 266 of 23 December 2005.
3. In implementation of art. 14 of Directive 2004/35/EC, with a decree of the President of the Council of Ministers, adopted on the proposal of the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory in concert with the Ministers of Economy and Finance and of Production Activities, measures are adopted for the definition of suitable forms of guarantee and for the development of the offer of the relative instruments, in order to allow their use by the interested operators for the purposes of fulfilling the responsibilities incumbent on them pursuant to the sixth part of this decree.
4. When environmental damage concerns or may concern a plurality of Member States of the European Union, the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory cooperates, including through an appropriate exchange of information, to ensure that a prevention action is taken and, if necessary, a repair of this environmental damage. In this case, when the environmental damage originated in Italian territory, the Minister of the Environment and Protection of the Territory provides sufficient information to the Member States potentially exposed to its effects. If the Minister identifies within the national territory damage whose cause has occurred outside these borders, he shall inform the European Commission and any other interested Member State; the Minister may recommend the adoption of prevention or repair measures and may seek, pursuant to the sixth part of this decree, to recover the costs incurred in relation to the adoption of prevention or repair measures.

This decree, bearing the State seal, will be included in the Official Collection of normative acts of the Italian Republic. It is mandatory for anyone concerned to observe it and have it observed
